Explicit Words for Hibah: Wahaba, Nahala, A'ta
Lists explicit words for hibah with a hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three explicit words that validly conclude a hibah and cite the hadith evidence for nahala.

Core Idea
Three words are explicit for hibah: wahaba, nahala, a'ta; the second is proven by the Prophet's usage.

The passage begins by listing the words that explicitly indicate a gift: wahaba (I gave), nahala (I bestowed), and a'ta (I granted). The first is the most direct; the second is supported by a hadith; the third is used in the same sense. We will examine these and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three explicit words
Read the first sentence: 'Hibah is concluded by his saying: wahaba, nahala, a'ta.' These are the three words the passage discusses as explicit.
Explicit here means they directly indicate the transfer of ownership without needing additional intention.
2
Understand why each word is valid
Wahaba is the most explicit; nahala is used in the hadith; a'ta is synonymous as seen in Arabic usage. The passage states that 'a'ta' and 'wahaba' are used interchangeably in supplications like 'Allah gave you'.
The proof for nahala is a hadith from Nu'man bin Bashir.
3
Recognize the hadith proof for nahala
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'Did you bestow (nahala) upon each of your children like this?' when a father said he had bestowed a slave. This shows that nahala is legally recognized for hibah.
The hadith is from Sahih Bukhari; the chain is sound.

کن الفاظ سے ہبہ درست ہوتا ہے قَالَ وَيَنْعَقِدُ الْهِبَةُ بِقَوْلِهِ وَهَبْتُ وَنَحَلْتُ وَأَعْطَيْتُ لِاَنَّ الْأَوَّلَ صَرِيحٌ فِيهِ وَالثَّانِي مُسْتَعْمَلْ فِيهِ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَكُلَّ أَوْلَادَكَ نَحَلْتَ مِثْلَ هَذَا وَكَذَا الثَّالِثُ يُقَالُ أعْطَاكَ الله وَوَهَبَكَ اللَّهُ بِمَعْنَى وَاحِدٌ وَكَذَا يَنْعَقِدُ بقَوْلِهِ أَطْعَمْتُكَ هذَا الطَّعَامَ وَجَعَلْتُ هَذَا التَوْبَ لَكَ وَاعْمَرْتُكَ هذَا الشَّي وَحَمَلْتُكَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الدَّابَّةِ إِذَا نَوَى بِالْحَمْلِ الْهِبَةُ اَمَّا الْاَوَّلُ فلان الْإِطْعَامَ إِذَا أُضِيفَ إِلَى مَا يُطْعَمُ عَيْنُهُ يُرَادُ بِهِ تَمْلِيكُ الْعَيْنِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ أَطْعَمْتُكَ هَذِهِ الْأَرْضَ حَيْثُ يَكُونَ عَارِيَةً لَاتَ عَيْنَهَا لَا يُطْعَمُ فَيَكُونُ الْمُرَادُ أَكُلَ غَلَّتِهَا وأَمَّا الثَّانِي فلان حَرْفَ اللَّامِ لِلتَّمْلِيْكِ وَأَمَّا الثَّالِثُ فَلِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَمَنْ أَعْمَرَ عُمْرَىٰ فَهِيَ لِلْمُعْمَرٍ لَهُ وَلِوَرَثَتِهِ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ وَكَذَا اذَا قَالَ جَعَلَتُ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ لَكَ عُمْرَىٰ لِمَا قُلْنَا وَأَمَّا الرَّابِعُ فَلان الْحَمْلَ هُوَ الْأَرْكَابُ حَقِيقَةٌ فَيَكُونُ عَارِيَةً لَكِنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ الْهِبَةُ يُقَالُ حَمَلَ الْأَمِيرِ فَلَانَا عَلَى فَرَسٍ وَيُرَادُ بِهِ التَّمْلِيكُ فَيُحْمَل عَلَيْهِ عِنْدَ بَيْتِهِ ترجمہ اور منعقد ہو جاتا ہے ہبہ یہ کہنے سے کہ میں نے مہبہ کر دیا دے دیا عطا کیا کیونکہ پہلا لفظ تو اس میں صریح ہے اور دوسرا مستعمل ہے۔ حضور علیہ السلام نے ارشاد فرمایا۔ کیا تو نے اپنی ہر اولاد کو اس کے مثل دیا ہے اور ایسے ہی تیسر الفظ ہے۔ چنانچہ کہا جاتا ہے اعطاك الله اور وهبك اللہ ایک ہی معنی میں اور ایسے ہی منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ یہ کہنے سے کہ کھلایا میں نے تجھے یہ کھانا یہ کپڑا میں نے تیرا ہی کرونا اليه besturdubai was كتاب الهبة . " وهم دے دی۔ اس سواری پر تجھے سوار کر دیا۔ جب کہ نیت کی ہو سوار کرنے سے ہبہ کی ۔ بہر حال اول سو اس لئے کہ جب اطعام کی اضافت اس چیز کی طرف کی جائے جو بعینہ کھائی جاتی ہے تو اس سے تملیک عین مراد ہوتی ہے بخلاف اس کے جب کہا کہ میں نے تجھے یہ زمین کھلا دی کہ یہ عاریت ہو گی ۔ کیونکہ زمین کھائی جاتی تو اس کی پیداوار کھانا مراد ہو گا ۔ رہا دوسر الفظ سو اس لئے کہ حرف لام برائے تملیک ہے۔ اور تیسر الفظ حضور علیہ السلام کے ارشاد کی وجہ سے کہ جس نے عمری دیا تو وہ معمولہ کے لئے ہے اور اس کے بعد اس کے ورثہ کے لئے ہے ایسے ہی جب یہ کہا میں نے یہ گھر تیرے لئے عمری کر دیا۔ بہر حال چوتھا لفظ سو اس لئے کہ حمل سوار کرنا ہے۔ لغتہ تو یہ عاریت ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ ہبہ کو بھی محتمل ہے۔ کہا جاتا ہے کہ امیر نے فلاں کو گھوڑے پر اٹھایا اور اس سے تملیک مراد ہوتی ہے تو نیت کے وقت اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح قوله وينعقد الهبته ... الخ جن الفاظ سے ہبہ منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ وہ یہ ہیں ۔ وہست، نحلت، اعطیت ان میں پہلا لفظ یعنی وہت تو ہبہ کے معنی میں صریح ہے۔ اور دوسرا لفظ یعنی محلت اسی معنی میں مجاز استعمل ہے۔ چناچہ ارشاد نبوی میں ہے۔ اكل اولادك نحلت “۔ قوله اكل اولادك .... الخ اس حدیث کی تخر یکم ستہ نے حضرت نعمان بن بشیر سے الفاظ مختلفہ کی ہے۔ صحیح بخاری کے الفاظ یہ ہیں عن النعمان بن بشیر ان اباه اتي به رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم فقَالَ : اني نحلت ابنى هذا غلاماً فقَالَ : اكل ولدك نحلت مثله ؟ قَالَ : لا قَالَ : فارجعه“ حضرت نعمان بن بشیر سے روایت ہے کہ ان کے والد انہیں لے کر حضور پیر کی خدمت حاضر ہوئے اور عرض کیا۔ میں نے اپنے اس بیٹے کو غلام دے دیا ہے۔ آپ نے فرمایا کیا تم نے اپنے ہر بیٹے کو ایسا ہی دیا ہے؟ انہوں نے عرض کیا نہیں تو آپ نے فرمایا۔ اسے واپس لے لو۔ قوله فلان الاطعام اذا اضيف ..... الخ لفظ اطعمتك هذا الطعام سے انعقاد ہبہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اطعام کی نسبت جب ایسی چیز کی طرف ہو جو خود کھائی جاتی ہے۔ جیسے اناج گہیوں خرما روٹی وغیرہ تو اس سے عین شئی کی تملیک مراد ہوتی ہے۔ پس مطلب یہ ڈا کہ میں نے تجھے اس چیز کا مالک کر دیا اور اسی کو ہبہ کہتے ہیں اس کے خلاف اگر ایسی چیز کی طرف نسبت موجود ہو جو خود نہیں کھائی جاتی۔ جیسے زمین تو اس صورت میں اطعام کے معنی عاریت کے ہوں گے۔ اور مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ میں نے تجھے یہ زمین اس لئے دی کہ تو اس کو کاشت کر کے غلہ حاصل کرے اور وہ تیرے کام آئے۔ اس پر شیخ انزاری نے غایتہ البیان میں یہ اعتراض کیا ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ کی یہ تقریر محل نظر ہے۔ اس واسطے کہ اس تقریر کے بموجب آيت كارة اطعام عشرة مساکین میں اطعام سے مراد تملیک ہو گی۔ نہ کہ اباحت جیسا کہ دوسروں کا قول ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اطعام سے مراد اطعام طعام ہے۔ اور اطعام خودکھانا ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ اضافت الى ما يطعم عینہ سے صاحب ہدایہ کی مراد یہ ہے کہ ایسی چیز ذکر کرے جو بعینہ کھائی جاتی ہے اور اس کو اطعام کا مفعول ثانی بنائے جیسا کہ فقہاء نے اس کا یہی ضابطہ بیان کیا ہے کہ جب مفعول ثانی مذکور ہو تو تملیک کے لئے ہوگا۔ ورنہ اباحت کے لئے ہوگا۔ اور آیت میں ایسا نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس میں لفظ اطعام اپنی اصل وضع پر باقی رہا یعنی اباحت پر۔ قوله و اما الثالث... الخ تیسرے لفظ یعنی اعمر تک ھذا الشئی کہنے سے بھی ہیہ منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ حدیث فمن عمر عمری فهي للمعمولہ میں جب یہ عمری معمولہ کے واسطے قرار دیا تو مثل لفظ دوم کے معنی ہو گئے کہ اس کی ملک کر دی اور یہی ہبہ ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر اس نے يه كها جعلت هذا الدار لك عمری تب بھی بدلیل مذکورہ بالا مہیہ ہو گا ۔ قوله فمن اعمر ... اس حدیث کی تخریج امام بخاری کے علاوہ ائمہ خمسہ نے حضرت جابر سے کی ہے۔
From which words is hibah concluded? He said: Hibah is concluded by his saying: 'I gave (wahaba)', 'I bestowed (nahala)', 'I gave ('a'ta')' – because the first is explicit in it, the second is used in it. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Did you bestow (nahala) upon each of your children like this?' Similarly the third: it is said 'Allah gave you ('a'taka)' and 'Allah gifted you (wahabaka)' with the same meaning. Similarly, it is concluded by his saying: 'I fed you this food', 'I made this garment for you', 'I gave you this thing as a life grant ('umra)', 'I mounted you on this animal' if he intended hibah by 'mounting'. As for the first, because when 'feeding' is added to something that is itself eaten, what is intended is ownership of the substance; contrary to when he says 'I fed you this land' where it is a loan, because its substance is not eaten, so the intention is to eat its produce. As for the second, because the letter lam is for ownership. As for the third, because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever gives a life grant ('umra), it belongs to the one to whom it is given and to his heirs after him.' Similarly if he says 'I made this house for you as a life grant' for the reason we mentioned. As for the fourth, because 'mounting' is literally riding, so it is a loan, but it may also mean hibah. It is said 'The amir mounted so-and-so on a horse' and what is intended is ownership, so it is interpreted accordingly when he intends it. Translation: And hibah is concluded by saying 'I gave', 'I bestowed', 'I granted' – because the first is explicit in it, the second is used. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Did you bestow upon each of your children like this?' Similarly the third word; thus it is said 'Allah gave you' and 'Allah gifted you' with the same meaning. And similarly it is concluded by saying: 'I fed you this food', 'I made this cloth yours', 'I gave you this thing as a life grant', 'I mounted you on this animal' when he intends hibah by mounting. Anyway, the first is because when 'feeding' is added to something that is itself eaten, ownership of the substance is intended; contrary to when he says 'I fed you this land', because that is a loan, as land is not eaten, so the intention is to eat its produce. As for the second word, because the letter lam is for ownership. As for the third word, because of the Prophet's saying: 'Whoever gives a life grant, it belongs to the one granted and to his heirs after him.' Similarly if he says 'I made this house for you as a life grant' for the reason we mentioned. As for the fourth word, because 'mounting' is literally riding, so it is a loan, but it may also be hibah. It is said 'The amir mounted so-and-so on a horse' and ownership is intended, so it is interpreted accordingly when intended. Explanation of his saying 'and hibah is concluded...': The words by which hibah is concluded are: wahaba, nahala, a'ta. Among them, the first word 'wahaba' is explicit in the meaning of hibah. The second word 'nahala' is used metaphorically in the same meaning. Thus the prophetic instruction: 'Did you bestow upon each of your children...' His saying 'Did you bestow upon each of your children...' This hadith is narrated by the six [authorities] from Nu'man bin Bashir with various wordings. The wording in Sahih Bukhari is: 'From Nu'man bin Bashir that his father brought him to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: I have bestowed (nahaltu) upon this son of mine a slave. He said: Did you bestow upon each of your children like this? He said: No. He said: Then take it back.' His saying 'because feeding when added...' The reason for the conclusion of hibah by the phrase 'I fed you this food' is that when feeding is attributed to something that is itself eaten, like grain, wheat, dates, bread etc., then it means ownership of the substance. So the meaning is: I have made you the owner of this thing, and that is called hibah. Contrary if it is attributed to something that is not itself eaten, like land, then in that case 'feeding' means loan, and the meaning would be: I gave you this land so that you cultivate it and get grain and benefit from it. On this, Shaykh Ansari in Ghayat al-Bayan objected that this explanation by the author of al-Hidayah is open to consideration, because according to this explanation, in the verse 'feeding ten poor persons' (Quran 5:89), 'feeding' would mean ownership, not permissibility (ibaha) as others say, because 'feeding' here is added to 'food' which is eaten. The answer is that by 'added to what is itself eaten' the author of al-Hidayah means that he mentions a thing that is itself eaten and makes it the second object of 'feeding', as the jurists have stated: when the second object is mentioned, it indicates ownership; otherwise it indicates permissibility. In the verse, it is not like that, so the word 'feeding' remains on its original meaning, i.e., permissibility. His saying 'as for the third...' By the third word, i.e., saying 'I granted you this thing as a life grant ('umra)', hibah is also concluded, because the hadith 'Whoever gives a life grant, it is for the one granted' makes it like the second word in meaning: he transferred ownership, and that is hibah. Similarly if he says 'I made this house for you as a life grant', it is also hibah by the aforementioned evidence. His saying 'Whoever gives a life grant...' This hadith is narrated by Imam Bukhari and the other five from Jabir.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the valid wording for a hibah contract. It begins by listing three explicit words: wahaba (gave), nahala (bestowed), and a'ta (granted). The first is explicit; the second is supported by a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) used nahala in the context of a gift; the third is used in the same sense in Arabic. The passage then lists other words that can constitute hibah with intention: (1) 'at'amtu' (I fed you) – when applied to something edible, it means ownership, but for land it means a loan; (2) 'ja'altu' (I made) – because the letter lam indicates ownership; (3) 'a'martu' (I gave as a life grant) – based on the hadith that 'umra belongs to the donee and his heirs; (4) 'hamaltu' (I mounted) – literally a loan, but when intended as hibah, it is accepted. The commentary also addresses a critique by Shaykh Ansari regarding the interpretation of 'at'amtu' in the context of Quranic verse, explaining that the difference lies in whether the second object is mentioned. The passage is from the chapter on hibah in al-Hidayah, and the commentary (Ashraf al-Hidayah) expands on it.

Key Terms
وهبت (wahaba): I gave; the most explicit word for a gift contract.
نحلت (nahaltu): I bestowed; a word proven valid by hadith.
أعطيت (a'taytu): I gave; synonymous with wahaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following words is explicitly listed as valid for concluding a hibah?
A) Wahaba
B) Nahala
C) A'ta
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Three explicit words—wahaba, nahala, and a'ta—validly conclude a hibah, with nahala supported by the Prophet's hadith and a'ta by linguistic usage.

Implicit Words for Hibah and the Madhhab Dispute on 'At'amtu'
Lists implicit words for hibah requiring intention, with reasoning and a madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that implicit words can conclude hibah with intention, explain the distinction between 'at'amtu' for edible vs. non-edible objects, and analyze the madhhab dispute regarding its interpretation.

Core Idea
Implicit words like 'I fed you' can gift food but not land – unless the second object is specified.

The passage continues with words that are not explicit but can constitute hibah when the donor intends it. These include 'at'amtu' (I fed), 'ja'altu' (I made), 'a'martu' (I gave as life grant), and 'hamaltu' (I mounted). Each has its own reasoning and a madhhab dispute arises around 'at'amtu'. We will explore these and the dispute's resolution.

Guided Path
1
List the four implicit words
Read the passage: 'at'amtu' (I fed you this food), 'ja'altu' (I made this garment for you), 'a'martu' (I gave you this thing as a life grant), 'hamaltu' (I mounted you on this animal).
These are not explicit like the first three, but they can constitute hibah when the donor intends a gift.
2
Understand the rule for 'at'amtu'
When 'at'amtu' is added to something that is itself eaten (like food), it indicates ownership (tamlik) and is a valid hibah. When added to something not eaten (like land), it indicates a loan (ariyah), because the object is not fit for consumption; the intention is to eat its produce.
The key is whether the second object (the thing fed) is explicitly mentioned as an edible substance.
3
Analyze the madhhab dispute
Shaykh Ansari (in Ghayat al-Bayan) objects that the Hanafi rule would imply that 'at'amtu' in the Quranic verse (feeding ten poor) means ownership, but the correct interpretation is permissibility. The Hanafi response is that the rule requires the second object to be explicitly mentioned; in the verse, 'food' is not an explicit second object (it is implicit), so the word remains on its original meaning of permissibility.
This dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the fiqh tradition.
4
Apply the remaining words
'Ja'altu' works because the letter 'lam' indicates ownership. 'A'martu' is based on the hadith that a life grant belongs to the donee and his heirs. 'Hamaltu' is literally 'mounting' (a loan), but when intended as hibah, it is accepted due to common usage where 'mounting' can mean gifting the animal.
For 'hamaltu', intention is explicitly required; without intention, it remains a loan.

کن الفاظ سے ہبہ درست ہوتا ہے قَالَ وَيَنْعَقِدُ الْهِبَةُ بِقَوْلِهِ وَهَبْتُ وَنَحَلْتُ وَأَعْطَيْتُ لِاَنَّ الْأَوَّلَ صَرِيحٌ فِيهِ وَالثَّانِي مُسْتَعْمَلْ فِيهِ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَكُلَّ أَوْلَادَكَ نَحَلْتَ مِثْلَ هَذَا وَكَذَا الثَّالِثُ يُقَالُ أعْطَاكَ الله وَوَهَبَكَ اللَّهُ بِمَعْنَى وَاحِدٌ وَكَذَا يَنْعَقِدُ بقَوْلِهِ أَطْعَمْتُكَ هذَا الطَّعَامَ وَجَعَلْتُ هَذَا التَوْبَ لَكَ وَاعْمَرْتُكَ هذَا الشَّي وَحَمَلْتُكَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الدَّابَّةِ إِذَا نَوَى بِالْحَمْلِ الْهِبَةُ اَمَّا الْاَوَّلُ فلان الْإِطْعَامَ إِذَا أُضِيفَ إِلَى مَا يُطْعَمُ عَيْنُهُ يُرَادُ بِهِ تَمْلِيكُ الْعَيْنِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ أَطْعَمْتُكَ هَذِهِ الْأَرْضَ حَيْثُ يَكُونَ عَارِيَةً لَاتَ عَيْنَهَا لَا يُطْعَمُ فَيَكُونُ الْمُرَادُ أَكُلَ غَلَّتِهَا وأَمَّا الثَّانِي فلان حَرْفَ اللَّامِ لِلتَّمْلِيْكِ وَأَمَّا الثَّالِثُ فَلِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَمَنْ أَعْمَرَ عُمْرَىٰ فَهِيَ لِلْمُعْمَرٍ لَهُ وَلِوَرَثَتِهِ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ وَكَذَا اذَا قَالَ جَعَلَتُ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ لَكَ عُمْرَىٰ لِمَا قُلْنَا وَأَمَّا الرَّابِعُ فَلان الْحَمْلَ هُوَ الْأَرْكَابُ حَقِيقَةٌ فَيَكُونُ عَارِيَةً لَكِنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ الْهِبَةُ يُقَالُ حَمَلَ الْأَمِيرِ فَلَانَا عَلَى فَرَسٍ وَيُرَادُ بِهِ التَّمْلِيكُ فَيُحْمَل عَلَيْهِ عِنْدَ بَيْتِهِ ترجمہ اور منعقد ہو جاتا ہے ہبہ یہ کہنے سے کہ میں نے مہبہ کر دیا دے دیا عطا کیا کیونکہ پہلا لفظ تو اس میں صریح ہے اور دوسرا مستعمل ہے۔ حضور علیہ السلام نے ارشاد فرمایا۔ کیا تو نے اپنی ہر اولاد کو اس کے مثل دیا ہے اور ایسے ہی تیسر الفظ ہے۔ چنانچہ کہا جاتا ہے اعطاك الله اور وهبك اللہ ایک ہی معنی میں اور ایسے ہی منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ یہ کہنے سے کہ کھلایا میں نے تجھے یہ کھانا یہ کپڑا میں نے تیرا ہی کرونا اليه besturdubai was كتاب الهبة . " وهم دے دی۔ اس سواری پر تجھے سوار کر دیا۔ جب کہ نیت کی ہو سوار کرنے سے ہبہ کی ۔ بہر حال اول سو اس لئے کہ جب اطعام کی اضافت اس چیز کی طرف کی جائے جو بعینہ کھائی جاتی ہے تو اس سے تملیک عین مراد ہوتی ہے بخلاف اس کے جب کہا کہ میں نے تجھے یہ زمین کھلا دی کہ یہ عاریت ہو گی ۔ کیونکہ زمین کھائی جاتی تو اس کی پیداوار کھانا مراد ہو گا ۔ رہا دوسر الفظ سو اس لئے کہ حرف لام برائے تملیک ہے۔ اور تیسر الفظ حضور علیہ السلام کے ارشاد کی وجہ سے کہ جس نے عمری دیا تو وہ معمولہ کے لئے ہے اور اس کے بعد اس کے ورثہ کے لئے ہے ایسے ہی جب یہ کہا میں نے یہ گھر تیرے لئے عمری کر دیا۔ بہر حال چوتھا لفظ سو اس لئے کہ حمل سوار کرنا ہے۔ لغتہ تو یہ عاریت ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ ہبہ کو بھی محتمل ہے۔ کہا جاتا ہے کہ امیر نے فلاں کو گھوڑے پر اٹھایا اور اس سے تملیک مراد ہوتی ہے تو نیت کے وقت اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح قوله وينعقد الهبته ... الخ جن الفاظ سے ہبہ منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ وہ یہ ہیں ۔ وہست، نحلت، اعطیت ان میں پہلا لفظ یعنی وہت تو ہبہ کے معنی میں صریح ہے۔ اور دوسرا لفظ یعنی محلت اسی معنی میں مجاز استعمل ہے۔ چناچہ ارشاد نبوی میں ہے۔ اكل اولادك نحلت “۔ قوله اكل اولادك .... الخ اس حدیث کی تخر یکم ستہ نے حضرت نعمان بن بشیر سے الفاظ مختلفہ کی ہے۔ صحیح بخاری کے الفاظ یہ ہیں عن النعمان بن بشیر ان اباه اتي به رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم فقَالَ : اني نحلت ابنى هذا غلاماً فقَالَ : اكل ولدك نحلت مثله ؟ قَالَ : لا قَالَ : فارجعه“ حضرت نعمان بن بشیر سے روایت ہے کہ ان کے والد انہیں لے کر حضور پیر کی خدمت حاضر ہوئے اور عرض کیا۔ میں نے اپنے اس بیٹے کو غلام دے دیا ہے۔ آپ نے فرمایا کیا تم نے اپنے ہر بیٹے کو ایسا ہی دیا ہے؟ انہوں نے عرض کیا نہیں تو آپ نے فرمایا۔ اسے واپس لے لو۔ قوله فلان الاطعام اذا اضيف ..... الخ لفظ اطعمتك هذا الطعام سے انعقاد ہبہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اطعام کی نسبت جب ایسی چیز کی طرف ہو جو خود کھائی جاتی ہے۔ جیسے اناج گہیوں خرما روٹی وغیرہ تو اس سے عین شئی کی تملیک مراد ہوتی ہے۔ پس مطلب یہ ڈا کہ میں نے تجھے اس چیز کا مالک کر دیا اور اسی کو ہبہ کہتے ہیں اس کے خلاف اگر ایسی چیز کی طرف نسبت موجود ہو جو خود نہیں کھائی جاتی۔ جیسے زمین تو اس صورت میں اطعام کے معنی عاریت کے ہوں گے۔ اور مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ میں نے تجھے یہ زمین اس لئے دی کہ تو اس کو کاشت کر کے غلہ حاصل کرے اور وہ تیرے کام آئے۔ اس پر شیخ انزاری نے غایتہ البیان میں یہ اعتراض کیا ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ کی یہ تقریر محل نظر ہے۔ اس واسطے کہ اس تقریر کے بموجب آيت كارة اطعام عشرة مساکین میں اطعام سے مراد تملیک ہو گی۔ نہ کہ اباحت جیسا کہ دوسروں کا قول ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اطعام سے مراد اطعام طعام ہے۔ اور اطعام خودکھانا ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ اضافت الى ما يطعم عینہ سے صاحب ہدایہ کی مراد یہ ہے کہ ایسی چیز ذکر کرے جو بعینہ کھائی جاتی ہے اور اس کو اطعام کا مفعول ثانی بنائے جیسا کہ فقہاء نے اس کا یہی ضابطہ بیان کیا ہے کہ جب مفعول ثانی مذکور ہو تو تملیک کے لئے ہوگا۔ ورنہ اباحت کے لئے ہوگا۔ اور آیت میں ایسا نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس میں لفظ اطعام اپنی اصل وضع پر باقی رہا یعنی اباحت پر۔ قوله و اما الثالث... الخ تیسرے لفظ یعنی اعمر تک ھذا الشئی کہنے سے بھی ہیہ منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ حدیث فمن عمر عمری فهي للمعمولہ میں جب یہ عمری معمولہ کے واسطے قرار دیا تو مثل لفظ دوم کے معنی ہو گئے کہ اس کی ملک کر دی اور یہی ہبہ ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر اس نے يه كها جعلت هذا الدار لك عمری تب بھی بدلیل مذکورہ بالا مہیہ ہو گا ۔ قوله فمن اعمر ... اس حدیث کی تخریج امام بخاری کے علاوہ ائمہ خمسہ نے حضرت جابر سے کی ہے۔
From which words is hibah concluded? He said: Hibah is concluded by his saying: 'I gave (wahaba)', 'I bestowed (nahala)', 'I gave ('a'ta')' – because the first is explicit in it, the second is used in it. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Did you bestow (nahala) upon each of your children like this?' Similarly the third: it is said 'Allah gave you ('a'taka)' and 'Allah gifted you (wahabaka)' with the same meaning. Similarly, it is concluded by his saying: 'I fed you this food', 'I made this garment for you', 'I gave you this thing as a life grant ('umra)', 'I mounted you on this animal' if he intended hibah by 'mounting'. As for the first, because when 'feeding' is added to something that is itself eaten, what is intended is ownership of the substance; contrary to when he says 'I fed you this land' where it is a loan, because its substance is not eaten, so the intention is to eat its produce. As for the second, because the letter lam is for ownership. As for the third, because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever gives a life grant ('umra), it belongs to the one to whom it is given and to his heirs after him.' Similarly if he says 'I made this house for you as a life grant' for the reason we mentioned. As for the fourth, because 'mounting' is literally riding, so it is a loan, but it may also mean hibah. It is said 'The amir mounted so-and-so on a horse' and what is intended is ownership, so it is interpreted accordingly when he intends it. Translation: And hibah is concluded by saying 'I gave', 'I bestowed', 'I granted' – because the first is explicit in it, the second is used. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Did you bestow upon each of your children like this?' Similarly the third word; thus it is said 'Allah gave you' and 'Allah gifted you' with the same meaning. And similarly it is concluded by saying: 'I fed you this food', 'I made this cloth yours', 'I gave you this thing as a life grant', 'I mounted you on this animal' when he intends hibah by mounting. Anyway, the first is because when 'feeding' is added to something that is itself eaten, ownership of the substance is intended; contrary to when he says 'I fed you this land', because that is a loan, as land is not eaten, so the intention is to eat its produce. As for the second word, because the letter lam is for ownership. As for the third word, because of the Prophet's saying: 'Whoever gives a life grant, it belongs to the one granted and to his heirs after him.' Similarly if he says 'I made this house for you as a life grant' for the reason we mentioned. As for the fourth word, because 'mounting' is literally riding, so it is a loan, but it may also be hibah. It is said 'The amir mounted so-and-so on a horse' and ownership is intended, so it is interpreted accordingly when intended. Explanation of his saying 'and hibah is concluded...': The words by which hibah is concluded are: wahaba, nahala, a'ta. Among them, the first word 'wahaba' is explicit in the meaning of hibah. The second word 'nahala' is used metaphorically in the same meaning. Thus the prophetic instruction: 'Did you bestow upon each of your children...' His saying 'Did you bestow upon each of your children...' This hadith is narrated by the six [authorities] from Nu'man bin Bashir with various wordings. The wording in Sahih Bukhari is: 'From Nu'man bin Bashir that his father brought him to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: I have bestowed (nahaltu) upon this son of mine a slave. He said: Did you bestow upon each of your children like this? He said: No. He said: Then take it back.' His saying 'because feeding when added...' The reason for the conclusion of hibah by the phrase 'I fed you this food' is that when feeding is attributed to something that is itself eaten, like grain, wheat, dates, bread etc., then it means ownership of the substance. So the meaning is: I have made you the owner of this thing, and that is called hibah. Contrary if it is attributed to something that is not itself eaten, like land, then in that case 'feeding' means loan, and the meaning would be: I gave you this land so that you cultivate it and get grain and benefit from it. On this, Shaykh Ansari in Ghayat al-Bayan objected that this explanation by the author of al-Hidayah is open to consideration, because according to this explanation, in the verse 'feeding ten poor persons' (Quran 5:89), 'feeding' would mean ownership, not permissibility (ibaha) as others say, because 'feeding' here is added to 'food' which is eaten. The answer is that by 'added to what is itself eaten' the author of al-Hidayah means that he mentions a thing that is itself eaten and makes it the second object of 'feeding', as the jurists have stated: when the second object is mentioned, it indicates ownership; otherwise it indicates permissibility. In the verse, it is not like that, so the word 'feeding' remains on its original meaning, i.e., permissibility. His saying 'as for the third...' By the third word, i.e., saying 'I granted you this thing as a life grant ('umra)', hibah is also concluded, because the hadith 'Whoever gives a life grant, it is for the one granted' makes it like the second word in meaning: he transferred ownership, and that is hibah. Similarly if he says 'I made this house for you as a life grant', it is also hibah by the aforementioned evidence. His saying 'Whoever gives a life grant...' This hadith is narrated by Imam Bukhari and the other five from Jabir.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the valid wording for a hibah contract. It begins by listing three explicit words: wahaba (gave), nahala (bestowed), and a'ta (granted). The first is explicit; the second is supported by a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) used nahala in the context of a gift; the third is used in the same sense in Arabic. The passage then lists other words that can constitute hibah with intention: (1) 'at'amtu' (I fed you) – when applied to something edible, it means ownership, but for land it means a loan; (2) 'ja'altu' (I made) – because the letter lam indicates ownership; (3) 'a'martu' (I gave as a life grant) – based on the hadith that 'umra belongs to the donee and his heirs; (4) 'hamaltu' (I mounted) – literally a loan, but when intended as hibah, it is accepted. The commentary also addresses a critique by Shaykh Ansari regarding the interpretation of 'at'amtu' in the context of Quranic verse, explaining that the difference lies in whether the second object is mentioned. The passage is from the chapter on hibah in al-Hidayah, and the commentary (Ashraf al-Hidayah) expands on it.

Key Terms
طعام (ta'am): Food; when used as the object of 'at'amtu' and explicitly mentioned, it indicates ownership.
عمرى (umra): A life grant; giving property for the donee's lifetime, which becomes ownership according to the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling if someone says 'I fed you this land'?
A) It is a valid hibah of the land.
B) It is a loan (ariyah), not a gift.
C) It is invalid because land cannot be fed.
D) It is a sale if the recipient pays.

Key Takeaway
Implicit words can conclude hibah with proper intention, but specific rules apply: 'at'amtu' for edible objects indicates ownership, 'ja'altu' with lam indicates ownership, 'a'martu' is based on hadith, and 'hamaltu' requires intention; the madhhab dispute on 'at'amtu' is resolved by the mention of the second object.

Effect of Wording in Gift and Loan Contracts
Explaining the effect of specific words in gift contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for key wordings (kasawa, manhattan, haml, hibah sukna, hibah taskunaha) and explain the proof from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
The definitive word controls: ambiguous terms are interpreted in light of definitive ones.

In Hanafi fiqh, the words used in a contract determine whether it is a gift (hibah) or a loan (ariyah). Some words like 'kasawtuka' always indicate a gift, while 'manahtuka' indicates a loan. When combined words create ambiguity, the definitive meaning prevails. This lesson examines the rulings and proofs for these wordings from the Hidayah commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wording and its ruling
Read the passage to see which wording is being discussed and whether the Hanafi school classifies it as hibah or ariyah.
e.g., 'kasawtuka' = hibah; 'manahtuka' = ariyah
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: Quran verse or hadith. For 'kasawtuka', the Quran (5:89) is used. For 'manahtuka', the hadith 'al-muntaha mardudah'.
The passage also uses custom (urf) as evidence for 'haml'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Determine how the dalil proves the ruling. For 'kiswah', the Quranic usage implies ownership transfer. For 'manhattan', the hadith indicates the item must be returned, so it is a loan.
The linkage is based on common understanding and usage.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Observe the opposing view: some scholars consider 'manhattan' as a gift. The Hanafi response uses the definitive meaning rule.
Also intra-Hanafi critique from Sahib Nata'ij is addressed.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that 'manhattan' is a loan, supported by hadith and the principle that ambiguous terms yield to definitive ones.
The commentary defends the Hidayah position.

قَالَ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من اعمرر جلا عمری له ولعقبه فقد قطع قوله حقه فيها و هي لمن اعمرو لعقبة.
آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا۔ جو کوئی عمرہ کرے کسی کے لئے اور اس کے وارثوں کے لئے تو اس نے اپنا حق کھو دیا۔ اب وہ معملہ کا ہو گا۔ اور اس کے وارثوں کا۔
قوله واما الرابع الخ چوتھے لفظ یعنی حمل سے انعقاد ہبہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ لفظ حمل کے حقیقی و لغوی معنی ارکاب یعنی سوار کرنا ہے۔ تو اس معنی کر یہ عاریت ہوگا۔ لیکن اس میں ہبہ کا بھی احتمال ہے۔ چنانچہ بولتے ہیں حمل الامير فلان على فرس اور اس سے مراد یہ ہوتی ہے کہ امیر نے فلاں کو گھوڑے کا مالک کر دیا۔ پس جب ہبہ کی نیت ہو تو اسی پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ پھر یہاں یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے عاریت میں کہا تھا۔ ان قوله حملتك لتمليك العين اور یہاں کہہ رہے ہیں۔ ان حقيقة الارکاب۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ لفظ حمل کا حقیقہ معنی ارکاب ہونا وضع کے پیش نظر ہے اور تملیک عین کے لئے ہونا عرف واستعمال کے لحاظ سے ہے۔ لیکن عرفہ کی وجہ سے حقیقت مہجور نہیں ہو گئی۔ پس لفظ حمل اسم مشترک کے معنی میں ہوا۔
كسوتك هذا الثوب كے الفاظ سے ہبہ درست ہے، منحتك هذه الجاریة کے الفاظ سے عاریہ ہوگا وَلَوْ قَالَ كِسْوَتُكَ هذَا التَّوْبَ يَكُونُ هِبَةً لِأَنَّهُ يُرَادُ بِهِ التَّمْلِيْكُ قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى اَوْ كِسْوَتُهُمْ وَيُقَالُ كَسَى الْأَمِيرُ فَلَانًا قَوْبًا أَي مَلكَهُ مِنْهُ وَلَوْ قَالَ مَنَحْتُكَ هَذِهِ الْجَارِيَةَ كَانَتْ عَارِيَةً لِمَا رَوَيْنَا مِنْ قَبْلُ وَلَوْ قَالَ دَارِي لَكَ هِبَةٌ سُكْنى اَوْ سكنى هِبَةً فَهِيَ عَارِيَةً لِاَنَّ الْعَارِيَةَ مُحْكَمَةٌ فِى تَمْلِيكِ الْمَنْفَعَةِ وَالْهِبَةُ تَحْتَمِلُهَا وَتَحْتَمِلُ تَمْلِيْكَ الْعَيْنِ فَيَحْمَلُ الْمُحْتَمَلُ عَلَى الْمُحْكَم وَكَذَا إِذَا قَالَ عُمْرَى سُكْنى اَوْ تُخلى سكنى أو سكنى صَدَقَةً أَوْ صَدَقَةً عَارِيَةً أَوْ عَارِيَةٌ هَبَةً لِمَا قَدَّمْنَاهُ وَلَوْ قَالَ هِبَةٌ تَسْكُنُهَا فَهِيَ هِبَةٌ لِاَنَّ قَوْلَهُ تَسْكُنُهَا مَشْوَرَةٌ وَلَيْسَ بِتَفْسِيرٍ لَهُ وَهُوَ تَبَيَة عَلَى الْمَقْصُودِ بخِلَافِ قَوْلِهِ هِيَةٌ سُكْنى لِأَنَّهُ تَفْسِيرٌ لَهُ.
ترجمہ اگر کہا کہ میں نے تجھے یہ کپڑا پہنایا تو ہبہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس سے تملیک مراد ہوتی ہے۔ حق تعالے کا ارشاد ہے اوكسو قسم اور کہا جاتا ہے امیر نے فلاں کو کپڑا پہنایا یعنی اس کا مالک کر دیا۔ اگر کہا کہ میں نے تجھے یہ باندی منحہ دی تو عاریت ہے۔ بدلیل اس کے جو ہم نے پہلے روایت کی ۔ اگر کہا کہ میرا گھر تیرے لئے بہہ سکتی ہے یا سکتی ہبہ ہے تو یہ عاریت ہے۔ کیونکہ عاریت تملیک عین منفعت میں قطعی ہے۔ اور ہبہ اس کا بھی محتمل ہے اور تملیک مین کا بھی تو محمل کو حکم پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر اس نے کہا کہ میرا گھر تیرے لئے عمری سکنی ہے یا نحلی سکنی ہے۔ یا سک صدقہ ہے یا صدقہ عاریہ ہے یا عاریہ ہیہ ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے جو ہم نے پہلے بیان کی۔ اگر یہ کہا کہ مہ ہے تو اس میں سکونت کرے تو یہ ہبہ ہو گا کیونکہ اس کا قول لتسكنها مشورہ ہے۔ ہبہ کی تفسیر نہیں ہے اور یہ مقصود پر تنبیہ ہے بخلاف مہبہ سکنی کے کہ یہ اس کی تفسیر ہے۔ تشریح قوله ولو قال منحتك الخ اگر کسی نے یہ کہا منحتك هذه الجارية تو یہ عاریت ہوگا۔ بدلیل حدیث سابق المنتحہ مردود ممکن ہے کوئی یہ کہے کہ صفحہ بمعنی ہیہ بھی آتا ہے۔
جواب یہ ہے کہ اول تو منحہ در حقیقت عاریت ہے اور مجاز بمعنی ہیہ ہے پس مجاز نہیں لیا جائے گا۔
دوم یہ کہ مواد اگر لفظ منحہ دونوں کا محتمل ہو تب بھی بہیہ کا مرتبہ اعلیٰ ہے۔ پس عاریت کا در جو کمتر ہے وہ یقینی ہوا اور ہبہ میں شک ہوا۔ لہذاہبہ پر محمول نہیں کیا جائے گا ( عین )۔
تنبیه.. صاحب نتائج نے یہاں دو وجہ سے کلام کیا ہے۔
اوّل یہ کہ مسئلہ منحہ کو مسئلہ حمل سے جدا کر کے ذکر کرنا اور عدم ارادہ کی قید نہ لگانا نہیں بتا رہا ہے کہ صحتك بده الجارية کہنے سے عاریت ہوگی۔ اگر چہ وہ منحہ سے ہبہ کا ارادہ کرے۔ حالانکہ کتاب العارية میں کہا تھا کہ سنتحك هذا الثواب اور حملتك على هذا الدابته كہنا عاریت ہوگا۔ بشرطیکہ ان سے بہیہ کا ارادہ نہ ہو اور اس کی تعمیل میں کہا تھا کہ لفظ منحہ اور حمل دونوں تملیک مین کے لئے ہیں اور ہبہ کا ارادہ نہ ہونے کے وقت مجاز اتملیک منافع پر محمول ہوتا ہے۔ پس دونوں جگہ کے دونوں کلاموں میں ایک طرح کا تنافر ہے۔
دوم ... يه که کتاب العاریہ میں مذکور شد : حدیث " المنتحہ مردورہ کے ساتھ اس مسئلہ کی تعلیل محل نظر ہے اس لئے کہ محیط میں اصل یعنی مبسوط سے منقول ہے کہ اگر کسی نے یہ کہا منحتك هذا الدراهم وهذا الطعام تو یہ نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر يه كہا منحتك هذا الارض او هذه الجارية تو یہ عاریت ہوگا۔ اس کے بعد کہا ہے کہ پس اصل کلی یہ نکلی کہ جب لفظ محہ کی اضافت ایسی چیز کی طرف ہو جس سے انتفاع مع بقاء عین ممکن ہو تو عاریت ہوگی " ( انهی ) عام معتبرات میں بھی یونہی مذکور ہے ۔ حالانکہ حدیث مذکوران دونوں فصلوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں کرتی۔ فتعليل الفصل الثانى به ينتقض با لفصل الاول قوله هبته سکنی اور سکنی هسته میں لفظ بہ حال یا تمیز ہونے کی بناء پر منصوب ہے۔ لمافی قوله دارى لك من الابهام .... الخ مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر واجب یوں کہے دارى لك هبته سكنى يايوں كے دارى لك سكنى هبته تو اس سے ہبہ نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ لفظ سکنی تملیک منفعت میں محکم ہے تو اس سے عاریت ہوگی نہ کہ ہبہ خواہ لفظ ہبہ کو مقدم ذکر کرے یا مؤخر اور ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایجاب کا لفظ تملیک رقبہ پر دال ہو تو ہبہ ہوگا اور تملیک منافع پر دال ہو تو عاربیت اور اگر دونوں کا احتمال ہو تو نیت کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ اب کلام مذکور میں دو احتمال ہیں ایک یہ کہ تملیک منفعت مراد ہو۔ کیونکہ لفظ سکنی تملیک منفعت کیلئے قطعی ہے۔ تملیک عین کا احتمال نہیں ہے اور لفظ بہ جواس کے ساتھ ملایا ہے اس میں تملیک مین اور تملیک منفعت دونوں کا احتمال ہے۔ پس اگر لفظ سکنی کا لحاظ کیا جائے تو مریض عاریت ہے اور اگر لفظ ہبہ کا لحاظ کیا جائے تو عاریت اور مہبہ دونوں کا احتمال ہے۔ پس محتمل کو چھوڑ کر قطعی معنی پرمحمول کیا جائے گا۔ قوله ليس بتفسير ... الخ یعنی اس کا تسكنھا کہنا اس بہیہ کی تفسیر نہیں ہے بلکہ بطور مشورہ ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ تسکنبہ فعل ہے جو اسم (ہبہ ) کی تفسیر نہیں ہوسکتا۔ بخلاف ہتہ سکنی اسم ہے تو یہ دوسرے اسم (ہبہ) کی تفسیر ہوسکتا ہے۔ اگر کوئی یہ کہے کہ آیت "هل ادلــكـم عـلـى تـجـارة تنجيكم من عذاب الیم تؤمنون بالله " میں تنجیکم اور تؤمنون فعل اسم تجارة کی تفسیر ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ قیر نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ تبیین ہے اور تفسیر و تبیین میں فرق ہے۔
The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: Whoever makes a life grant (umra) for someone and his descendants, his statement cuts off his right in it, and it belongs to the one who was given the life grant and his descendants. The Prophet ﷺ said: Whoever makes a life grant for someone and his heirs, then he has lost his right; now it belongs to the recipient and his heirs. (Commentary:) The fourth wording, meaning 'haml' (mounting), establishes a gift because the real and literal meaning of 'haml' is to mount (rakub). So in that meaning it is a loan (ariyah). But it also carries the possibility of gift. Thus they say: 'The amir mounted so-and-so on a horse' meaning the amir made him the owner of the horse. So when intention of gift is present, it is interpreted accordingly. Then an objection arises: The author of Hidayah said in the book of Ariyah that 'hamaltuka' is for ownership of the substance (tamlik al-ayn), while here he says the reality is mounting (irkab). The answer: The literal meaning of 'haml' is mounting from the perspective of coinage, while its use for ownership of the substance is based on custom and usage. But due to custom, the real meaning is not abandoned; thus 'haml' becomes a homonym. The wording 'kasawtuka hatha al-thawb' constitutes a gift, while 'manahtuka hadhihi al-jariyah' constitutes a loan. If he says 'kaswatuka hatha al-thawb' it is a gift because it denotes ownership. Allah Almighty says: 'or their clothing' (Quran 5:89). And it is said: 'The amir clothed so-and-so with a garment' meaning he made him its owner. If he says 'manahtuka hadhihi al-jariyah' it is a loan based on what we previously narrated. If he says 'dari laka hibah sukna' or 'sukna hibah' then it is a loan because the word 'sukna' is definitive for ownership of benefit, while 'hibah' can imply both ownership of benefit and ownership of substance. So the ambiguous is interpreted in light of the definitive. Similarly if he says 'umra sukna' or 'tukhla sukna' or 'sukna sadaqah' or 'sadaqah ariyah' or 'ariyah hibah', the same rule applies. If he says 'hibah taskunaha' then it is a gift because his saying 'taskunaha' is advice, not an interpretation, and it points to the purpose, unlike his saying 'hibah sukna' which is an interpretation. (Urdu translation of the above Arabic:) ... (Then detailed commentary on 'manhattan' and 'haml', citing hadith 'al-muntaha mardudah', and critique by Sahib Nata'ij about inconsistency. Then discussion of 'hibata sukna' and distinction between tafsir and tabyin.)
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal exposition from the commentary of Hidayah on the effect of specific wordings in gift contracts. It opens with a hadith about 'umra (life grant) to illustrate that certain wordings irrevocably transfer ownership. The main discussion focuses on the fourth wording 'haml' (to mount), explaining that while its literal meaning is to give temporary use (ariyah), custom allows it to be used for outright ownership (tamlik al-ayn), making it a homonym. The commentator then presents the rulings: 'kasawtuka' (I clothed you) always constitutes a gift because the Quranic usage (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:89) and common parlance point to ownership transfer. In contrast, 'manahtuka' (I granted you) is a loan unless proven otherwise, based on the hadith 'al-muntaha mardudah'. When a contract combines words like 'hibah sukna' (gift of residence), the principle is that the definitive word ('sukna' for benefit) controls, making it a loan; but 'hibah taskunaha' (a gift that you reside in) is a proper gift because 'taskunaha' is mere advice, not a qualifier. The commentator also addresses an intra-Hanafi critique from Sahib Nata'ij regarding inconsistency in the treatment of 'manhattan' and 'haml'. Finally, the passage distinguishes tafsir (interpretation, which changes legal effect) from tabyin (clarification, which does not), citing the Quranic verse 61:10-11 as an example of tabyin. The overall rule: if the wording clearly indicates ownership of the substance, it is a gift; if it indicates ownership of benefits, it is a loan; if both are possible, the definitive meaning prevails.

Key Terms
هِبَة (hibah): A contract that grants ownership of a specific substance (tamlik al-ayn) without consideration, usually immediately.
عَارِيَة (ariyah): A contract that grants ownership of the benefit (manfa'ah) of a property while the substance remains with the owner.
تَفْسِير (tafsir): A clarification that changes the legal nature of the contract; e.g., saying 'hibah sukna' makes it a loan because 'sukna' interprets the gift as of benefit only.
تَبْيِين (tabyin): A clarification that does not alter the legal ruling; e.g., 'hibah taskunaha' is a gift, and 'taskunaha' merely points out the intended use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone says 'Dari laka hibah sukna', what is the ruling?
A) It is a valid gift (hibah) of the house.
B) It is a loan (ariyah) of the house.
C) It is invalid because of ambiguous wording.
D) It is a sale.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when contract wording is ambiguous, the definitive meaning (e.g., from hadith or clear usage) controls, and tafsir changes the legal nature while tabyin does not.

Gift of an Undivided Share: When is it Valid?
Ruling statement on hibah musha' with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hibah musha' and distinguish between divisible and indivisible property for the purpose of gifting an undivided share.

Core Idea
Gift of an undivided share is valid in indivisible property but requires possession and division in divisible property.

The gift of an undivided share (hibah musha') is a common transaction in joint property. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on whether the property can be divided without harm. This lesson unpacks the ruling from the matn of al-Hidayah, explaining the key conditions and the rationale behind the distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is gifting an undivided share (musha') in jointly owned property. The matn states two rulings: one for divisible property and one for indivisible.
2
Distinguish divisible vs. indivisible property
Divisible property (ma yuqsam) is that which can be divided without harming its value or utility. Indivisible (ma la yuqsam) is property where division would cause damage (e.g., a small room, a shared pathway).
The criterion is harm to value, not physical possibility.
3
Apply the condition of possession and division
For divisible property, the gift is invalid unless the donor takes possession (qabd) and the share is physically separated (divided). For indivisible property, possession of the undivided share suffices.
The condition of division ensures clarity of ownership and prevents dispute.
4
Determine the ruling for a given scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., half of a commercial building, half of a well), first assess divisibility: can it be divided without harming value? Then apply the conditions to conclude validity.
Practice applying to everyday examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہبہ مشاع کی بحث
قَالَ وَلَا تَجُوزُ الْهِبَةُ فِيْمَا يُقْسَمُ إِلَّا مَحُوزَة مَقْسُومَةً وَهِبَةُ المُشَاعِ فِيمَا لَا يُقْسَمُ جَائِزٌ ترجمہ اور جائز نہیں ہبہ قابل تقسیم چیزوں میں مگر یہ حقوق سے فارغ او تقسیم شدہ ہواور غیر مقوم کا بہ جائز ہے اس میں جو تقسیم نہ ہو سکے۔ تشريح قوله ولا يجوز الهيته ... الخ اس قول میں ہبہ مشاع کا بیان ہے جو کو ایک اہم بحث ہے کہ یہ جائز ہے یانہیں؟ تشریح بحث سے پہلے چند چیزیں ذہن نشین رہنی چاہئیں۔ اول یہ کہ ما قسم و مالا يقسم سے مراد کیا ہے۔؟ سو جانا چاہیے کہ ہر وہ چیز جس کے لئے تبعیض ( ٹکڑے ٹکڑے کرنا) مضر ہو اور اس کی
Discussion of hibah musha'. He (the author) said: 'The gift is not permissible in that which is divisible unless it is possessed and divided, and the gift of an undivided share in that which is not divisible is permissible.' Translation: Gift is not permissible in divisible things unless it is free of rights (?) and divided, and gift of an undivided share is permissible in that which cannot be divided. Commentary: This statement explains hibah musha', which is an important discussion: is it permissible or not? Before the explanation, a few things should be kept in mind. First: What is meant by 'that which is divisible' and 'that which is not divisible'? It should be known that every thing for which division (breaking into pieces) is harmful and its...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage introduces the ruling on hibah musha' (gift of an undivided share) from the matn of Hidayah. The matn states two rulings: (1) A gift of an undivided share in divisible property is not valid unless the donor takes possession and the property is actually divided (i.e., the share is physically separated). (2) A gift of an undivided share in indivisible property is valid as is. The commentary begins by explaining the key concepts: 'ma yuqsam' (divisible) and 'ma la yuqsam' (indivisible). Divisible property is that for which division would cause harm or destruction of value, while indivisible property cannot be divided without destroying its utility. The commentary then proceeds to elaborate on the conditions and reasoning behind this ruling. The discussion is important because it relates to the validity of gifts of shares in jointly owned property.

Key Terms
مُشَاع (musha'): An undivided share in jointly owned property; e.g., half of a house without physical partition.
مَا يُقْسَمُ (ma yuqsam): Divisible property: property that can be divided without harming its value or utility.
مَحُوزَة مَقْسُومَة (mahuza maqsuma): Possessed and divided: the gift must be physically taken into possession and the share separated from the rest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it valid to gift an undivided half share of a commercial building (which can be divided without harm) without physically separating the share?
A) Yes, it is valid.
B) No, it is not valid because the property is divisible and the share was not separated.
C) Yes, only if the recipient is a relative.
D) It is valid only if the donor retains the other half.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the validity of gifting an undivided share depends entirely on whether the property is divisible or indivisible.

Intra-Hanafi Critique: Inconsistency in Manīḥah and ʿĀriyah Rulings
Critical note on inconsistencies in manīḥah/ʿāriyah rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two objections raised by the author of Nata’ij against the Hidayah's rulings on manīḥah and ʿāriyah, and explain why they reveal an inconsistency in reasoning.

Core Idea
A ruling that ignores its own conditions exposes its reasoning to internal critique.

The Hidayah contains rulings on manīḥah (gift of use) and ʿāriyah (loan). However, the author of Nata’ij points out two inconsistencies: first, a contradiction between the Book of Hibah and the Book of ʿĀriyah regarding the role of intention; second, a flawed reliance on a hadith that does not support the distinction made. This lesson dissects these critiques, sharpening your ability to detect inconsistency within a single madhhab's texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
Read the passage carefully and list the two distinct criticisms the author of Nata’ij directs against the Hidayah. One concerns a contradiction between two sections of the Hidayah itself; the other concerns the use of a hadith as evidence.
The first objection is about intention; the second about the hadith 'al-muntaḥatu mardūdah'.
2
Trace the first objection: compare the rulings
In the Book of Hibah, the Hidayah rules that saying 'ṣaḥḥaka biddah al-jāriyah' results in ʿāriyah regardless of intention. In the Book of ʿĀriyah, similar phrases are ʿāriyah only if no gift is intended. Identify the inconsistency: does intention matter or not?
The author of Nata’ij argues that the two statements conflict.
3
Trace the second objection: analyze the hadith and principle
The Hidayah uses the hadith 'al-muntaḥatu mardūdah' to support a distinction: manīḥah of a non-consumable becomes ʿāriyah, but of a consumable does not. The author of Nata’ij notes that the hadith itself does not differentiate; thus the reasoning is invalid. Check the reported principle from al-Mabsūṭ.
The hadith applies to all manīḥah, but the Hidayah only applies it to non-consumables.
4
Understand the overall critique
The author of Nata’ij concludes that there is incongruity (tanāfur) between the two sections of the Hidayah and that the reliance on the hadith is questioned because it does not justify the distinction. This shows that even within a single madhhab, scholars critically examine each other's reasoning.
The critique is methodological, not a rejection of the rulings themselves.

Chapter of Gift. It will not be carried (ʿayn). Caution: The author of Nata’ij has spoken here for two reasons. First: that the issue of manihah is mentioned separately from the issue of pregnancy, and not restricting it to lack of intention, does not indicate that saying 'ṣaḥḥaka biddah al-jāriyah' would be a loan, even if he intends a gift by manihah. Whereas in the Book of Loan it was said that saying 'santaḥuka hādhā al-thawāb' and 'ḥamaltuka ʿalā hādhā al-dābbah' would be a loan, provided they do not intend a gift from them, and in its explanation it was said that the words manihah and ḥaml are both for ownership of the substance, and when there is no intention of gift, they are metaphorically construed for ownership of benefits. So there is a kind of incongruity between the two statements in both places. Second: that mentioned in the Book of Loan: the hadith 'al-muntaḥatu mardūdah' ... the reasoning for this issue is open to scrutiny because in al-Muḥīṭ, from al-Mabsūṭ, it is reported that if someone said 'manaḥtuka hādhā al-darāhima wa hādhā al-ṭaʿām', it would not be [a loan], and if he said 'manaḥtuka hādhā al-arḍa aw hādhihi al-jāriyah', it would be a loan. After that he said: thus the general principle is that when the word manīḥah is added to something from which benefit with the preservation of the substance is possible, it becomes a loan. It is similarly mentioned in the general reliable works. Yet the aforementioned hadith does not differentiate between the two sections. So the reasoning of the second section is invalidated by the first section.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a critical note (tanbīh) from the author of the Nata’ij, objecting to two apparent inconsistencies in the Hidayah. The first objection concerns the treatment of manīḥah (gift of use) versus ʿāriyah (loan). In the Book of Hibah, the ruling is given that saying 'ṣaḥḥaka biddah al-jāriyah' results in ʿāriyah, regardless of intention, while in the Book of ʿĀriyah, similar phrases are ʿāriyah only if no gift is intended. The author sees a contradiction. The second objection points out that the hadith 'al-muntaḥatu mardūdah' (the one given for use is returned) is used to support a distinction based on the object, but the hadith itself does not differentiate. The commentary from al-Muḥīṭ and al-Mabsūṭ makes a distinction between consumable and non-consumable items, but the hadith applies to both, thus the reasoning is flawed. The passage highlights a scholarly debate within the Hanafi school regarding the precise boundaries between hibah and ʿāriyah.

Key Terms
منحہ (manīḥah): A gift of the use of an object (temporary transfer of benefit) as opposed to ownership of the substance.
عاریت (ʿāriyah): A loan of an object for use with the substance remaining; the object must be returned.
تنافر (tanāfur): Incongruity or inconsistency between two statements or rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the critique, what is the second objection raised by the author of Nata’ij?
A) That the hadith 'al-muntaḥatu mardūdah' is weak in its chain of transmission.
B) That the hadith does not differentiate between consumable and non-consumable items, yet the Hidayah uses it to support that distinction.
C) That the Hidayah fails to mention the condition of possession (qabd) in the Book of Hibah.
D) That the principle from al-Mabsūṭ is not reliable.

Key Takeaway
The Hidayah's treatment of manīḥah and ʿāriyah contains internal inconsistencies that later Hanafi scholars critiqued, underscoring the importance of coherent reasoning.

Interpreting 'Hibatan Sukna': When 'Gift' Means Loan
Ruling on interpreting compound gift phrases with 'sukna'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hibah and aariyah based on the wording of the offer, and apply the Hanafi rule that definitive words for benefit transfer override ambiguous words for ownership.

Core Idea
A gift phrase including 'sukna' becomes a loan, because usufruct wording is definitive.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common confusion: when someone uses the word 'hibah' (gift) but adds 'sukna' (residence), what is the legal outcome? The Hanafi scholars rule that the transaction becomes aariyah (loan) because the word 'sukna' definitively indicates a transfer of benefit, not ownership. This lesson explores the linguistic principles and the rule for resolving ambiguity in contract wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compound phrase
The phrase 'dārī laka hibatan sukna' contains both 'hibah' and 'sukna'. Note that 'sukna' is in the accusative case, functioning as a state or specification.
2
Recognize the two components
Each word has a distinct legal indication: 'hibah' can indicate transfer of ownership (tamlīk al-raqabah) or benefit; 'sukna' definitively indicates transfer of benefit (tamlīk al-manfa'ah).
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
The rule: if the wording indicates ownership of substance → hibah; if it indicates ownership of benefits → aariyah; if both possible → intention is considered. Here 'sukna' is unambiguous for benefit, so it governs.
The definitive meaning takes precedence over the probable.
4
Address the counterargument
Some might argue that the verb 'taskunuhā' clarifies the gift as residence, but the commentator distinguishes between tafsīr (interpretation by a noun) and bayān (clarification by a verb). A verb cannot interpret a noun; thus 'taskunuhā' is merely advice.
The Quranic example (tijārah... tunjīkum) is bayān, not tafsīr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله هبته سکنی اور سکنی هسته میں لفظ بہ حال یا تمیز ہونے کی بناء پر منصوب ہے۔ لمافی قوله دارى لك من الابهام .... الخ مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر واجب یوں کہے دارى لك هبته سكنى يايوں كے دارى لك سكنى هبته تو اس سے ہبہ نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ لفظ سکنی تملیک منفعت میں محکم ہے تو اس سے عاریت ہوگی نہ کہ ہبہ خواہ لفظ ہبہ کو مقدم ذکر کرے یا مؤخر اور ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایجاب کا لفظ تملیک رقبہ پر دال ہو تو ہبہ ہوگا اور تملیک منافع پر دال ہو تو عاربیت اور اگر دونوں کا احتمال ہو تو نیت کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ اب کلام مذکور میں دو احتمال ہیں ایک یہ کہ تملیک منفعت مراد ہو۔ کیونکہ لفظ سکنی تملیک منفعت کیلئے قطعی ہے۔ تملیک عین کا احتمال نہیں ہے اور لفظ بہ جواس کے ساتھ ملایا ہے اس میں تملیک مین اور تملیک منفعت دونوں کا احتمال ہے۔ پس اگر لفظ سکنی کا لحاظ کیا جائے تو مریض عاریت ہے اور اگر لفظ ہبہ کا لحاظ کیا جائے تو عاریت اور مہبہ دونوں کا احتمال ہے۔ پس محتمل کو چھوڑ کر قطعی معنی پرمحمول کیا جائے گا۔ قوله ليس بتفسير ... الخ یعنی اس کا تسكنھا کہنا اس بہیہ کی تفسیر نہیں ہے بلکہ بطور مشورہ ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ تسكنبہ فعل ہے جو اسم (ہبہ ) کی تفسیر نہیں ہوسکتا۔ بخلاف ہتہ سکنی اسم ہے تو یہ دوسرے اسم (ہبہ) کی تفسیر ہوسکتا ہے۔ اگر کوئی یہ کہے کہ آیت "هل ادلــكـم عـلـى تـجـارة تنجيكم من عذاب الیم تؤمنون بالله " میں تنجیکم اور تؤمنون فعل اسم تجارة کی تفسیر ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ قیر نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ تبیین ہے اور تفسیر و تبیین میں فرق ہے۔
His statement: 'hibatan sukna' – and 'sukna' is in the accusative because it is a state or specification. The meaning of his statement 'dārī laka' from the ambiguity etc. is that if the obligator says 'dārī laka hibatan sukna' or 'dārī laka sukna hibatan', this does not constitute a gift. Because the word 'sukna' is authoritative in transferring benefit, so it becomes a loan, not a gift, whether the word 'hibah' is mentioned first or last. The rule is that if the wording of offer indicates ownership of the substance, it is a gift; if it indicates ownership of benefits, it is a loan; and if both are possible, intention is considered. In the present speech, there are two probabilities: one is that transfer of benefit is intended, because the word 'sukna' is definitive for transfer of benefit, with no possibility of ownership of substance; and the word 'hibah' joined to it has both possibilities. So if the word 'sukna' is considered, it is a loan; if the word 'hibah' is considered, both loan and gift are probable. Therefore the probable is abandoned and it is construed upon the definitive meaning. His statement: 'it is not an interpretation' means that his saying 'taskunuhā' is not an interpretation of this gift, but rather a piece of advice. The reason is that 'taskunuhā' is a verb, which cannot be an interpretation of a noun (hibah). In contrast, 'hātihā sukna' is a noun, so it can be an interpretation of another noun (hibah). If someone argues that in the verse 'Hal adullukum ʿalā tijāratin tunjīkum min ʿadhābin alīmin tuʾminūna billāh' the verbs 'tunjīkum' and 'tuʾminūna' are interpretations of the noun 'tijārah', the answer is that this is not tafsīr but bayān, and there is a difference between tafsīr and bayān.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a detailed linguistic analysis of a compound phrase in a gift contract. The commentator explains that when someone says 'dārī laka hibatan sukna' (my house is for you as a gift for residence), the word 'sukna' (residence) is decisive in indicating a transfer of usufruct only, not ownership of the house. Therefore the transaction is a loan (ʿāriyah), not a gift (hibah), regardless of whether the word 'hibah' is used. The ruling is based on the principle that if the wording of the offer (ījāb) is explicit about transferring ownership of the substance, it is hibah; if explicit about transferring benefits, it is ʿāriyah; and if ambiguous, intention is considered. Here 'sukna' is unambiguous for benefit, so the ambiguity of 'hibah' is resolved in favor of the explicit meaning. The commentator also distinguishes between tafsīr (interpretation of a noun by another noun) and bayān (clarification by a verb), using a Quranic verse to illustrate the latter.

Key Terms
سکنی (suknā): Usufruct of residence; a specific type of benefit transfer.
تملیک منفعت (tamlīk al-manfaʿah): Transfer of ownership of the benefit/usufruct only, not the substance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'dārī laka hibatan sukna', what is the ruling in Hanafi fiqh?
A) It is a valid gift (hibah) of the house because the word 'hibah' is explicit.
B) It is a loan (ʿāriyah) of the house for residence, not a gift.
C) It is void because the wording is contradictory.
D) It depends on the intention of the speaker.

Key Takeaway
When a gift phrase includes a word definitive for benefit (like 'sukna'), the contract becomes aariyah, not hibah.

Hibah Mushā': Conditions for Validity in Divisible and Indivisible Property
Ruling on hibah mushā' with conditions and Shafi'i difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hibah mushā' for divisible and indivisible property, and explain the Shafi'i counterposition.

Core Idea
A gift of an undivided share is valid only in indivisible property or after actual partition in divisible property.

The gift of an undivided share (mushā') is a classic point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This passage from Al-Hidayah lays out the Hanafi position, distinguishing between property that can be divided without loss and property that cannot. It also presents the Shafi'i view, which permits hibah mushā' in both cases. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the conditions of mahūz (complete possession) and maqsūm (divided), as well as the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish divisible from indivisible property
Identify the two categories: divisible (mā yuqsam) — property that retains utility when divided; indivisible (mā lā yuqsam) — property that loses value or is unusable after division, e.g., a single garment or a tiny house.
The commentator lists examples: dirhams/dinars are divisible; a single slave or small bathhouse is not.
2
Apply the Hanafi conditions for divisible property
For divisible property, hibah mushā' is not effective unless the gifted share is mahūz (completely separated from the donor's ownership) and maqsūm (actually divided). Ownership transfers only after partition.
The text emphasizes that possession (qabd) must be complete, analogous to facing the entire Kaaba in prayer.
3
Understand the timing of possession
The condition of mushā' is checked at the time of possession, not at the time of contract. If the donor later separates the share and gives possession, the gift becomes valid.
Example: gifting half a house and then gifting the other half before delivery — both are valid if complete possession occurs.
4
Recognize the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hibah mushā' is valid in both divisible and indivisible property, analogizing to sale, loan, and bequest, which are valid in mushā'.
The Shafi'i school argues that mushā' can receive ownership, and the gratuitous nature does not prevent validity.
5
Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In the Hanafi school, gifting half a house requires actual division; in the Shafi'i school, the gift is effective immediately without division. This affects inheritance, sale, and other transactions.
The Hanafi mufta bihi is the ruling requiring partition.

Source Text

ایسی مالا يقسم ہے اور اس کے ماسواما يقسم ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ قابل قسمت اشیاء میں ہبہ مشاع (غیر مقسوم) کے جائز نہ ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ملک ثابت نہیں ہوتی یہ مطلب نہیں کہ ہبہ باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس قابل قسمت چیزوں میں مشاع کا عقد ہبہ تو جائز ہوگا۔ مگر ملکیت اس وقت ثابت ہوگی جب بٹوارہ کر کے الگ کر دی جائے اور وہ محوز ہو۔ یعنی اس کے ساتھ واہب کا کوئی تعلق نہ رہے۔ سوم یہ کہ شیوع کا اعتبار قبضہ کے وقت ہے نہ کہ بوقت عقد یہاں تک کہ اگر شاع کا ہی کیا پر انوار سے جدا کرکے سپرد کیا یا نصف دار ہبہ کر کے سپردگی سے پہلے نصف باقی بھی ہبہ کر کے سپر د کر دیا۔ تو ہبہ جائز ہوگا۔ چہارم یہ کہ ہبہ میں چونکہ قبضہ منصوص ہے اس لئے قبضہ کا بطریق کمال ہونا شرط ہو گا ۔ جیسے نماز میں استقبال قبلہ چونکہ نصا مشروط ہے اس لئے کامل استقبال ضروری ہے ۔ یہاں تک کہ صرف حطیم کا استقبال کافی نہ ہو گا ۔ جب یہ باتیں ذہن نشین ہو گئیں تو اب پہلے متن کو دیکھے۔ لايجوز الهبة فيما يقسم الامحوزة اس میں حوزہ سے مراد یہ ہے کہ ملک واہب اور اس کے حقوق سے فارغ ہو۔ اس قید کے زریعہ درخت پر لگے ہوئے پھل درخت کے بغیر ۔ پشت غنم پر رہتے ہوئے اون اور زمین پر کھڑی ہوئی کھیتی زمین کے بغیر ہبہ کرنے سے احتراز ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ ان سورتوں میں موہوب چیز مجوز یعنی بطریق کمال مقبوض نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ تو واہب کی ملک سے متصل ہے اور مقسومہ قید کے ذریعہ مشاع سے انتر از ہے کہ اگر درخت پر رہتے ہوئے پھلوں پر قبضہ کیا اور وہ موہوب لہ اور اس کے غیر کے درمیان مشترک رہے تو ہبہ جائز نہ ہوگا۔ پس عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہو کہ جن چیزوں میں تقسیم ہونے کی صلاحیت ہے اور واہب ایسی چیز ہبہ کرنا چاہے تو اگر وہ مجوز ہو یعنی ملک واہب اور اس کے حقوق سے فارغ ہوا اور مقسوم ہو تو اس کا ہبہ درست ہے اور اگر محوز و مقسوم نہ ہو تو درست نہیں اور چیزیں قسمت پزیر نہ ہوں۔ یعنی تقسیم کے بعد قابل انتفاع نہ رہیں تو ایسی چیزوں میں ہنہ مشاع یعنی ہونہ غیر مقسوم جائز ہے۔

امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَجُوزُ فِى الْوَجْهَيْنِ لأَنَّهُ عَقْدُ تَمْلِيْكِ فَيَصِحُ فِى الْمُشَاعِ وَغَيْرِهِ كَالْبَيْعِ بِأَنْوَاعِهِ وَ هذا لانَّ الْمُشَاعَ قَابِل لِحُكْمِهِ وهُوَ الْمِلْكُ فَيَكُونُ مَحَلالَهُ وَكَوْنُهُ تَبَرُّعًا لَا يُبْطِلُهُ الشَّيُوعَ كَالْقَرْضِ وَالْوَصِيَةِ.
......
ترجمہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ دونوں صورتوں میں جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ عقد تملیک ہے۔ تو وہ مشترک وغیرہ مشترک دونوں میں صحیح ہو گا جیسے بیع اپنی جمیع اقسام کے ساتھ اور یہ اس لئے کہ مشترک بھی حکم ہبہ یعنی ملک کو قبول کرتا ہے تو وہ بھی ہبہ کا محل ہوگا اور ہبہ کے احسان ہونے کو شرکت نہیں مٹاتی جیسے قرض اور وصیت۔ تشریح قوله وقال الشافعي الخ امام شافعی اور مالک و احمد فرماتے ہیں کہ شئی موہوب قابل تقسیم ہو یا نا قابل تقسیم بہر دو صورت ہیئہ مشاع جائز ہے۔ چنانچہ روضہ میں ہے یجوز هبه المشاع المنقسم وغیرہ سواء “ جو ہر مالکیہ میں ہے ولا يمتنع با لشيوع وان كان
Discussion of hibah of mushā'. He said: 'Gift is not permissible in what can be divided except when it is taken possession of (mahūzah) and divided (maqsūmah), and gift of mushā' in what cannot be divided is permissible.' Translation: Gift is not permissible in divisible items unless free from rights and divided; and gift of non-divisible items is permissible. Explanation of his statement 'لا يجوز الهبة الخ': This statement is about the gift of mushā', which is an important discussion: is it permissible or not? Before explanation, several things should be kept in mind. First: what is meant by 'what can be divided' and 'what cannot be divided'? Know that every thing for which division (cutting into pieces) is harmful and which decreases its value is 'what cannot be divided', like dirhams and dinars? And what is other than that is 'what can be divided'. Second: things that after division become completely incapable of use, like a single slave or a single animal, or the benefit that could be had before division is lost, like a small house, a small bathhouse, a millstone, etc., such things are 'what cannot be divided', and other than them are 'what can be divided'. A third reason for the distinction is that every thing that is shared between two, and one wants division and the other does not, and the judge cannot compel the unwilling one to divide, every such thing is 'what cannot be divided', and other than it is 'what can be divided'. Second: The meaning of the impermissibility of hibah mushā' (undivided) in divisible items is that ownership is not established; it does not mean that the gift becomes invalid. So the contract of gift of mushā' in divisible items is valid, but ownership is established only when division is made and it becomes mahūz (separated), i.e., the donor has no connection with it. Third: Consideration of mushā' applies at the time of possession, not at the time of contract, such that if one makes a gift of mushā' and then separates it from the rest before giving possession, or gifts half a house and then before giving possession gifts the remaining half and gives possession, the gift is valid. Fourth: Since possession (qabd) is textually required in gift, possession must be complete (kāmil), just as facing the qiblah is textually required in prayer, so complete facing is necessary, to the extent that facing only the Ḥaṭīm is not sufficient. When these points are understood, then look at the text. 'لا يجوز الهبة فيما يقسم إلا محوزة' – here 'mahūzah' means free from the ownership and rights of the donor. By this condition, the gift of fruit on a tree without the tree, wool on a sheep's back, and standing crops without the land are excluded, because in these cases the gifted thing is not mahūz, i.e., completely possessed, since it is still attached to the donor's property. And by the condition 'maqsūmah' (divided), the gift of mushā' is excluded; if possession is taken of fruit still on the tree and it remains shared between the recipient and others, the gift is not permissible. So the meaning of the text is: in items capable of division, if the donor wants to give a gift, it is valid only if it is mahūz (free from donor's rights) and maqsūmah (divided); otherwise it is not valid. In items not capable of division (i.e., after division they are not usable), the gift of mushā' (undivided) is permissible.

Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint: al-Shāfiʿī said: 'It is permissible in both cases because it is a contract of transfer of ownership, so it is valid in mushā' and non-mushā' like sale in all its types. This is because mushā' is capable of receiving its ruling, which is ownership, so it is its place; and its being a gratuitous contract does not nullify it due to mushā', like qarḍ (loan) and waṣiyyah (bequest).' Translation: Imam Shāfiʿī says it is permissible in both cases. Because this is a contract of transfer of ownership, so it is valid in both shared and non-shared, like sale in all its types, and this is because mushā' can accept its ruling, which is ownership, so it is its locus; and its being gratuitous does not nullify it due to mushā', like loan and bequest. Explanation of his statement 'وقال الشافعي الخ': Imam Shāfiʿī, Mālik, and Aḥmad say that the gifted item, whether divisible or not, the gift of mushā' is permissible in both cases. Thus in al-Rawḍah it is stated: 'The gift of mushā' in divisible and other is permissible, equally.' And in the Mālikī school: 'It is not prevented by mushā', even if...'
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the ruling on gifting an undivided share (mushā'). The author first states the matn: that gift of an undivided share is not valid in divisible property unless it is taken possession of (mahūzah) and divided (maqsūmah); but in indivisible property, it is valid even if undivided. The commentary clarifies key points: (1) The distinction between divisible (mā yuqsam) and indivisible (mā lā yuqsam) property: indivisible property is that which would lose value or utility if divided, such as a single garment, a house too small to split, or a single animal. Divisible property is that which can be divided without loss of utility. (2) The term 'mahūzah' means the gifted item must be completely separated from the donor's ownership and control, free of any rights or attachments. (3) The condition of possession (qabd) is crucial; for a gift to be effective, possession must be complete, similar to how facing the qiblah must be complete in prayer. (4) For divisible property, the contract is valid but ownership is suspended until the item is actually partitioned and delivered. For indivisible property, the gift is effective immediately even if undivided, because division is impossible. The passage then presents the Shafi'i (and Maliki, Hanbali) view that the gift of mushā' is valid in both types of property, analogizing it to sale, loan, and bequest, which are valid in mushā'. The Hanafi position is based on the nature of a gratuitous contract (tabarruʿ) and the requirement of complete possession to avoid ambiguity and dispute. The commentator explains the Shafi'i reasoning but does not provide a Hanafi rebuttal in this portion.

Key Terms
مشاع (mushāʿ): An undivided share in a jointly owned property; the share is a fraction (e.g., half, quarter) not physically separated.
محوز (maḥūz): Taken possession of completely, with the donor having no remaining connection or rights.
ما یقسم / مالا یقسم (mā yuqsam / mā lā yuqsam): Divisible property (which can be divided without loss of utility) vs. indivisible property (division would destroy utility or value).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a gift of an undivided half share of a divisible house is:
A) Valid immediately upon the contract.
B) Valid only after the house is physically divided and the half is handed over to the donee.
C) Completely invalid and null.
D) Valid but the donee must give something in return.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on hibah mushā' hinges on the nature of the property and the completeness of possession, distinguishing between divisible and indivisible items.

intermediate
8 min
Why Hanafis Invalidate Gifting Undivided Property (Hibah al-Musha')
Hanafi ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on hibah of musha'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that hibah of undivided property in divisible items is invalid, identify the condition of complete possession (qabd kamal), and explain the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i evidence from the Prophet's gift of his share.

Core Idea
Complete possession is essential for hibah; undivided property prevents it, making such gifts invalid in the Hanafi school.

In this lesson, we examine the classical dispute over gifting undivided property (musha'). The Hanafi school takes a strict position: such gifts are invalid because the donor cannot deliver complete possession. We will explore the rationale, the objections, and the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i school's proof.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position and Its Basis
Identify the ruling: hibah of musha' in divisible property is invalid. Note the key condition: complete possession (qabd kamal) is required.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the Condition of Complete Possession
Understand why undivided property prevents complete possession: the donor cannot deliver exclusive control, and the donee's ownership is incomplete.
Hanafis argue that partial possession is insufficient; completeness requires the ability to dispose of the item exclusively.
3
Examine the Shafi'i Evidence
Review the hadith of Qays (Prophet gifting his share of spoils) and the analogy to sale. What is the Shafi'i basis for permitting hibah of musha'?
The Shafi'i school considers the Prophet's act as general permission.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
Study the Hanafi refutation: the Prophet's gift was a specific exception (khususiyyah); sale is different because it involves consideration; the hadith of Ibn 'Umar shows the importance of immediate possession.
The Hanafi response also refutes qiyas on wasiyyah and qard.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis require partition before transfer; Shafi'is allow immediate transfer. How does this affect transactions?
In practice, Hanafis advise against gifting undivided property unless it is first partitioned.
