Hiba of Attached Property: Hanafi vs Three Imams
Hanafi ruling on gift of attached property with madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi position on hiba of attached property with that of the three Imams, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Gifting attached property is like giving an undivided share — valid but requiring separate possession.

The Hanafi school treats the gift of items like milk in the udder or wool on the sheep as similar to a gift of an undivided share (mushā'). This lesson explores the reasoning behind this view and the dispute with the three Imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali), who consider such gifts permissible outright.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items in question
The passage lists milk in udders, wool on sheep, crops in the ground or on trees, and dates on palm trees. These are existent but attached to the donor's property.
They are not nonexistent; they are called متصل (attached).
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The gift is concluded (mun'aqid) but not permissible (ja'iz) until the donee takes separate possession after separation from the donor's property.
It is like the gift of an undivided share (مشاع).
3
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
The impediment to permissibility is the connection to the donor's property, which prevents the donee from taking possession. The items are existent, so the contract is valid, but ownership is not complete without possession.
Connection (اتصال) is similar to the common ownership in mushā'.
4
Contrast with the three Imams' view
The three Imams consider such gifts permissible immediately because the items are existent. They do not see attachment as an impediment.
The passage states: وعند الثلاثه يجوز (and according to the three, it is permissible).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
According to Hanafi, the donee does not own the item until he takes possession after separation. According to the others, ownership transfers immediately upon the contract.
This affects the donee's right to sell or dispose of the item before separation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائده .... صورت مذکورہ میں اگر موہوب لہ نے مشاع ہی پر قبضہ کر لیا اور شئی اس کے پاس بلاک ہو گئی تو ضامن ہوگا یا نہیں ؟ ابن رستم نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ موہوب لہ ضامن ہوگا اور قبضہ مفید ملک نہ ہو گا۔ امام طحاوی نے اس کو اختیار کیا ہے اور عصام نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ قبضہ مفید ملک ہوگا اور موہوب کہ ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ بعض مشائخ نے اس کو لیا ہے۔ کذافی فتاوی قاضی خان (بنایه، کنایه ) قولـه ولـو وهـب دقيق.. الخ اگر کسی نے وہ آنا جو گیہوں میں ہے یا تیل جو تلوں میں ہے یا مکھن جو دودھ میں ہے یہ کیا تو یہ بہ فاسد ہے۔ اب اگر وہ گہیوں پیس کر آنا یا تلوں کو پیس کر تیل اس کے حوالہ کر دے۔ تب بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بوقت ہیں آتا، تیل مکھن موجود نہیں معدوم ہے (یہاں تک کہ اگر کوئی شخص گہیوں، تیل، دودھ غصب کر کے آنا، تیل مکھن نکال لے تو مغصوب کا ضامن ہوکر ان چیزوں کا مالک ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ غصب کے وقت یہ چیزیں موجود نہیں تھیں تو ان پر فعل غصب واقع نہیں ہوا)۔ اور معدوم شئی محل ملک نہیں ہوتی تو عقد باطل واقع ہوالہذ ا آٹا ہو جانے پر دوبارہ ہبہ کرنا چاہئے۔ تجدید کے بغیر مبہ منعقد نہ ہوگا۔ بخلاف زمین وغیرہ کے ایک ٹکڑے کے یعنی ہبہ غیر مقسوم کے کہ وہ منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ مگر ملکیت نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ جو چیز مشاع موجود ہے وہ تملیک ہے تو اس میں ہوارہ کی ضرورت ہے۔ رہا یہ اشکال کہ آٹا وغیرہ گو با فعل موجود نہیں مگر بالقوہ تو موجود ہے۔ سواس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں۔ ورنہ ظاہر ہے کہ عام ممکنات کا یہی حال ہے حالانکہ ان کو موجود نہیں کہتے۔ قوله وهبة اللبن الخ تھنوں میں دودھ کا، پشتِ غنم پر اون کا۔ زمین میں لگی ہوئی کھیتی یا درخت کا۔ درخت خرما میں لگی ہوئی کھجور کا مہبہ کرتا بمنزلہ بہ مشاع کے ہے۔ یعنی اصل میں تو منعقد ہو گا گر جواز کا حکم نہ ہوگا (و عند الثلاثه يجوز ) کیونکہ ان چیزوں میں جواز کا امتناع ملک واہب کے ساتھ اتصال کی وجہ سے ہے ( اور اتصال مانع قبضہ ہے جیسے مشاع میں ہوتا ہے) ان اشیاء کے معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے۔
Benefit: In the mentioned case, if the donee took possession of the undivided share and the thing became blocked in his possession, is he a guarantor or not? Ibn Rustam mentioned that the donee will be a guarantor and possession will not effect ownership. Imam Tahawi chose this, and 'Isam mentioned that possession will effect ownership and the donee will not be a guarantor. Some mashā'ikh adopted this. Also in Fatawa Qadi Khan (Bina'yah, Kinayah). His statement: 'And if he gave as gift flour...' etc. If someone gave the flour that is in wheat, or the oil that is in sesame, or the butter that is in milk, then this is invalid (fāsid). Now if he grinds the wheat and gives the flour, or grinds the sesame and gives the oil to him, even then it will not be permissible. Because at the time of grant, the flour, oil, butter were not present, they were nonexistent. (To the extent that if a person usurps wheat, oil, milk and extracts flour, oil, butter, he becomes the owner of those things by being liable for the usurped item. Because at the time of usurpation these things were not present, so the act of usurpation did not occur on them). And a nonexistent thing cannot be the subject of ownership, so the contract becomes void. After the flour comes into existence, one should give it again as a new gift. Without renewal, the gift will not be valid. Contrary to a piece of land, etc., i.e., the gift of an undivided share, because it is concluded, but ownership is not established because the undivided share exists, it is a transfer of ownership, so it requires possession. As for the objection that flour etc. although not actually existing, potentially exist. Its answer is that potential existence has no consideration. Otherwise, it is obvious that all possible things would be the same, yet they are not considered existent. His statement: And the gift of milk, etc.: milk in udders, wool on the back of sheep, crops in the ground or on trees, dates on palm trees giving as gift is like the gift of undivided property. That is, in principle it is concluded but the ruling of permissibility is not given (and according to the three Imams it is permissible). Because the impediment to permissibility in these things is due to their connection to the property of the donor (and connection prevents possession, as in undivided property), not due to their non-existence.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage covers two key rulings on the subject of gift (hiba). First, the gift of a nonexistent item is fasid (void). Examples include flour while still in the wheat, oil still in sesame, or butter still in milk. The ruling is based on the principle that the subject of a contract must exist at the time of the contract. The text also notes an exception: if someone usurps the wheat and then extracts flour, he becomes the owner of the flour because the usurpation did not fall on the flour (nonexistent), but he is liable for the wheat. Second, the gift of items that are existent but attached to the donor's property, such as milk in the udder, wool on the sheep, crops in the ground, or dates on trees, is treated like the gift of an undivided share (mushā'). That is, the contract is initially valid but requires separate possession to be complete. This is the Hanafi position. The three Imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) consider such gifts permissible directly, because they view the impediment as attachment to the donor's property which prevents possession, not non-existence. The Hanafi school maintains that these items are existent (in essence) but their attachment to the donor's property makes them like undivided property, so they are not immediately possessable without separation. This difference leads to practical consequences in when ownership transfers.

Key Terms
مشاع (mushā'): An undivided share in a common property; in the context of hiba, a gift of a share of joint property is valid but requires separate possession to transfer ownership.
متصل (muttasil): Attached or connected; property that is attached to the donor's ownership, such as milk in udder or wool on sheep.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the donee become the owner of gifted milk in the udder?
A) Immediately upon the contract
B) After the milk is extracted and the donee takes possession
C) Never, because the gift is invalid
D) After the donor dies

Key Takeaway
Gift of attached property is valid but requires possession after separation to complete ownership, unlike the three Imams who allow immediate ownership.

Hiba Without New Possession: The Trust Rule
Ruling that donee owns gift by contract alone if item is already in his trust possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between trust possession and guarantee possession, and apply the rule that existing trust possession suffices for a valid hiba.

Core Idea
A gift is valid without new possession if the item is already held as a trust.

In Hanafi fiqh, possession (qabd) is a condition for ownership transfer in gifts (hiba). However, a critical nuance is that if the donee already holds the item as a trust (e.g., as a deposit), the gift is perfected by the contract alone. This lesson unpacks this rule, contrasts it with sale (where guarantee possession is required), and explores its application to gifts to minors by fathers and guardians.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the opening line: if the item is in the donee's hand, he owns it by the gift without renewing possession. Note that possession is already fulfilled.
The ruling is a clear exception to the general requirement of new possession.
2
Contrast with sale
Compare the ruling: in sale, existing trust possession does not substitute because sale possession is guarantee (madhmun), requiring a new act of guarantee possession.
The distinction hinges on the nature of possession: trust vs. guarantee.
3
Analyze the father-minor scenario
The father's possession on behalf of his minor son suffices because the father takes possession for the son, and the item is already in the father's hand or his depositee's hand.
This extends the rule to guardians who have custody.
4
Understand the principle of substitution
The commentary introduces a general principle: same-genus possessions substitute; higher (guarantee) substitutes for lower (trust), but not vice versa.
This explains why trust possession works for hiba but not for sale.
5
Identify exceptions
The gift does not transfer if the item is in another's possession (e.g., mortgaged, usurped, or sold fasid) because it is not in the father's control or ownership.
The rule applies only when the possessor is authorized to take possession on behalf of the donee.

He said: And if the item itself is in the hand of the donee, he owns it by the gift even if he does not renew possession in it, because the item is in his possession and possession is the condition. Contrary to if he sold it to him, because possession in sale is guarantee (madhmun), so trust possession does not substitute for it. As for possession of gift, it is not guarantee, so it substitutes for it. And if the father gives a gift to his minor son, the son owns it by the contract, because he is in the possession of the father regarding the possession of the gift. And there is no difference between when it is in his hand or in the hand of his depositee (mūda'), because his hand is like his hand. Contrary to when it is mortgaged, or usurped, or sold in a fasid sale, because it is in the hand of another or in the property of another. And charity in this is like the gift. Similarly, when his mother gives him a gift while he is in her care, and the father is dead and he has no executor, and likewise everyone who takes care of him. Translation: When the item itself is in the possession of the donee, he becomes the owner by the gift itself even if he does not renew possession, because the gifted item is in his possession and possession is the condition. Contrary to when the owner sells it to him, because the possession of sale is guarantee, so trust possession does not substitute; and the possession of gift is not guarantee, so it substitutes. And there is no difference in whether it is in the father's possession, because the depositee's possession is like the father's possession. Contrary to when it is mortgaged or usurped or sold in a fasid sale, because it is in the possession of someone other than the father or in another's property. And charity in all these cases is like gift. Similarly, when the mother gives something to the minor while he is in her care and the father is dead and he has no executor. Likewise, everyone who takes care of him... Commentary on his statement: 'And if the item...' The rule for these issues is that when two possessions are of the same genus, each substitutes for the other; and when the two possessions are different, the higher substitutes for the lower; the lower does not substitute for the higher. Understand this with an example: Zayd took possession of an item through a fasid contract. Then the owner sold it to him, so no new possession is needed because this possession is higher, so it substitutes for the gift possession. And if the item was previously in his possession as a deposit or loan, then the owner sold it to him, in this case new possession is needed because both possessions are trust possessions, and if the owner sells it to him, new possession is needed; without it the donee does not become owner. Because the possession of sale is guarantee which is higher, so the trust possession which is lower cannot substitute for it. His statement: 'And if the father gave a gift to his minor son...' If the father gave a gift to his minor son, the son becomes owner by the contract itself, because the father takes possession on behalf of the son and the item is in the father's possession. So this existence of possession serves as the possession which substitutes. Then making witnesses for this possession is not a condition. However, caution lies in making witnesses so that after the father's death or the child's maturity, the heirs cannot deny it, and if they deny, it can be established by witnesses. His statement: 'And there is no difference between what...' Whether the item given by the father is in the father's own hand or the father placed it with someone, there is no difference because the depositee's possession is like the owner's possession. Question: If the owner gives the deposited property as a gift to the depositee, according to you this is permissible. So if the depositee's possession is like the owner's possession, then in this case he did not take possession for himself. Answer: The depositee's possession being like the owner's possession is only as long as he acts for the owner in preserving the deposit, and before the transfer of ownership by gift. When the owner gave it to him as a gift, he became an actor for himself. His statement: 'Contrary to when it is mortgaged...' The item that the father gave to the minor, if the father had pawned it to someone, or someone usurped it, or the father sold it in a fasid sale and handed it to the buyer, then in these cases possession is not established by the gift contract alone, because the item is in the property of another. So the possession of the mortgagee and the usurper does not substitute for the possession of the gift for the son... Question: When the gifted item is in the depositee's possession, should the gift not be complete? Because in gift, complete possession is a condition, and the depositee's possession is legal (hukmi) which is deficient compared to actual possession. Answer: For completion of gift, legal possession is sufficient. Because gift becomes valid merely by vacating. Contrary to the gift of an undivided share, its possession will be in the context of the whole, and the implied is as if it were not. His statement: 'And likewise everyone who takes care of him...' Similarly, anyone who takes care of the child, like brother, paternal uncle, stranger, and he gives something to the child, the same ruling applies that it is permissible for him to take possession of the gifted item for the child. According to the three Imams, if guardians other than the father give a gift to the child, they need to appoint a representative who will accept and take possession on his behalf. But Ibn Qudamah said in al-Mughni that in this matter, the father and others are equal. Then here 'everyone who takes care of him' is absolute, but in Idah and Mukhtasar al-Karkhi it is stated that their guardianship is only when the father, his executor, after the father the grandfather, the grandfather's executor, none are present.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents a critical ruling in the Hanafi law of gift (hiba): if the item being gifted is already in the possession of the donee (e.g., as a trust), the gift is valid and ownership transfers by the contract alone without needing a new act of possession. The reason is that the condition of possession is already fulfilled. The text contrasts this with sale, where possession in sale is a guarantee (madhmun) responsibility, so existing trust possession does not suffice. The passage then discusses the father's gift to his minor son: the father takes possession on behalf of the son, and since the item is already in the father's possession, no new possession is needed. This applies whether the item is in the father's own hand or in the hand of a depositee. However, if the item is mortgaged, usurped, or sold in a fasid sale (invalid transaction) to a third party, the gift does not transfer ownership because the item is in another's possession or ownership. The passage also clarifies that for a mother or any guardian caring for the minor, the same rule applies: they can take possession on behalf of the minor without formalities. The commentary introduces a general principle: when two possessions are of the same genus (both trust), each can substitute; when different, the higher (guarantee) can substitute for the lower (trust), but not vice versa. This governs when a new possession is required. The passage also addresses a question: if a depositee is given a gift of the deposited item, does his existing possession suffice? Yes, because his possession was acting for the owner, but upon gift, he acts for himself. Finally, the text notes that according to the three Imams, only the father or his executor can take possession for a minor; other guardians need a representative. The Hanafi school, however, allows anyone caring for the child to do so, as stated in the Hidayah.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Possession; in hiba, it is a condition for completion of ownership, but if the donee already has the item in his possession (as trust), no new possession is needed.
مضمان (madmūn): Guarantee possession; in sale, possession makes the buyer liable for loss, so it must be a new act of taking possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A father gives his minor son a gift of a book that is in the father's own hand. Does the son need to take new possession of the book?
A) Yes, because the son must physically hold the book
B) No, because the father's possession on behalf of the son suffices
C) Only if the book is in another's hand
D) Only if witnesses are present

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a gift is perfected by contract alone if the donee already holds the item as a trust, because trust possession suffices for the condition of qabd.

Superior Possession Substitutes for Inferior in Hibah
Explains rule of possession substitution with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that superior possession substitutes for inferior possession in hibah and apply it to determine whether new possession is required.

Core Idea
Superior possession replaces inferior, but not vice versa.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of a gift (hibah) depends on the type of possession the donee already holds. This lesson introduces a key rule: the superior form of possession (e.g., from a sale) can replace the need for a new possession when the same item is gifted, but an inferior trust possession (e.g., deposit) cannot. Understanding this distinction prevents errors in completing hibah transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State that superior possession (قبض اعلی) can substitute for inferior (قبض ادنی), but inferior cannot substitute for superior.
2
Categorize possession types
Distinguish between guarantee possession (مضمون) which is superior, and trust possession (امانتی) which is inferior. Guarantee includes sale and defective sale; trust includes deposit and loan.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply to defective sale followed by sale
If a person took possession via a defective contract (superior), then the owner sells it to him, no new possession is needed because the existing superior possession suffices.
The defective contract gives a guarantee possession because the taker is liable for loss.
4
Apply to trust possession followed by sale
If the person held the item as a deposit or loan (trust/inferior) and the owner sells it without a new handover, the sale is incomplete because the inferior possession cannot replace the superior sale possession.
A new handover is required for the sale to be valid.
5
Apply to hibah
The same rule applies to gifts: if the donee already holds the item with a superior possession, the gift is valid without new possession. If the prior possession is inferior, the donor must hand it over anew.
This is the practical application of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جب دونوں قبضے متغیر ہوں تو اعلیٰ ادنی کا نائب ہو جاتا ہے۔ ادنی اعلیٰ کا نائب نہیں ہوتا۔ اس کو مثال سے یوں سمجھو کہ زید نے کوئی چیز بذریعہ عقد فاسد اپنے قبضہ میں کرلی۔ پھر مالک نے اس کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دی تو جدید قبضہ کی ضرورت نہیں کیونکہ یہ قبضہ اعلی ہے تو قبضہ فاسد کا نائب ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر وہ چیز ودیعت یا عاریت کے طور پر پہلے سے اس کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ پھر مالک اسی کو بیع کر دے جیسا کہ پیش نظر قول میں یہی صورت ہے تو اس میں جدید قبضہ کی ضرورت نہیں۔ کیونکہ دونوں قبضے امانتی ہیں۔ اور مالک اس کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دے تو جدید قبضہ کی ضرورت ہوگی اس کے بغیر موہوب لہ اس کا مالک نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بیع کا قبضہ مضمونتی ہے جو اعلی ہے تو اس کا نائب امانتی قبضہ نہیں ہو سکتا جو ادنی ہے۔
When the two possessions are different, the superior becomes a substitute for the inferior. The inferior does not become a substitute for the superior. Understand this by example: Zaid took possession of something through a defective contract. Then the owner sold it to him. No new possession is required because this possession is superior, so it becomes a substitute for the defective possession. And if the thing was previously in his possession as a deposit or loan, then the owner sells it to him—as is the case in the quoted statement—then no new possession is required because both possessions are trust possessions. But if the owner sells it to him with a new handover, then new possession is required; otherwise the donee will not own it. Because the possession of sale is a guarantee possession which is superior, so the trust possession which is inferior cannot be a substitute for it.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage establishes a key rule in Hanafi fiqh regarding possession (qabd) in contracts, specifically hibah. It distinguishes between two types of possession: superior (اعلی) and inferior (ادنی). A superior possession can substitute for an inferior one, but not vice versa. The example given: if a person already holds an item through a defective (fāsid) contract (which gives a guarantee possession), and then the owner sells it to him, no new physical possession is needed because the existing guarantee possession (superior) suffices. However, if the prior possession was trust-based (amānī) like a deposit or loan, and the owner sells it without a new handover, the sale is invalid because the trust possession (inferior) cannot substitute for the guarantee possession (superior) of sale. This principle applies to hibah as well, where the type of possession determines the validity of the gift.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Possession or taking physical control of an item.
اعلی (a'la): Superior type of possession that entails liability for loss.
ادنی (adna): Inferior type of possession without liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if Zaid took possession through a defective contract and then the owner sells it to him, what is required for the sale to be valid?
A) New physical possession is required because the first possession was defective.
B) No new possession is required because the defective contract possession is superior and substitutes.
C) The sale is invalid because a defective contract cannot lead to a valid sale.
D) Witnesses are required for the sale to be valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi hibah, a prior superior possession (like from a defective sale) eliminates the need for new possession, but a prior inferior trust possession does not.

Father's Hibah to Minor Son: Possession and Witnesses
Ruling on father's hibah to minor with conditions for constructive possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on father's hibah to a minor son and identify when constructive possession suffices versus when new possession is required.

Core Idea
A father's gift to his minor son is complete by contract alone because the father's existing possession substitutes for the gift's possession.

This passage clarifies a unique Hanafi concession: when a father gives a gift (hibah) to his minor son, no physical transfer of the item is necessary. The father's existing possession, whether with himself or a depositee, counts as the son's possession due to the father's guardianship (wilayah). However, this rule has limits: if the item is held by someone with a competing ownership right (mortgagee, usurper, buyer in a defective sale), the gift is not complete by contract alone. Witnesses are not required but recommended to prevent future disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling and Its Basis
Locate the sentence: 'the son becomes its owner by the contract alone.' Understand that the father's wilayah over the minor allows his constructive possession to suffice.
2
Understand Constructive Possession
The father's existing possession (qabda hukmi) replaces the need for a new physical possession. This applies whether the item is with the father or with a depositee (mudi').
3
Distinguish Between Valid and Invalid Situations
Contrast the cases where constructive possession works (own possession, depositee) with those where it does NOT (mortgage, usurpation, defective sale). The key difference is whether the item is in another's ownership.
The possession of a mortgagee or usurper does NOT substitute for the father's possession.
4
Analyze the Depositee Scenario
Note the subtle point: if the father gifts the deposited item to the depositee himself, the depositee's possession becomes his own, so no new possession is needed. The rule that 'depositee's possession is like depositor's' applies only before the gift.
5
Evaluate the Need for Witnesses
Witnesses are not a condition for validity but are recommended (mustahabb) for evidentiary purposes, especially to protect against denial by heirs.
This is a prudential recommendation, not a legal requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله واذا وهب الاب الخ اگر باپ نے اپنے پسر صغیر کو کوئی چیز ہبہ کی تو پسر عقد بید ہی سے اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ صغیر کا باپ صغیر کی جانب سے قبضہ کرے گا اور وہ چیز باپ کے قبضہ میں موجود ہے۔ تو یہ موجود و قبضہ ہی قبضہ جس کا نائب ہو جائے گا۔ پھر اس قبضہ میں کسی کو گواہ بنانا شرط نہیں ہے۔ البتہ احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ گواہ کر لے۔ تا کہ باپ کے مرنے یا بچہ کے بالغ ہونے کے بعد ورثہ اس کا انکار نہ کر سکیں اور وہ انکار کریں تو گواہوں سے اس کا اثبات ہو سکے۔ قوله ولا فرق بین ما الخ باپ کی ہی کی ہوئی چیز خود اپنے پاس ہو یا باپ نے کسی کے پاس رکھوائی ہو اس میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مودع کا قبضہ مودع کے مثل ہے۔ سوال اگر مالک نے مودع کو مال ودیعت ہبہ کر دیا تو یہ بقول شما جائز ہے۔ پس اگر مودع کا قبضہ قبضہ مودع کے مانند ہو تو اس صورت میں وہ اپنے لئے قبضہ کنندہ نہ ہوا۔ جواب مودع کے قبضہ کا قبضہ مودع کے مانند ہونا اسوقت تک ہے جب تک وہ حفظ ودیعت میں مودع کے لئے عامل ہے اور تملیک بالہبہ سے پہلے ہے اور جب مودع نے اس کو ہبہ کر دیا۔ تو وہ اپنے لئے عامل ہو گیا۔ قـولـه بخلاف ما اذا كان مرهونا .. الخ باپ نے جو چیز پر صغیر کو ہبہ کی ہے۔ اگر وہ باپ نے کسی کے پاس رہن رکھی ہو یا اس کو کسی نے غصب کر لیا ہو یا باپ نے بطور بیع فاسد فروخت کر کے مشتری کو سپرد کر دی ہو تو ان صورتوں میں صرف عقد ہبہ سے قبضہ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ چیز (رہن و غصب کی صورت میں) دوسرے کی ملک میں ہے۔ فلا ينوب قبض المرتهن والغاصب عن قبض الهبة للولد.
His statement: 'And when the father gives...' If the father gives a hibah to his minor son, the son becomes its owner by the contract alone because the father will take possession on behalf of the son and the item is already in the father's possession. So this existing possession becomes a substitute for the hibah possession. Then, making witnesses for this possession is not a condition. However, caution dictates that he should make witnesses so that after the father's death or the child's maturity, the heirs cannot deny it, and if they do, it can be proven by witnesses. His statement: 'And there is no difference between...' There is no difference whether the father's own property is with him or deposited with someone else, because the depositee's possession is like the depositor's possession. Question: If the owner gave the deposited item as a hibah to the depositee, then according to your statement it is permissible. So if the depositee's possession is like the depositor's possession, then in that case he did not take possession for himself. Answer: The depositee's possession being like the depositor's possession applies as long as he is acting for the depositor in preserving the deposit and before the transfer of ownership by hibah. When the depositor gives it as hibah, then he becomes acting for himself. His statement: 'Contrary to when it is mortgaged...' If the father has given hibah of an item to the minor son, but the father had mortgaged it to someone, or someone had usurped it, or the father had sold it through a defective contract and given it to the buyer, then in these cases possession is not achieved by the hibah contract alone. Because the item (in case of mortgage or usurpation) is in the ownership of another. So the possession of the mortgagee or usurper does not substitute for the possession of the hibah for the child.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage covers multiple sub-rulings on father's hibah to minor son. First, if the father gives a gift to his minor son, the son becomes owner immediately because the father already has possession of the item (whether with himself or with a depositee). No new physical possession or witnesses are required, though witnesses are recommended to avoid future disputes. Second, if the item is deposited with someone (mudi'), the depositee's possession is considered like the father's possession. However, if the father then gives that same item as a hibah to the depositee himself, the depositee's possession now becomes his own, so no new possession is needed. Third, if the item is mortgaged (rahn), usurped (ghasb), or sold via a defective contract (bay' fāsid), then the father's hibah to the son is not complete by contract alone because the item is in the ownership of another (mortgagee, usurper, buyer). The possession of those parties does not substitute for the hibah possession for the son.

Key Terms
قبضہ (qabza): Taking possession; in this context, it can be constructive (existing possession suffices).
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship; father has wilayah over minor's property.
مودع (mudi'): Depositee, the person with whom property is deposited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The friend must physically hand the item to the son.
B) The father must take it back and then give it to the son.
C) No new possession needed; the deposit possession suffices.
D) The son must take it himself if he is discerning.

Key Takeaway
Father's hibah to minor son is valid upon contract alone due to constructive possession, except when the item is in another's ownership (mortgage, usurpation, defective sale).

Possession of Hibah for Minors by Various Guardians
Rulings on who may take possession for a minor from a stranger's hibah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the various guardians who may take possession of hibah for a minor and apply the conditions that limit their authority.

Core Idea
A minor's hibah requires valid possession; the father is primary but many others can act under specific conditions.

When a stranger gifts something to a minor, the gift is not complete until possession (qabḍ) is taken by a qualified person. This passage from al-Hidayah details who may take possession: the father, guardians of orphans, mothers, custodians, the discerning minor himself, and the husband of a minor wife. Each has limits. This lesson parses these categories to help you apply them correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default guardian
The father is the primary guardian; he can take possession because he has general authority over the minor's harmful and beneficial matters.
Father acts by inherent wilayah.
2
List guardians for an orphan
For an orphan, the executor (wasī), grandfather (jadd), and executor of the grandfather can take possession as they stand in the father's place.
They must be explicitly appointed.
3
Analyze the mother's capacity
The mother can take possession when the child is in her custody, but only after the father's death or disconnected absence (ghaybah munqati'ah).
Her authority is based on necessity.
4
Examine the stranger custodian
A stranger raising the child (ajnabī yurabbīhi) has a recognized hand (yad mu'tabarah) and may take possession of purely beneficial items.
This is due to effective custody.
5
Consider the minor's own capacity and the husband's special role
The discerning minor (ʿāqil) can accept the hibah himself. The husband can take possession for his wife after the wedding (zifāf), even in the father's presence.
Husband acts by implicit delegation; minor acts by his own legal capacity for beneficial matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ وَهَبَ لَهُ أَجْنَبِيٌّ هِبَةٌ تَمَّتْ بِقَبْضِ الْآبِ لِأَنَّهُ يَمْلِكُ عَلَيْهِ الضَّائِرَ وَالنَّافِعَ فَأَوْلَى أَنْ يَمْلِكَ النَّافِعَ وَإِنْ وُهِبَ لِلْيَتِيمِ هِبَةٌ فَقَبَضَها لَهُ وَلِيُّهُ وَهُوَ وَصِيُّ الْآبِ أَوْ جَدُّ الْيَتِيمِ أَوْ وَصِيُّ الْجَدِّ جَازَ لِأَنَّ لِهَؤُلَاءِ وَلَايَةً عَلَيْهِ لِقِيَامِهِمْ مَقَامَ الْآبِ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي حِجْرِ أُمِّهِ فَقَبضُهَا لَهُ جَائِرٌ لِأَنَّ لَهَا الْوِلَايَةَ فِيمَا يَرْجِعُ إِلَى حِفْظِهِ وَحِفْظِ مَالِهِ وَهَذَا مِنْ بَابِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَبْقَى إِلَّا بِالْمَالِ فَلَابُدَّ مِنْ وِلَايَةِ تَحْصِيلِ النَّافِعِ وَكَذَا إِذَا كَانَ فِي حِجْرٍ أَجْنَبِيٍّ يُرَبِّيْهِ لِأَنَّ لَهُ عَلَيْهِ يَدًا مُعْتَبَرَةً أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّهُ لَا يَتَمَكَّنُ أَجْنَبِيٌّ آخَرُ أَنْ يَنْزَعَهُ مِنْ يَدِهِ فَيَمْلِكُ مَا يَتَمَحْضُ نَفْعًا فِي حَقِهِ وَإِنْ قَبَضَ الصَّبِيُّ الْهِبَةَ بِنَفْسِهِ جَازَ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا كَانَ عَاقِلًا لِأَنَّهُ نَافِعٌ فِي حَقِهِ وَهُوَ مِنْ أَهْلِهِ وَفِيمَا وُهِبَ لِلصَّغِيرَةِ يَجُوزُ قَبضُ زَوْجِهَا لَهَا بَعْدَ الزِّفَافِ لِتَفْوِيضِ الْآبِ أُمُورَهَا إِلَيْهِ دِلَالَةً بِخِلَافِ مَا قَبْلَ الزِّفَافِ وَيَمْلِكُهُ مَعَ حَضْرَةِ الْآبِ بِخِلَافِ الْأُمِّ وَكُلَّ مَنْ يَعُولُهَا غَيْرُهَا حَيْثُ لَا يَمْلِكُونَهَا إِلَّا بَعْدَ مَوْتِ الْآبِ أَوْ غِيْبَتِهِ غَيْبَةً مُنْقَطِعَةً فِي الصَّحِيحِ لِأَنَّ تَصَرُّفَ هَؤُلَاءِ لِلضَّرُورَةِ لَا بِتَفْوِيضِ الْآبِ وَمَعَ حُضُورِهِ لَا ضَرُورَةَ.
And if a stranger gives a hibah to him (the minor), it is completed by the father's possession because he (the father) has authority over him regarding harmful and beneficial matters, so it is more appropriate that he have authority over the beneficial. And if a hibah is given to an orphan and his guardian takes possession of it for him—and he is the executor of the father, or the grandfather of the orphan, or the executor of the grandfather—it is valid because these people have wilayah over him due to standing in the place of the father. And if he is in the custody of his mother, her taking possession for him is valid because she has authority in matters related to his preservation and the preservation of his property, and this is from that category because he cannot survive except with wealth, so there must be authority to obtain beneficial things. Similarly, if he is in the custody of a stranger who is raising him, because that stranger has a recognized hand over him—do you not see that another stranger cannot take him from his hand? So he owns whatever is purely beneficial in his right. And if the minor takes possession of the hibah himself, it is valid, meaning if he is discerning, because it is beneficial in his right and he is capable of it. As for what is given to a minor girl, her husband's taking possession for her after the wedding is valid because the father has implicitly delegated her affairs to him, contrary to before the wedding. And he (the husband) owns it even in the presence of the father, unlike the mother. And everyone who supports her besides him (the father) does not own it except after the death of the father or his disappearance in a disconnected absence, according to the correct opinion, because their actions are out of necessity, not by the father's delegation, and in his presence there is no necessity.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage expands the rules of possession for hibah to minors. When a stranger gives a gift to a minor, the father's possession completes it because the father has general authority over the minor's affairs. For an orphan, the executor, grandfather, or the grandfather's executor can take possession. If the orphan is with his mother, her possession is valid because she is responsible for his care and property. Even a stranger who is raising the child can take possession because he has effective custody (recognized hand). The minor himself can accept if he is discerning (āqil). For a minor girl, her husband can take possession after marriage (after zafāf) because the father has delegated her affairs to him by implication. The husband can take possession even when the father is alive, unlike the mother and other supporters who can only take possession after the father's death or his disconnected absence (ghaybah munqati'ah). This distinction is because the mother and others act out of necessity, but when the father is present, there is no necessity.

Key Terms
ولایت (wilayah): Authority or guardianship over a minor, enabling one to take possession of hibah.
ید معتبرة (yad mu'tabarah): A recognized hand, meaning de facto custody recognized by law.
غیبة منقطعة (ghaybah munqati'ah): Disconnected absence, where the father's whereabouts are unknown and communication impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A stranger gifts a cow to a minor girl who lives with her mother (father alive). Who can validly take possession for the girl?
A) Only the father.
B) The mother, because she has custody.
C) The father, or after his death/absence the mother.
D) The girl herself if she is discerning, but not the mother.

Key Takeaway
The authority to take possession of a minor's hibah extends beyond the father to include many guardians under specific conditions, ensuring the minor's benefit and necessity.

Possession of a Gift for a Minor: Who May Take Qabd?
Rulings on who may take possession of a gift for a minor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which possession (qabd) of a gift for a minor is valid, and identify which persons may take possession on his behalf.

Core Idea
A gift for a minor is perfected only by possession; Hanafi law permits possession by guardians, foster parents, and the minor himself if discerning.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a fundamental question in gift (hiba) law: who can take possession when the recipient is a minor? Since a minor cannot manage his own affairs, the law designates certain persons with guardianship (wilayah) to take possession on his behalf. The ruling explores several categories: the father, grandfather, executor, mother, foster parent, and even the minor himself under istihsan. It also addresses the special case of a husband receiving a gift for his minor wife. Understanding these rules is essential for ensuring that gifts to minors are legally valid and irrevocable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is taking possession (qabd) of a gift (hiba) for a minor. The ruling is that possession is required for the gift to be perfected (tammat). Various persons may validly take possession.
The possession must be actual or constructive, and it completes the gift, making it binding.
2
Classify the persons who can take possession
List the persons: father, grandfather, executor of father/grandfather, mother, foster parent (ajnabi yurabbihi), the minor himself (if discerning), and husband of a minor wife (after zifaf).
Each has a different basis of authority.
3
Trace the basis of each person's authority
Father has wilayah over harm/benefit; grandfather and executors stand in place of father; mother has wilayah al-hifz (guardianship of protection); foster parent has a recognized hand (yad mu'tabarah); minor's own possession is by istihsan; husband has implicit delegation after wedding.
The authority may be general (wilayah 'ammah) or specific to benefit.
4
Note the conditions and limitations
The minor must be discerning (aqil) for his own possession. Husband's possession only after zifaf and even in father's presence. Mother and foster parent can only take possession after father's death or prolonged absence (ghayba munqati'a).
These limitations prevent conflict with the father's primary authority.
5
Consider the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam Shafi'i does not permit the minor's own possession even if intelligent, based on qiyas. The Hanafi response is istihsan, favoring benefit.
This is a clear example of istihsan overriding qiyas in Hanafi jurisprudence.

قوله وان قبض الخ اگر بچہ کو کوئی چیز ہبہ کی گئی اور اسپر خود بچہ نے قبضہ کر لیا تویہ ہمارے نزدیک استحسانا جائز ہے بشرطیکہ بچہ سمجھ دار ہو ) امام احمد سے بھی ایک روایت یہی ہے۔ دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ اگرولی کی اجازت سے قبضہ کیا تو جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ امام شافعی کے یہاں بچہ کاقبضہ کرنا جائز نہیں۔ اگر چہ وہ عاقل ہو ۔ مقتضائے قیاس بھی یہی ہے کیونکہ بلوغ سے پہلے بچے کا کوئی فعل معتبر نہیں ہے بالخصوص ایسے امر میں جس کی تحصیل غیر کے ذریعہ سے ممکن ہو اس لئے کہ بچہ کی عقل کا اعتبار بوجہ ضرورت ہے اور ضرورت انہیں امور میں ہے جو غیر سے حاصل نہ ہوں۔ اسی لئے امام شافعی نے بچہ کے اسلام کی صحت میں اس کی عقل کا اعتبار نہیں کیا۔ ہاں اس کی وصیت میں اور احد الا بوین کے اختیار کرنے میں اس کا اعتبار کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی تحصیل غیر کے ذریعہ سے ناممکن ہے۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ مہبہ پر قبضہ کر ن اس کے حق میں نفع محض ہے اور اس کو قبضہ کی لیاقت حاصل ہے۔
قوله وفيما وهب للصغير.. الخ اگر کسی کی زوجہ صغیرہ یعنی نابالغہ کو کچھ ہبہ کیا گیا اور اس کے شوہر نے قبضہ کیا۔ پس اگر وہ صغیرہ شوہر کے گھر بھیج دی گئی ہوتو شو ہر کا قبضہ کرنا جائز ہے اس لئے کہ صغیرہ کا متولی اگر چہ اس کا باپ ہے لیکن باپ کا صغیرہ کو شوہر کے پاس رخصت کر دینا اس امر کی دلیل ہے کہ اس نے صغیرہ کے امور کو اس کے شوہر کے سپرد کر دیا۔ اور اگر شوہر کے یہاں نہیں بھیجی گئی تو شوہر کا قبضہ کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ دلیل مذکور نہیں پائی گئی۔ پھر صاحب ہدایہ نے زفاف کو ذکر کیا ہے اور ایضاح میں دخول مذکور ہے اور ذخیرہ میں صغیرہ کے قابل جماع ہونے کی شرط ہے۔ لیکن صحیح وہی ہے جو صاحب ہدایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے۔
And if a stranger makes a gift to him (the minor), it is perfected by the father's possession because he (the father) has authority over him regarding matters that oscillate between benefit and harm, so it is more appropriate that he should have authority over pure benefit. And if a gift is made to an orphan and his guardian takes possession of it for him – and he is the father's executor, or the orphan's grandfather, or the executor of the grandfather – it is permitted, because these persons have guardianship over him due to their standing in the place of the father. And if he (the minor) is in the care of his mother, her possession for him is permitted, because she has guardianship in matters that pertain to his protection and the protection of his property, and this is of that category, because he does not survive except with property, so guardianship for obtaining benefit is necessary. Likewise, if he is in the care of a stranger who is raising him, because he has a recognized hand over him; do you not see that no other stranger can snatch him from his hand? So he has ownership over that which is pure benefit for him. And if the minor himself takes possession of the gift, it is permitted – meaning when he is intelligent, because it is beneficial for him and he is qualified for it. And regarding what is gifted to a small girl (minor wife), the possession of her husband for her is permitted after the wedding procession (zifaf), due to the father's delegation of her affairs to him by implication, unlike before the wedding. And he (the husband) owns it even in the presence of the father, unlike the mother and everyone who supports her other than him, for they do not own it except after the father's death or his being absent in a severed absence, according to the sound view, because the actions of these are out of necessity, not by delegation of the father, and in his presence there is no necessity.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof from the Hidayah on who may take possession of a gift (hiba) on behalf of a minor (saghir). The author discusses several categories: The father can take possession because he has guardianship over the minor's affairs that involve both benefit and harm, so he certainly has authority over pure benefit. For an orphan, the guardian (executor of father, grandfather, or executor of grandfather) can take possession as they stand in the father's place. If the minor is under his mother's care, she may take possession because she has guardianship over his protection and property. Similarly, a stranger who is raising the minor (a foster parent) may take possession because he has a recognized hand (yad mu'tabarah) over the minor, evident by the fact that no other stranger can remove the minor from his custody. The minor himself, if discerning (aqil), may take possession; this is by istihsan, contrary to qiyas which would invalidate it because a minor's actions are not legally effective. The minority view (Shafi'i) disallows it even if intelligent. The husband of a minor wife may take possession for her after the wedding is consummated (zifaf), because by sending her to him, the father implicitly delegates authority. Before zifaf, the husband cannot take possession. The husband's ability to take possession exists even when the father is alive, unlike the mother or other supporters who can only do so after the father's death or his long absence, because their action is based on necessity, not delegation.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Taking physical or constructive possession of the gifted item, which is a condition for the completion (tamam) of the gift (hiba) in Hanafi law.
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority or guardianship over a minor, including the power to take possession of property on his behalf.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas (analogy) in favor of a more equitable ruling, used here to validate the minor's own possession despite general incapacity.
زفاف (zifaf): The wedding procession or consummation, after which the husband gains authority to take possession of gifts for his minor wife.
غیبت منقطعہ (ghayba munqati'a): A severed absence where the father's whereabouts are unknown and there is no possibility of communication, rendering his authority effectively nonexistent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, whose possession of a gift for a minor is valid only after the father's death or his severed absence?
A) The mother and the foster parent
B) The husband of a minor wife
C) The grandfather's executor
D) The minor himself

Key Takeaway
Possession of a gift for a minor is valid only when taken by someone with proper legal authority; a discerning minor may take possession himself by istihsan, but the mother and foster parent require the father's absence or death.

Hiba to Multiple Donees: Shuyu' and the Scholar's Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hiba to multiple donees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two disciples on the validity of giving a single property to two donees, and apply the distinction between hiba and rahn to explain the difference.

Core Idea
Giving a whole to two donees creates shuyu' — but the disciples see it as a single valid transfer.

When two people own a house together and give it to one person, the gift is valid because delivery is whole. But when one person gives his house to two people, a key difference arises: Abu Hanifa says it's invalid due to shuyu', while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it's valid. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each view and the critical distinction between gift and pawn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed scenario
Start with the undisputed case: two donors giving one property to one donee is valid. Understand why shuyu' does not arise.
The whole is delivered and received as a whole.
2
State the disputed scenario
Now consider one donor giving one property to two donees. Abu Hanifa rules it invalid (fasid); the disciples rule it valid (sahih).
This is the core of the lesson.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the gift effectively gives half to each donee, creating shuyu'. Shuyu' prevents completion because possession (qabd) of an undivided share is not feasible.
He uses the principle that shuyu' in a divisible item invalidates hiba.
4
Analyze the disciples' proof
The disciples see the transfer as one act (tamlik wahid), so the whole is given jointly. They draw an analogy to pawning (rahn) a house to two people, which is valid.
Their analogy: in rahn, detention (habs) is the effect, and it is complete for each; in hiba, ownership transfer could also be seen as complete jointly.
5
Examine the rebuttal and distinctions
Abu Hanifa replies that pawn is different: its effect is habs, which does not require division, whereas hiba transfers ownership, which does. Also, the text discusses sadaqah to the needy vs. rich, and the proxy argument.
These distinctions determine the practical ruling.
6
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, such a gift is invalid and must be redone; according to the disciples, it is valid and the donees become co-owners.
The mufta bihi tends toward validity for needy donees or by considering proxy, but for rich donees, invalidity is the sounder view.

دو آدمیوں نے اپنا مشترک مکان کسی کو ہبہ کیا تو جائز ہے اگر ایک آدمی دو کو کرے تو ہبہ جائز ہے یا نہیں؟ اقوال فقہاء
قَالَ وَإِذَا وَهَبَ إِثْنَانِ مِنْ وَاحِدٍ دَارًا جَازَ لِأَنَّهُمَا سَلَّمَاهَا جُمْلَةً وَهُوَ قَدْ قَبَضَهَا جُمْلَةٌ فَلَا شُيُوعَ وَإِنَ وَهَبَهَا وَاحِدٌ مِنَ اثْنَيْنِ لَا يَجُوزُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ وَقَالَا يَصِحُ لِاَنَّ هَذِهِ هِبَةَ الْجُمْلَةِ مِنْهُمَا إِذِ التَّمْلِيكُ وَاحِدٌ فَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ السُّيُوعُ كَمَا إِذَا رَهَنَ مِنْ رَجُلَيْنِ دَارًا وَلَهُ أَنَّ هَذِهِ هِبَةَ النِصْفِ مِنْ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا وَلِهَذَا لَوْ كَانَتِ الْهِبَةُ فِيْمَا لَا يُقْسَمُ فَقَبِلَ اَحَدُهِمَا صَحَ وَلاَنَّ الْمِلْكَ يَثَبِّتُ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا فِي النِّصْفِ فَيَكُونُ السَّمْلِكُ كَذَالِكَ لأَنَّهُ حُكْمُهُ وَعَلى هَذَا الْاِعْتِبَارِ يَتَحَقَّقُ الشُّيُوعُ بِخِلَافِ الرَّهْنِ لِاَنَّ حُكْمَهُ الْحَبْسُ وَيَثْتُ لِكُلّ مِنْهُمَا كَمَلًا فَلَا شُيُوعَ وَلِهَذَا لَوْ قَضَى دَيْنَ أَحَدِهِمَا لَا يَسْتَرِدُّ شَيْئًا مِنَ الرَّهْنِ وَفِي الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ إِذَا تَصَدَّقَ عَلَى مُحْتَاجَيْنِ بِعَشَرَةِ دَرَاهِمَ اَوْ وَهَبَهَا لَهُمَا جَازَ وَلَوْ تَصَدَّقَ بِهَا عَلَى غَنِيَّيْنِ أَوْ وَهَبَهَا لَهُمَا لَمْ يَجُزْ وَقَالَا يَجُوزُ لِلْغَنِيَّيْنِ أَيْضًا جَعَلَ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مَجَازًا عَنِ الْآخَرِ وَالصَّلَاحِيَّةُ ثَابِتَةٌ لِأَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا تَمْلِيكَ بِغَيْرِ بَدَلٍ وَفَرَّقَ بَيْنَ الْهِبَةِ وَالصَّدَقَةِ فِي الْحُكْمِ فِي الْجَامِعِ وَفِي الْأَصْلِ سَوَّى فَقَالَ وَكَذلِكَ الصَّدَقَةُ لَاَنَّ الشُّيُوعَ مَانِعٌ فِى الْفَصْلَيْنِ لِتَوَقُفِهِمَا عَلَى الْقَبْضَ وَوَجْهُ الْفَرْقِ عَلَى هَذِهِ الرِّوَايَةِ أَنَّ الصَّدَقَةَ يُرَادُ بِهَا وَجُهُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَهُوَ وَاحِدٌ وَالْهِبَةُ يُرَادُ بِهَا وَجْهُ الْغَنِيِّ وَهُمَا إِثْنَانِ وَقِيلَ هَذَا هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْمَذْكُورِ فِي الْأَصْلِ الصَّدَقَةُ عَلَى غَنِيَّيْنِ
Two men gave their shared house to one person as a gift – it is permissible, because they delivered it as a whole and he took possession of it as a whole, so there is no shuyu' (undivided share). And if one person gave it to two, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. But the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is valid, because this is a gift of the whole from him to them, since the transfer of ownership is one, so shuyu' does not materialize, just as if he pawned a house to two men. And his (Abu Hanifa's) argument: This is a gift of half from each of them, and therefore if the gift is of something indivisible and one of them accepts, it is valid. And because ownership is established for each of them in half, so the transfer of ownership is likewise, since it is its ruling. On this basis, shuyu' does materialize, unlike pawning, because its ruling is detention (habs) and it is established for each of them completely, so no shuyu'. For this reason, if he pays off one of their debts, he cannot reclaim anything from the pawn. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: If he gives charity to two needy persons with ten dirhams, or gifts it to them, it is permissible. But if he gives charity with it to two rich persons, or gifts it to them, it is not permissible. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is permissible for the rich as well, considering each of them as a proxy for the other, and the capacity is established because each of them is receiving ownership without compensation. And a distinction was made between hiba and sadaqah in the ruling in al-Jami', while in al-Asl (by Muhammad) they were treated equally, saying: And likewise sadaqah, because shuyu' is a preventive factor in both cases, since both depend on possession. And the basis of distinction according to this narration is that sadaqah is intended for the sake of Allah, which is one, while hiba is intended for the sake of the donee, and they are two. And it is said: This is the correct view, and what is mentioned in al-Asl refers to sadaqah to two rich persons.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. the two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the validity of giving a single property to two donees or by two donors. The issue is whether joint ownership (shuyu') in the gifted property prevents validity. When two people give a jointly owned house to one person, all agree it is valid because the delivery and possession are of the whole, so no shuyu' exists. When one person gives a single property to two recipients, Abu Hanifa rules it invalid because it effectively gives each half, creating shuyu' (undivided co-ownership) in a single item, and shuyu' in a divisible item prevents the gift from being complete. The two disciples argue it is valid because the transfer of ownership is a single act, and the donees receive the entire property jointly, similar to pawning (rahn), where a single item can be pawned to multiple creditors, and the pawn remains as a whole for each. Abu Hanifa distinguishes: in a pawn, the legal effect is detention (habs), not transfer of ownership, so each creditor has a complete right of detention without shuyu'. But in a gift, ownership is transferred, and each donee would own an undivided half, which constitutes shuyu'. The text then references al-Jami' al-Saghir, where giving charity (sadaqah) to two needy persons is valid, but to two rich persons is not, by Abu Hanifa's view. The disciples allow it even for the rich, considering each as proxy for the other. However, the author notes that some distinguish between hiba and sadaqah: sadaqah is for Allah, so the intention is one, while hiba is for the donees, so two intentions require separate gifts. The correct view according to the text is the one from al-Asl: sadaqah to two rich persons is also invalid due to shuyu'.

Key Terms
شیوع (shuyu'): Undivided co-ownership or joint ownership in a single item; considered a preventing factor (mani') for the validity of hiba because possession of an undivided share is not feasible.
ہبة الجملة (hibat al-jumlah): A gift of the whole (as a collective) to multiple donees; the disciples consider this valid because the transfer is one act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Abu Hanifa consider a gift of one house to two recipients invalid, while a pawn of one house to two creditors is valid?
A) Because a pawn involves a higher level of formality than a gift.
B) Because in a pawn, the effect is detention (habs), which is complete for each creditor, whereas in a gift, ownership creates undivided shares (shuyu').
C) Because the two disciples only differ on gift, not on pawn.
D) Because the gift cannot be delivered jointly, but a pawn can.

Key Takeaway
Shuyu' is a preventing factor in hiba, but its application differs depending on whether the transfer is considered one act or multiple, and on the status (need/rich) of the donees.

Minor's Acceptance of Gifts: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Expounds Hanafi positions on who may accept gifts on behalf of minors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits a discerning minor to accept a gift by istihsan, and contrast this with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A child's acceptance of a gift is valid by istihsan as pure benefit, setting aside qiyas.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can a minor child independently take possession of a gifted item? The Hanafi school, applying istihsan, allows it if the child is discerning, while the Shafi'i school maintains that a minor's actions are legally invalid. The text also examines the related issue of a husband accepting a gift on behalf of his minor wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage covers two distinct scenarios: (1) a child's own possession of a gift, and (2) a husband's possession for his minor wife. Recognize that each has its own ruling and conditions.
2
State the Hanafi position on child's possession
By istihsan, a child's taking possession is valid if the child is discerning (sa'ih dar). This is the mufta bihi position.
Contrast with the Shafi'i position that it is never valid.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof (istihsan vs qiyas)
The Shafi'i school relies on qiyas: since a minor's actions are generally invalid, accepting a gift should also be invalid. The Hanafi school counters by istihsan: the child has capacity for pure benefit, and necessity requires recognizing this capacity in matters that cannot be delegated.
Istihsan overrides qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) here.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a child's possession is invalid even if discerning. He applies qiyas strictly and does not accept istihsan as a source of law.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different usul methodologies.
5
Apply the second ruling: husband's acceptance
A husband may accept a gift on behalf of his minor wife only if she has been sent to his home (or consummation has occurred). The father's sending her indicates transfer of authority.
Al-Hidayah conditions this on zifaf (consummation), while others require intercourse or capability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وان قبض الخ اگر بچہ کو کوئی چیز ہبہ کی گئی اور اسپر خود بچہ نے قبضہ کر لیا تویہ ہمارے نزدیک استحسانا جائز ہے بشرطیکہ بچہ سمجھ دار ہو ) امام احمد سے بھی ایک روایت یہی ہے۔ دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ اگرولی کی اجازت سے قبضہ کیا تو جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ امام شافعی کے یہاں بچہ کاقبضہ کرنا جائز نہیں۔ اگر چہ وہ عاقل ہو ۔ مقتضائے قیاس بھی یہی ہے کیونکہ بلوغ سے پہلے بچے کا کوئی فعل معتبر نہیں ہے بالخصوص ایسے امر میں جس کی تحصیل غیر کے ذریعہ سے ممکن ہو اس لئے کہ بچہ کی عقل کا اعتبار بوجہ ضرورت ہے اور ضرورت انہیں امور میں ہے جو غیر سے حاصل نہ ہوں۔ اسی لئے امام شافعی نے بچہ کے اسلام کی صحت میں اس کی عقل کا اعتبار نہیں کیا۔ ہاں اس کی وصیت میں اور احد الا بوین کے اختیار کرنے میں اس کا اعتبار کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی تحصیل غیر کے ذریعہ سے ناممکن ہے۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ مہبہ پر قبضہ کر ن اس کے حق میں نفع محض ہے اور اس کو قبضہ کی لیاقت حاصل ہے۔ قوله وفيما وهب للصغير.. الخ اگر کسی کی زوجہ صغیرہ یعنی نابالغہ کو کچھ ہبہ کیا گیا اور اس کے شوہر نے قبضہ کیا۔ پس اگر وہ صغیرہ شوہر کے گھر بھیج دی گئی ہوتو شو ہر کا قبضہ کرنا جائز ہے اس لئے کہ صغیرہ کا متولی اگر چہ اس کا باپ ہے لیکن باپ کا صغیرہ کو شوہر کے پاس رخصت کر دینا اس امر کی دلیل ہے کہ اس نے صغیرہ کے امور کو اس کے شوہر کے سپرد کر دیا۔ اور اگر شوہر کے یہاں نہیں بھیجی گئی تو شوہر کا قبضہ کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ دلیل مذکور نہیں پائی گئی۔ پھر صاحب ہدایہ نے زفاف کو ذکر کیا ہے اور ایضاح میں دخول مذکور ہے اور ذخیرہ میں صغیرہ کے قابل جماع ہونے کی شرط ہے۔ لیکن صحیح وہی ہے جو صاحب ہدایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے۔
His statement: 'And if he took possession...' If a gift is given to a child and the child himself takes possession, this is permissible by istihsan in our school, provided the child is discerning. A narration from Imam Ahmad is the same. Another narration says it is permissible if done with the guardian's permission, otherwise not. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, a child's taking possession is not permissible, even if he is intelligent. Analogy (qiyas) also dictates this, because before puberty no act of a child is considered valid, especially in a matter that can be accomplished through another, because reliance on the child's intellect is due to necessity, and necessity exists only in matters that cannot be accomplished by others. For this reason, Imam al-Shafi'i did not consider the child's intellect valid for the validity of his Islam. Yes, he considered it in his will and in choosing one of the parents, because these cannot be accomplished through others. The basis of istihsan is that taking possession of the gifted item is pure benefit for him, and he possesses the capacity for possession. His statement: 'And regarding what is gifted to a minor...' If someone's minor wife (i.e., a minor girl) is given a gift and her husband takes possession, then if that minor wife has been sent to the husband's house, the husband's taking possession is permissible, because even though the guardian of the minor is her father, the father's sending his minor daughter to the husband is evidence that he has entrusted her affairs to her husband. And if she has not been sent to the husband's house, then the husband's taking possession is not permissible, because the mentioned evidence is not found. Then the author of al-Hidayah mentioned consummation (zifaf), and in al-Idah, intercourse (dukhul) is mentioned, and in al-Dhakhirah, the condition of the minor being capable of intercourse. But the correct view is what the author of al-Hidayah mentioned.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the Hidayah's rulings on gifts to minors. It first addresses whether a minor child can take possession of a gift themselves. The Hanafi school, by istihsan (juristic preference), allows it if the child is discerning (sa'ih dar), contrary to qiyas which would invalidate the child's action. The Shafi'i school does not allow it at all. The Hanafi justification is that the child has capacity for pure benefit, and necessity allows this exception. The second part discusses a husband taking possession of a gift given to his minor wife. If the wife has already been sent to the husband's home (implying the father has handed over authority), the husband may accept; otherwise, he may not. The text notes a difference among Hanafi authorities: al-Hidayah mentions consummation (zifaf), al-Idah mentions intercourse, and al-Dhakhirah adds the condition that the wife be capable of intercourse. The author sides with al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that sets aside strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling, used here to validate the child's possession due to necessity.
قبضہ (qabd): Taking physical possession of the gifted item, which is a condition for the validity of a gift (hibah).
صغیرہ (saghirah): A minor female who has not reached puberty; in this context, a wife who is still a minor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a husband's acceptance of a gift on behalf of his minor wife is valid only if:
A) The wife is discerning.
B) The wife has been sent to the husband's home.
C) The husband is the legal guardian.
D) The gift is in the form of money.

Key Takeaway
A discerning child can accept a gift by istihsan; a husband may accept for his minor wife only if she has been sent to his home.

Hibah of One Item to Two Persons: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hibah to two persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of a gift of one divisible item to two persons, and explain the proof and rebuttal using the analogy of rahn.

Core Idea
A single gift to two persons on a divisible item: Abu Hanifa invalidates due to shuyu'; the Sahibayn validate via unified tamlik.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about gifting one house to two individuals. Imam Abu Hanifa considers it invalid because each recipient gets an undivided half, creating forbidden shuyu'. The Sahibayn argue that the gift is a single contract of ownership transfer, so no shuyu' arises. You will trace the reasoning and understand why the mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
The act is a gift (hibah) of a house (divisible property) by one person to two recipients in a single contract. Abu Hanifa and Zufar say it is invalid (batil); the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is valid (sahih).
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
State Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the gift implicitly distributes half to each. Since the item is divisible, each recipient's share is undivided (shuyu'), which invalidates the hibah. If the item were indivisible or only one accepted, it would be valid.
The key point: shuyu' in a divisible thing is the obstacle.
3
State the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that the contract is a single tamlik (ownership transfer), not two separate gifts. Thus, there is no shuyu'. They analogize to rahn (pawn): pawning one item to two creditors is valid, even though the item is undivided.
The analogy (qiyas) with rahn is central to their position.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
Abu Hanifa distinguishes rahn: in rahn, the ruling is detention (habs), which is fully established for each creditor. In hibah, the ruling is ownership (milk), which is split into shares, creating shuyu'.
The distinction shows why the analogy does not apply according to Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the thamarah and mufta bihi
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that if the gift is invalid (Abu Hanifa), the recipients must return the house. If valid (Sahibayn), they become co-owners. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the Sahibayn, as it is easier and more widely applied.
Imam al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah leans toward the Sahibayn.

یہاں شیوع نہیں ہے اور اگر ایک مکان ایک ہی شخص نے دو کو ہبہ کیا تو جائز نہیں امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ان دونوں کو یکبارگی ہدیہ ہے اس لئے کہ تملیک ایک ہی ہے تو شیوع متحقق نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے دو کے پاس ایک مکان رہن رکھے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان کی میں سے ہر ایک کو نصف مکان کا ہبہ ہے۔ اسی لئے اگر یہ ہبہ قابل تقسیم چیز میں ہوتا اور ان میں سے ایک قبول کرتا تو صحیح ہو جاتا اور اس لئے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے نصف میں ملکیت ثابت ہوتی ہے تو تملیک بھی یونہی ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ملکیت تملیک ہی کا حکم ہے۔ اور اس اعتبار سے شیوع متحقق ہوگا۔ بخلاف رہن کے کیونکہ اس کا حکم روکنا ہے اور روکنا ان میں سے ہر ایک کو پورا ثابت ہوتا ہے تو اس میں کچھ شیوع نہیں۔ اسی وجہ سے اگر ان میں سے ایک کا قرض چکا یا تو رہن سے کچھ واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ اگر دو محتاجوں کو دس درہم صدقہ یا ہبہ کئے تو جائز ہے اور اگر دو مالداروں کو صدقہ یا ہبہ کئے جائز نہیں۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ مالداروں کے لئے بھی جائز ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ نے ہبہ اور صدقہ میں سے ہر ایک کو دوسرے سے مجاز قرار دیا ہے اور صلاحیت ثابت ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک تملیک ہے بلا عوض۔ اور جامع صغیر میں ہبہ وصدقہ کے درمیان حکم میں فرق کیا ہے۔ اور مبسوط میں یکساں رکھا ہے۔ چناچہ کہا ہے کہ ایسے ہی صدقہ ہے۔ کیونکہ شیوع کا ہونا دونوں میں مانع ہے۔ ان دونوں کے قبضہ پر ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور روایت جامع پر وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ صدقہ سے رضائے الہی مقصود ہے اور وہ ایک ہی ہے اور ہبہ سے مالدار کی خوشی مطلوب ہوتی ہے۔ اور یہ دو ہیں۔ کہا گیا ہے کہ یہی صحیح ہے اور مبسوط میں جو مذکور ہے اس سے دو مالداروں پر صدقہ مراد ہے۔
تشریح قوله ولو وهب اثنان الخ دو آدمی ایک گھر ایک آدمی کو ہبہ کریں تو ہبہ درست ہے کیونکہ دونوں نے پورا گھر موہوب کے حوالے کیا ہے اور موہوب لہ نے پورے پر قبضہ کیا ہے تو شیوع نہیں پایا گیا لہذا یہ جائز ہے لیکن اس کا عکس صحیح نہیں۔ یعنی اگر ایک شخص اپنا گھر دو آدمیوں کو ہبہ کرے تو امام صاحب اور امام زفر کے نزدیک صحیح نہیں اور صاحبین کے نزدیک صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ تملیک متحد اور عقد واحد ہے تو شیوع نہ رہا۔ جیسے ایک چیز دو شخصوں کے پاس گروی رکھنا صحیح ہے۔ امام صاحب یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ واہب نے ایک کو نصف نصف گھر ہبہ کیا ہے اور نصف غیر معین و غیر مقسوم ہے۔ پس محتمل القسمتہ میں شیوع پایا گیا جو جواز ہبہ کے لئے مانع ہے۔ چناچہ اگر یہی ہبہ ناقابل قسمت چیز میں ہوتا اور ان دونوں میں سے کوئی ایک قبول کر لیتا تو ہبہ صحیح ہو جاتا اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ گویا اس نے ہر ایک کو علیحدہ علیحدہ نصف نصف حصہ ہبہ کیا ہے۔ نیز اس لئے بھی کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے نصف میں ملکیت ثابت ہوتی ہے تو تملیک بھی اسی طرح نصف نصف کی ہوگی اس لئے کہ ملکیت تملیک ہی کا حکم یعنی اس کا اثر ہے۔ پس اس اعتبار سے شیوع محقق ہوگا۔ بخلاف رہن کے کہ اس میں کل شئی مرہون ہر ایک کے دین کے بدلہ میں بس ہوگی۔ اس لئے رہن صحیح ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر اس نے دونوں میں سے کسی کا قرضہ چکایا تو رہن میں سے کچھ واپس نہیں لے سکتا جب تک کہ دونوں کا قرضہ ادا نہ کرے۔

قوله و في الجامع الخ جامع صغیر ومبسوط کی روایت میں چونکہ اختلاف واقع ہوا ہے اس لئے صاحب ہدایہ جامع صغیر کی روایت ذکر کر رہے ہیں جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ اگر دس درہم دو فقیروں کو صدقہ یا ہبہ کئے تو صحیح ہے اور اگر دو مالداروں کو ہبہ یا صدقہ کئے تو صحیح نہیں یہ تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ مالداروں کے لئے بھی صحیح ہے قول ابو حنیفہ کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ آپ نے ہبہ وصدقہ میں سے ہر ایک کو دوسرے سے مجاز قرار دیا ہے یعنی جب فقیر کو ہبہ کیا گیا تو وہ مجاز ا صدقہ ہے اور صدقہ میں بٹوارا ہو کر قبضہ شرط نہیں ہے تو دو یا اس سے زائد فقیروں کو مشترک ہبہ جائز ہوا کیونکہ یہ ہبہ بمعنی صدقہ ہے اور جب مالداروں کو صدقہ دیا گیا تو یہ جائز نہیں کیونکہ یہ صدقہ بمعنی ہبہ ہے۔
قوله وفرق بين الهبة ... الخ اور امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں ہبہ وصدقہ کے درمیان حکم میں فرق کیا ہے۔ اور مبسوط میں دونوں کو یکساں رکھا ہے۔ چنانچہ مسئلہ ہبہ کے بعد کہا ہے کہ اسی طرح صدقہ بھی جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ اشتراک کا ہونا ہبہ اور صدقہ دونوں میں مانع ہے اس لئے کہ دونوں کا پورا ہونا قبضہ پر موقوف ہے۔ روایت جامع صغیر پر وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ صدقہ سے رضائے الہی مقصود ہوتی ہے اور یہ دو فقیروں کو دینے میں بھی واحد ہے اور مالداروں کو ہبہ کرنے میں خود ان کی خوشی مقصود ہوتی ہے۔ اور یہ دو ہیں۔ بقول بعض مشائخ روایت جامع ہی صحیح ہے اور مبسوط میں جو صدقہ مذکور ہے اس سے مالداروں پر صدقہ مراد ہے یعنی ہبہ کو مجاز صدقہ کہا ہے۔
Here there is no shuyu'. And if one person gives a house to two persons, it is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifah; the two companions (Sahibayn) say it is valid. Because he gave it to both simultaneously, since the ownership transfer (tamlik) is one, so shuyu' does not occur. Like if he pawns one house with two persons. Imam Abu Hanifah's proof is that he gave each of them a gift of half the house. Therefore, if this gift was of a divisible thing and one of them accepted, it would be valid. And because each of them gets ownership of half, so the ownership transfer is likewise, for ownership is the effect of transfer. On this basis, shuyu' is realized. Unlike pawn (rahn), because its ruling is detention, and detention is established completely for each of them, so there is no shuyu' in it. For this reason, if one of them pays off his debt, he cannot take back anything from the pawn until both debts are paid. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is stated that if one gives ten dirhams as sadaqah or hibah to two needy persons, it is valid; if to two rich persons, it is not valid. The two companions say it is valid even for the rich. Imam Abu Hanifah considers each of hibah and sadaqah as a metaphor for the other, and the capacity is established that each is a transfer without compensation. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, a distinction is made in the ruling between hibah and sadaqah. In al-Mabsut, they are treated equally. Thus it is said that sadaqah is similar (invalid) because shuyu' is an obstacle in both, due to both being dependent on possession. According to the narration of al-Jami', the reason for the distinction is that in sadaqah, the pleasure of Allah is intended, and that is one; in hibah to the rich, their pleasure is sought, and they are two. It is said that this is correct, and what is mentioned in al-Mabsut means sadaqah to the rich (i.e., hibah metaphorically called sadaqah).
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a hibah (gift) when a single item is given to two persons. The main ruling: Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar hold that such a gift is invalid due to shuyu' (undivided sharing), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider it valid. The proof of Abu Hanifa is that the giver actually gives half to each, and since the item is divisible (qabil al-qismah), shuyu' arises. If the item were indivisible and only one accepted, it would be valid. The Sahibayn argue that the gift is a single contract of tamlik (ownership transfer), so no shuyu' occurs. They analogize to rahn (pawn), where pawning one item with two creditors is valid. Abu Hanifa distinguishes rahn because it involves detention (habs), which applies fully to each, not shared ownership. The passage then discusses a related issue from Jami' al-Saghir: giving ten dirhams to two needy persons as sadaqah or hibah is valid; to two rich persons, it is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn consider it valid even for the rich. The commentator explains that Abu Hanifa treats hibah to the needy as a metaphor for sadaqah, which does not require divided possession, while sadaqah to the rich is metaphorically hibah, which does require it. The difference between the rulings in Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut is reconciled: al-Mabsut's statement that sadaqah is also invalid refers to sadaqah given to the rich (i.e., hibah disguised as sadaqah).

Key Terms
شُيُوع (shuyu'): Undivided common ownership of a single item among multiple parties, which is generally not allowed in hibah as it prevents the full transfer intended.
تَمْلِيك (tamlik): The act of transferring ownership from the giver to the receiver, which is the essence of hibah.
هِبَة (hibah): A voluntary gift of property to another person without compensation, which requires offer (ijab), acceptance (qabul), and possession (qabd) for binding effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, is a hibah of one house to two persons valid or invalid?
A) Invalid, because the house is divisible and shuyu' is forbidden.
B) Valid, because the contract is a single tamlik.
C) Valid only if the recipients are poor.
D) Invalid unless the house is indivisible.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position allows a single gift to two persons, treating it as one contract of ownership transfer, even for divisible items.

Sadaqah vs Hibah: The Jami' al-Saghir Distinction
Extension: Sadaqah vs Hibah distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Imam Abu Hanifa's distinction between sadaqah and hibah when given to multiple poor vs rich persons, and reconcile the differing narrations in Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut.

Core Idea
Shuyu' allowed in sadaqah to the poor (one divine pleasure) but not in hibah to the rich (multiple human pleasures).

This lesson extends the discussion of shuyu' to charitable giving. In Jami' al-Saghir, Imam Abu Hanifa rules that giving ten dirhams to two poor persons as sadaqah or hibah is valid, but to two rich persons it is invalid. The Sahibayn consider it valid even for the rich. You will explore the reasoning and the reconciliation with al-Mabsut.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario from Jami' al-Saghir
The case: one person gives ten dirhams to two recipients. If the recipients are poor, it is valid; if rich, it is invalid (Abu Hanifa). The Sahibayn say it is valid in both cases.
The key variable is the wealth of the recipients, not the nature of the gift.
2
State Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa treats hibah to the poor as metaphorically sadaqah (since divine pleasure is the intent), and sadaqah to the rich as metaphorically hibah (since human pleasure is the intent). Shuyu' is allowed in sadaqah but not in hibah.
The intention behind the gift changes the ruling.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn do not make this distinction; they hold that any gift (sadaqah or hibah) to multiple recipients is valid regardless of the recipients' wealth.
Their position is consistent with their general view on shuyu'.
4
Reconcile al-Mabsut with Jami' al-Saghir
In al-Mabsut, Imam Muhammad treats sadaqah and hibah equally (both invalid when given to multiple persons). The commentator reconciles: al-Mabsut refers to sadaqah given to the rich (i.e., disguised hibah). Jami' al-Saghir refers to sadaqah to the poor.
Thus, there is no real contradiction; the difference is about the intended recipient.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Jami' al-Saghir (Abu Hanifa's distinction), as it is more nuanced and widely accepted. Some later scholars prefer the Sahibayn's view for general convenience.
The commentator notes that the distinction in Jami' al-Saghir is considered correct by many mashayikh.
