قوله وفرق بين الهبة ... الخ اور امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں ہبہ وصدقہ کے درمیان حکم میں فرق کیا ہے۔ اور مبسوط میں دونوں کو یکساں رکھا ہے۔ چنانچہ مسئلہ ہبہ کے بعد کہا ہے کہ اسی طرح صدقہ بھی جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ اشتراک کا ہونا ہبہ اور صدقہ دونوں میں مانع ہے اس لئے کہ دونوں کا پورا ہونا قبضہ پر موقوف ہے۔ روایت جامع صغیر پر وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ صدقہ سے رضائے الہی مقصود ہوتی ہے اور یہ دو فقیروں کو دینے میں بھی واحد ہے اور مالداروں کو ہبہ کرنے میں خود ان کی خوشی مقصود ہوتی ہے۔ اور یہ دو ہیں۔ بقول بعض مشائخ روایت جامع ہی صحیح ہے اور مبسوط میں جو صدقہ مذکور ہے اس سے مالداروں پر صدقہ مراد ہے یعنی ہبہ کو مجاز صدقہ کہا ہے۔
Here there is no shuyu'. And if one person gives a house to two persons, it is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifah; the two companions (Sahibayn) say it is valid. Because he gave it to both simultaneously, since the ownership transfer (tamlik) is one, so shuyu' does not occur. Like if he pawns one house with two persons. Imam Abu Hanifah's proof is that he gave each of them a gift of half the house. Therefore, if this gift was of a divisible thing and one of them accepted, it would be valid. And because each of them gets ownership of half, so the ownership transfer is likewise, for ownership is the effect of transfer. On this basis, shuyu' is realized. Unlike pawn (rahn), because its ruling is detention, and detention is established completely for each of them, so there is no shuyu' in it. For this reason, if one of them pays off his debt, he cannot take back anything from the pawn until both debts are paid. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is stated that if one gives ten dirhams as sadaqah or hibah to two needy persons, it is valid; if to two rich persons, it is not valid. The two companions say it is valid even for the rich. Imam Abu Hanifah considers each of hibah and sadaqah as a metaphor for the other, and the capacity is established that each is a transfer without compensation. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, a distinction is made in the ruling between hibah and sadaqah. In al-Mabsut, they are treated equally. Thus it is said that sadaqah is similar (invalid) because shuyu' is an obstacle in both, due to both being dependent on possession. According to the narration of al-Jami', the reason for the distinction is that in sadaqah, the pleasure of Allah is intended, and that is one; in hibah to the rich, their pleasure is sought, and they are two. It is said that this is correct, and what is mentioned in al-Mabsut means sadaqah to the rich (i.e., hibah metaphorically called sadaqah).
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a hibah (gift) when a single item is given to two persons. The main ruling: Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar hold that such a gift is invalid due to shuyu' (undivided sharing), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider it valid. The proof of Abu Hanifa is that the giver actually gives half to each, and since the item is divisible (qabil al-qismah), shuyu' arises. If the item were indivisible and only one accepted, it would be valid. The Sahibayn argue that the gift is a single contract of tamlik (ownership transfer), so no shuyu' occurs. They analogize to rahn (pawn), where pawning one item with two creditors is valid. Abu Hanifa distinguishes rahn because it involves detention (habs), which applies fully to each, not shared ownership. The passage then discusses a related issue from Jami' al-Saghir: giving ten dirhams to two needy persons as sadaqah or hibah is valid; to two rich persons, it is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn consider it valid even for the rich. The commentator explains that Abu Hanifa treats hibah to the needy as a metaphor for sadaqah, which does not require divided possession, while sadaqah to the rich is metaphorically hibah, which does require it. The difference between the rulings in Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut is reconciled: al-Mabsut's statement that sadaqah is also invalid refers to sadaqah given to the rich (i.e., hibah disguised as sadaqah).

Key Terms
صَدَقَة (sadaqah): Charitable gift given for the pleasure of Allah, which is treated more leniently regarding shuyu' when given to the poor.
هِبَة (hibah): A voluntary gift of property to another person without compensation, which requires divided possession for multiple recipients if they are rich.
تَمْلِيك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; in sadaqah, this is not strict.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi, giving a joint gift of money to two rich people is:
A) Valid, because the contract is a single tamlik.
B) Invalid, because it is considered hibah and shuyu' invalidates it.
C) Valid, because it is sadaqah.
D) Invalid, unless the amount is less than a certain limit.

Key Takeaway
The intention and recipient status transform the ruling: sadaqah to the poor permits shuyu'; hibah to the rich does not.

Hiba of Specified Shares to Two Persons: Two-Thirds and One-Third
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hibah with specified shares and the concept of shuyu'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on hibah with specified unequal shares, identify the key factor (tansis) that distinguishes their views, and apply their reasoning to similar cases.

Core Idea
Specifying shares (tansis) in a hibah to multiple persons makes shuyu' explicit and invalidates the gift according to most Hanafi imams.

This passage delves into a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding hibah (gift) when the donor specifies distinct shares for two recipients, such as two-thirds and one-third. While all imams agree on the general rule that a hibah to multiple persons without specifying shares is valid, disagreement arises when shares are explicitly stated. Understanding this nuance—and the underlying reasoning about shuyu' (undivided share)—is essential for correctly applying Hanafi law in gift transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
What is the act? Hibah to two persons with specified unequal shares (two-thirds and one-third). Note the specification.
2
State the positions of the three imams
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: invalid. Muhammad: valid. For equal halves, Abu Yusuf has two narrations.
Abu Yusuf's position depends on whether shares are specified.
3
Understand the core reasoning (shuyu')
Why does specifying shares lead to shuyu' and invalidity? Because it shows the donor's intent to transfer ownership of specific parts, which necessitates undivided shares in the item.
Shuyu' is unavoidable when parts are specified.
4
Analyze the distinction for Abu Yusuf
Why does Abu Yusuf agree with Abu Hanifa when shares are specified but has two views on equal shares? Because specification makes shuyu' apparent; without specification, the contract may be seen as a single tamlik.
Equal halves without specification may be valid.
5
Apply the principle to a similar case (rahn)
The text uses pawn as analogy: specifying parts in a pawn (rahn) is also invalid due to shuyu'. This supports the majority view.
The analogy reinforces the centrality of tansis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ وَهَبَ لِرَجُلَيْنِ دَارًا لِأَحَدِهِمَا ثُلُثَاهَا وَلِلْآخَرِ ثُلُثَهَا لَمْ يَجُزْ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَجُوزُ وَلَوْ قَالَ لِأَحَدِهِمَا نِصْفُهَا وَلِلْآخَرِ نِصْفُهَا عَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ فِيهِ رِوَايَتَانِ فَأَبُو حَنِيفَةَ مَرَّ عَلَى أَصْلِهِ وَكَذَا مُحَمَّدٌ وَالْفَرْقُ لِأَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّ بِالتَّنْصِيصِ عَلَى الْأَبْعَاضِ يَظْهَرُ أَنَّ قَصْدَهُ ثُبُوتُ الْمِلْكِ فِي الْبَعْضِ فَيَتَحَقَّقُ الشُّيُوعُ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَجُوزُ إِذَا رَهَنَ مِنْ رَجُلَيْنِ وَنَصَّ عَلَى الْأَبْعَاضِ.
And if he gives a house to two men, to one of them two-thirds of it and to the other one-third of it, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said it is permissible. And if he said to one of them half of it and to the other half of it, from Abu Yusuf there are two narrations. So Abu Hanifa follows his principle, and likewise Muhammad. And the distinction for Abu Yusuf is that by specifying the parts, it becomes apparent that his intention is to establish ownership in a part, so shuyu' is realized, and for this reason it is not permissible if he pawns an item with two persons and specifies the parts.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage addresses a more specific case within the same chapter on hibah: when the giver specifies distinct shares for each recipient, such as two-thirds for one and one-third for the other. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, this is invalid because specifying the shares makes the shuyu' (undivided sharing) explicit. Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, considers it valid, following his general principle that a single contract of tamlik suffices. The commentator explains that Abu Yusuf distinguishes between specifying the shares (e.g., two-thirds and one-third) and not specifying (e.g., simply giving to two without mention of shares). When shares are specified, the giver's intent to transfer ownership of specific portions is evident, thus shuyu' is unavoidable, invalidating the hibah. But if no shares are mentioned, the gift might be considered a single tamlik. Abu Yusuf has two narrations on the case of equal halves: one allowing it (by analogy with Muhammad) and one disallowing (by analogy with Abu Hanifa). The Quranic example of rahn (pawn) supports the invalidity when parts are specified, as that would also create shuyu' in pawn.

Key Terms
أَبْعَاض (ab'ād): Parts or portions of an item, specifically the shares like two-thirds and one-third.
تَنْصِيص (tansīs): The act of specifying or designating the shares explicitly in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person gives a house to two individuals, specifying that one gets one-third and the other gets two-thirds, what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?
A) Valid because it is a single contract of tamlik.
B) Invalid because specifying shares leads to shuyu'.
C) Valid only if the recipients accept.
D) Invalid only if the house is undivided.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, specifying shares (tansis) in a hibah to multiple persons invalidates the gift due to the creation of shuyu'.

Revocation of Hibah: Hanafi–Shafi‘i Dispute
Opening ruling of the chapter on revocation of hibah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on revocation of hibah to a non-relative and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith.

Core Idea
Revocation of a gift to a non-relative is allowed in Hanafi law, despite the hadith prohibiting it.

This passage opens the chapter on revocation of gifts (rujūʿ) in al-Hidayah. The Hanafi school holds that a gift to a non-relative (ajnabī) can be revoked, while Imam al-Shāfiʿī prohibits all revocation after possession. The disagreement hinges on the interpretation of the Prophet’s hadith: 'The one who revokes his gift is like the one who returns to his vomit.' We will examine both positions and their evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling given in the text: for a gift to a non-relative (ajnabī), the giver may revoke it.
This is the default Hanafi rule.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The text cites Imam al-Shafi'i: 'No revocation in it.' Recognize that this is an absolute prohibition.
Shafi'is base this on the hadith.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The hadith 'lā yarjiʿ...' (the full version: 'The one who revokes his gift is like the one who returns to his vomit') is used by Shafi'is as evidence for absolute prohibition.
They take the apparent meaning as general.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis interpret the hadith as applying specifically to gifts to relatives (dhawi rahim) or as a strong discouragement (makruh tahrimi), not as absolute nullity. They also employ istihsan to allow revocation for non-relatives.
The prohibition is not universal in Hanafi usul.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis permit revocation for gifts to non-relatives; Shafi'is forbid it entirely. This affects many everyday transactions.
Example: a gift to a neighbor can be revoked in Hanafi but not in Shafi'i.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ مَا يَصِحُ رُجُوعُهُ وَمَا لَا يَصِحُ قَالَ وَإِذَا وَهَبَ هِبَةً لِأَجْنَبِيٍّ فَلَهُ الرُّجُوعُ فِيهَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا رُجُوعَ فِيهَا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا يَرْجِعُ
Chapter on what makes revocation valid and what does not. He said: And when he gives a gift to a non-relative (stranger), he may revoke it. And al-Shafi'i said: No revocation in it, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'He does not revoke...'
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage introduces a new topic in the book of Hibah: the ruling on whether a gift can be revoked by the giver. The text is from the matn of al-Hidayah. The initial ruling: According to the Hanafi school, if a gift is given to a non-relative (ajnabī), the giver has the right to revoke it (rujūʿ). Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees entirely, holding that no gift can be revoked under any circumstances. His evidence is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'He does not revoke...' (the full hadith is: 'The one who revokes his gift is like the one who returns to his vomit'). In the Hanafi view, this hadith is interpreted as referring to gifts to relatives or as a strong discouragement (karahah) but not absolute prohibition, allowing revocation in certain cases. The chapter will then detail conditions and exceptions.

Key Terms
رُجُوع (rujūʿ): Revocation of a gift, i.e., the giver taking back the gifted property from the donee.
أَجْنَبِي (ajnabī): A non-relative, i.e., someone not connected by blood or marriage within the prohibited degrees (mahram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on revoking a gift given to a non-relative (ajnabi)?
A) Revocation is not allowed under any circumstances.
B) Revocation is allowed.
C) Revocation is allowed only if the gift is still in the giver's possession.
D) Revocation is allowed only if the donee agrees.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law permits revocation of a gift to a non-relative, distinguishing it from gifts to relatives and sadaqah, and interpreting the prohibition hadith as non-absolute.

Hibah to Two Persons with Specified Shares: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hibah with specified shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on gifting specified fractional shares and apply the principle of shuyu‘ to distinguish valid from invalid hibah.

Core Idea
Specifying shares at the outset creates shuyu‘, making hibah invalid for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

When a donor gifts a property to two recipients and explicitly states the shares (e.g., two-thirds and one-third), the validity of the gift depends on whether the specification is initial or after a general mention. Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known disagreement among the three leading imams. This passage presents their positions and the underlying analogies with pawn (rahn) and sale (bay‘).

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The central question: Is a hibah valid when the donor specifies fractional shares (e.g., one-third, two-thirds) at the time of gifting, without first making a general mention of the entire property?
This issue arises only when shares are specified; if the donor says 'I gift you this house' and later specifies, it is valid by consensus.
2
State the three positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (in one narration) hold it invalid. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it valid. For equal shares (one-half each), Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one equating it to unequal shares (invalid) and one allowing it (valid).
3
Understand Abu Hanifa’s principle
Abu Hanifa relies on the principle that specifying parts at the outset creates an undivided share (shuyu‘), which is not permissible in hibah because hibah requires complete possession. He analogizes to pawn (rahn): if one pawns an item to two persons with specified shares, it is invalid due to shuyu‘.
4
Understand Muhammad’s analogy
Muhammad al-Shaybani argues by analogy to sale (bay‘): if one sells an item to two persons with specified shares, the sale is valid; similarly, hibah should be valid. The Hanafi response distinguishes sale as an exchange contract where specification is acceptable, whereas hibah is pure beneficence.
5
Analyze Abu Yusuf’s distinction
Abu Yusuf distinguishes between unequal shares (tafadul) and equal shares (taswiya). According to one narration, he allows equal shares because they may not imply specification of distinct parts, but considers unequal shares invalid.
This distinction is unique to Abu Yusuf.

Source Text

کہ اگر بائع مشتریین میں سے ہر ایک کے ساتھ نصف نصف فروخت کرے یا کمی بیشی کے ساتھ فروخت کرے بہر دو صورت بیع جائز ہے تو ایسے ہی ہبہ بھی جائز ہے۔
If he gifted to two men a house, for one of them two-thirds and for the other one-third, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said it is valid. And if he said to one of them half of it and to the other half of it, there are two narrations from Abu Yusuf. So Abu Hanifa proceeded on his principle, and likewise Muhammad. The distinction for Abu Yusuf is that by specifying the parts, it becomes apparent that his intent is to establish ownership in the part, so the undivided share (shuyū') is realized, and for this reason it is not valid if he pawned (rahan) to two men and specified the parts. [Commentary in Urdu]
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a hibah (gift) made to two recipients with specified fractional shares. The ruling is part of the discussion on hibah of undivided shares (shuyū'). The basis of the disagreement is whether specifying shares at the outset (without prior general mention) renders the gift valid or not. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that if the shares are unequal (e.g., two-thirds and one-third), the gift is invalid because the donor's intent to assign specific parts is clear, leading to an undivided share (shuyū') which is not permissible in hibah. Muhammad al-Shaybani considers it valid by analogy to sale, where such specification is allowed. For equal shares (one-half each), Abu Hanifa maintains invalidity, Muhammad maintains validity, and Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one equating it to unequal shares (invalid) and another allowing it (valid). The commentary elaborates that the specification may be either before or after a general mention; if after, it is permissible by consensus; if at the outset, the disagreement applies. The analogy with pawn (rahn) is used to illustrate the principle of shuyū'.

Key Terms
شُيُوع (shuyū‘): Undivided share or common ownership of a specific part of a jointly owned property, where the exact division is not yet made.
تفاضل (tafāḍul): Inequality of shares (e.g., two-thirds vs one-third).
تسوية (taswiya): Equality of shares (e.g., one-half each).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, which of the following hibah is valid?
A) Gifting a house to two persons saying 'two-thirds for Zaid and one-third for Amr' without any prior general mention.
B) Gifting a house to two persons saying 'I gift this house to both of you, half for Zaid and half for Amr' without prior general mention.
C) Gifting a house to two persons with a general statement 'I gift this house to both of you' and later specifying unequal shares.
D) Gifting a house to two persons saying 'I gift this house to both of you equally' without specifying shares.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, hibah with specified fractional shares is invalid if the specification is made at the outset, due to shuyu‘, though Imam Muhammad allows it by analogy to sale.

Donor's Right to Revoke a Gift before Compensation
Hanafi evidence for donor's right to revoke

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on gift revocation, identify the primary dalil (hadith and custom), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A donor may revoke his gift only if no compensation has been received; it is legally valid but severely disliked.

The ability to take back a gift after delivery is a contested issue between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi proofs: a specific hadith and a rational argument based on custom. It also addresses and refutes the Shafi'i evidence. Understanding this dispute clarifies not only a specific ruling but also how Hanafi jurists weigh textual evidence and customary practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school holds: the donor may revoke the gift as long as he has not received any compensation (عوض) from the donee.
The ruling is that revocation is permissible (mubah) but makruh tanzih.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a gift after delivery is completely irrevocable, like sadaqah.
The Shafi'i position is based on a different hadith and analogy.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith of Abu Darda' that compares an undemanded gift to sadaqah, and the analogy that ownership is fully transferred.
The text critiques the chain of this hadith.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Study how the Hanafi school rebuts the Shafi'i proof: the chain is weak, and the word 'yastawhib' is interpreted as seeking reward, not compensation. Also, the custom of gift-giving supports revocation.
The Hanafi response also distinguishes the father's special right (which is agreed upon).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: Hanafis allow the donor to take back the gift; Shafi'is do not. This affects everyday transactions like giving gifts to friends or relatives without compensation.
The hadith about the dog and vomit explains why revocation, though valid, is disliked.

Source Text

قَالَ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلّم الرجل احق بهبته مالم يثب منها .
حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ واہب شئی موہوب کا زیادہ حقدار ہے جب تک کہ اس کو اس کا عوض نہ دیا گیا ہو اس کو ابن حزم نے یوں معلول کیا ہے کہ اس کا راوی ابراہیم بن اسمعیل بن مجمع بن جاریہ ضعیف ہے اور عمرو بن دینار کو حضرت ابو ہریرہ سے.

اشرف الہدایہ جلد - يازدهم
۲۶۱
طبرانی کو ابن ابی لیلی کی وجہ سے اور طریق دارقطنی کو ابراہیم بن ابی یحی اسلمی اور محمد بن عبید اللہ عزرمی کی وجہ سے معلول کہا گیا ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث اگر فی نفسہ حجت ہونے کے قابل نہ بھی ہو تو شاہد ضرور ہو سکتی ہے ۔ جب کہ ابن ابی لیلی حسن الحدیث ہے۔ ۔ حدیث ابن عمر اس کی تخریج حاکم نے مستدرک میں دار قطنی نے سنن میں بیہقی نے کتاب للعرفہ میں کی ہے۔ ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من وهب هبة فهو احق بها مالم يثبت منها حافظ بیٹی کہتے ہیں کہ اس کے رفع میں عبداللہ بن موسی کو وہم ہوا ہے اور محفوظ روایت عبد اللہ بن واہب کی ہے جو حضرت ابن عمر پر موقوف ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ حاکم نے اس حدیث کو شرط شیخین صیح مانا ہے۔ شیخ عبدالحق نے الا حکام میں کہا ہے کہ اس کے رواۃ ثقہ ہیں۔ ابن حزم نے بھی اس کی تصحیح کی ہے۔ پھر احمد بن حازم بن ابی عزرہ کا متابع علی بن سہل بن المغیرہ بھی موجود ہے ( عند البیہقی ) صاحب جو ہر تقی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ
کہنا بھی غلط ہے کہ اس میں عبداللہ بن موسی کو وہم ہوا ہے بلکہ اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا کہ عبداللہ کے پاس اس حدیث کی دوسندیں ہیں۔ سوال ممکن ہے کہ حدیث میں واہب کے لئے احق ہونے کا حکم شئی موہوب سپرد کرنے سے پہلے پہلے ہو۔ پس حدیث سے حجت قائم نہیں ہوتی۔ جواب ... یہ احتمال صحیح نہیں اس لئے کہ اول تو یہاں مال پر ہبہ کا لفظ بولا گیا ہے اور قبض و تسلیم سے پہلے وہ ہبہ نہیں ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ واہب کو احق کہا گیا۔ معلوم ہوا کہ اس میں دوسرے کا بھی حق ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ دوسرے کا حق قبضہ کے بعد ہی ہوگا۔
حدیث عبدالہ بن عمر اس کی تخریج امام ابوداور نسائی، ابن ماجہ نے کی ہے۔ عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه و سلّم قَالَ: مثل الذي يستر وما وهب كمثل الكلب يقئى فيأكل قيئه فاذا استرد الواهب فليو قف فليعرف بما استردثم ليد فع اليه ما وهب “
حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا۔ جو دے کر پھیر لیتا ہے۔ اس کی مثال کتے کی سی ہے جو تی، کر کے پھر کھالیتا ہے پس جو شخص ہبہ کر کے پھیر لینا چاہے تو موہوب لہ کو پھیر لینے کا سبب پوچھنا چاہیے۔ اگر بدلہ نہ ملنا سبب ہو تو بدلہ دیوے۔ جب معلوم ہو جائے تو اس وقت پھیر دے۔ اس حدیث میں صریح دلالت ہے کہ واہب کے لئے حق استرداد ہے ورنہ موہوب لہ کو واپس کرنے کا حکم نہ کیا جاتا۔ ابن حزم نے اس کو اسامہ بن زید راوی کی وجہ سے معلول کہا ہے۔ لیکن یہ س لئے میچ نہیں۔ کہ اسامہ بن زید ضعیف نہیں بلکہ صدوق ہے اور صحیح مسلم و سنن اربعہ کے رجال میں سے ہے امام بخاری نے اس سے تعلیمیا روایت لی ہے۔ سوال امام طحاوی نے معانی الآثار میں حضرت ابوالدردانہ سے روایت کیا ہے۔ من وهب من غيران يستوهب فهي كسبيل الصدقة فليس له ان يرجع في صدقته حالا نکہ امام ابو حنیفہ اس کے قائل نہیں۔
جواب ... اس اثر کی سند میں راشد بن سعد ہے جس کی بابت حافظ ابن حجر نے تہذیب میں کہا ہے کہ حضرت ابو درداء سے اس کی روایت محل نظر ہے۔ نیز اس حدیث میں جو استیہاب آیا ہے یہ اردہ ثواب پر محمول ہے نہ کہ شرط عوض پر ۔ فكان هذافی معنی حدیث عمر۔
.......
قوله ای لم يعوض .... ب لفظ جز حدیث سے نہیں بلکہ صاحب ہدایہ کی طرف سے عالم جب منھا کی تفسیر ہے لفظ لم یشب - اثا بہ معنی تعویض
سے مجہول کا صیغہ ہے اور یہ اصل میں ثواب بمعنی رجوع سے مشتق ہے یقال ثاب(ن) تو ابا معنی لوٹنا و اثاب الثابه معنی بدلہ دینا۔ قوله ولأنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ الخ یہ ہماری عقلی دلیل ہے کہ از راہ عادت غالب اوقات ہبہ سے مقصود یہی ہوتا ہے کہ اس کا عوض ملے۔ چنانچہ آدمی اپنے سے اونچے مرتبہ والے کو تو ہدیہ اس لئے دیتا ہے تا کہ اس کے جاہ و حشم اور رعب کے ذریعہ خود کومحفوظ رکھ سکے اور اپنے سے کم تر کو اس لئے دیتا ہے تا کہ وہ اس کی خدمت کرے اور آڑے وقت میں کام آئے۔ اور اپنے برابر کو اس لئے دیتا ہے تا کہ وہ اس کا مالی عوض ملے۔ اسی لئے کہا جاتا ہے۔ الا یــادی قروض “ ہدایا تو قرضے ہیں ) پس جب واہب کو ہبہ کا عوض نہیں ملا تو اسکو نخ کا اختیار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس عقد میں فسخ ہونے کی صلاحیت ہے۔
Hanafi Proof: And our proof is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'The donor is more entitled to his gift as long as he has not received compensation (i.e., not been recompensed). And because the purpose of the contract (gift) is compensation by custom, so the authority to rescind is established when compensation is missed, since the contract admits rescission. What is meant by the narrated hadith (from Shafi'i) is to deny the absolute right of revocation and to establish it for the father alone, for he becomes owner of it due to need, and that is called revocation. And his saying in the book 'he has the right to revoke' is a statement of the ruling. As for the dislike, it is necessary due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'The one who revokes his gift is like the one who returns to his vomit.' And this is to indicate its repugnance. Commentary... (follows with hadith of Abu Hurairah, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, and responses to criticisms)... Then hadith: 'The example of one who takes back what he gave is like a dog that vomits and then eats its vomit.' So when a donor wants to take back, the donee should be asked why it is taken back; if due to no compensation, give compensation. Then he may take it back. This hadith explicitly indicates the donor's right of retrieval. (Then response to Shafi'i's hadith from Abu Darda'...). The text then explains the word 'لم يعوض' and the rational proof: by custom, gifts are given for compensation, so when no compensation is received, revocation is allowed.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive commentary (sharh) from Ashraf al-Hidayah on the Hanafi proof for the donor's right to revoke a gift (رجوع الواهب). The main evidence is the hadith: 'الواهب أحق بهبته ما لم يثب منها' (The donor is more entitled to his gift as long as he has not been compensated). The commentator explains that 'لم يثب' means 'لم يعوض' (no compensation received). Then a rational proof (عقلی دلیل) is given: by custom, the purpose of a gift is to receive something in return—whether protection, service, or material compensation. Therefore, when that compensation does not materialize, the donor has the right to rescind the gift because the contract admits rescission. The commentator also addresses the Shafi'i objection and multiple hadith chains (Abu Hurairah, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar) with detailed criticism and defense. The hadith about the dog and vomit establishes that revocation, though legally permissible, is severely disliked (كراهة). The commentator concludes that the donor may revoke as long as no compensation has been given.

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): The act of the donor taking back the gifted property from the donee.
ثواب (thawab): Compensation (عوض) in return for the gift.
واہب (wahib): The donor, the person who makes the gift.
هبة (hiba): Gift; a contract of transfer of ownership without compensation at the time of contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can a donor revoke his gift?
A) At any time, even after receiving compensation.
B) Never, because gift is like sadaqah.
C) Only if he has not received any compensation (iwad) for the gift.
D) Only if the donee is a stranger, not a relative.

Key Takeaway
A donor may revoke a gift only if no compensation has been received; it is legally permissible but makruh.

intermediate
12 min
The Donor's Right to Revoke a Gift and Refutation of Opposing Arguments
Defends Hanafi position on gift revocation with hadith and rational proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on gift revocation, identify the key proofs (hadith and rational), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-arguments using the madhhab dispute map.

Core Idea
A donor may revoke an uncompensated gift, but doing so is severely disliked — a balance of legal permissibility and moral prohibition.

This passage from Al-Hidayah defends the Hanafi ruling that a donor may take back a gift if no compensation was received, even though it is religiously disliked. The author marshals hadith evidence and rational arguments, then systematically refutes objections from Imam al-Shafi'i and others. By studying this lesson, you will engage with the key proofs and understand the practical consequences of this inter-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the donor has the legal right to revoke the gift (ruju') if no compensation (iwad) was given, but it is makruh tahrimi to do so.
This ruling applies only to gifts (hibah), not charity (sadaqah).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the donor cannot revoke a gift once given, except for a parent's gift to a child.
The Shafi'i position relies on a different interpretation of the same hadiths.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith 'la yarji'u fi hibatihi' (do not revoke a gift) and analogy to irrevocable charity.
They also cite the hadith of Umar about not buying back a charity horse.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Study how the Hanafi school refutes each point: the hadith 'la yarji'u' is interpreted as requiring mutual consent or a judge's order, not absolute prohibition; charity is distinct because its purpose is solely divine reward.
The Hanafi school also uses the hadith comparing the revoking donor to a dog returning to vomit as evidence of prohibition, but not nullification.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis allow revocation of an uncompensated gift before any impediment arises; Shafi'is do not allow revocation except for parents.
This affects everyday transactions and disputes over gifted property.

صدقتك
حضرت عمرہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے راہ خدا میں کسی کو سواری کے لئے گھوڑا دیا۔ پھر میں نے دیکھا کہ وہ فروخت ہو رہا ہے میں نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے پوچھا۔ آپ نے فرمایا اسے نہ خرید و اور اپنے صدقہ میں نہ لوٹو۔
حالانکہ خریدنا در حقیقت رجوع نہیں ہے۔ اور حدیث ثانی لا یحل للرجل الھ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عدم حلت نیستلزم حرمت ہے نی مستلزم بطلان ۔ اس لئے کہ حلت کبھی کامل ہوتی ہے اور وہ وہ ہے جس میں نہ حرمت ہونہ کراہت اور کبھی ناقص ہوتی ہے جس میں کراہت موجود ہو۔ اور حدیث میں حل کامل کی نفی ہے نہ کہ حل مطلق کی جو کراہت کو بھی شامل ہوتی ہے۔ اور کر بہت رجوع کے ہم بھی قائل ہیں۔
قوله وقوله في الكتاب ... الخ یعنی کتاب میں جو فرمایا کہ واہب کو رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ہے یہ حکم (دنیاوی) کا بیان ہے۔ رہی کراہت سودہ لازمی ہوگی۔ چنانچہ از راہ دیانت رجوع کرنا مکروہ تحریمی ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے "العائد في هبته كالعائد في قينه" (الجماعة الا الترمذی عن ابن عباس)
This passage explains the Hanafi stance on the donor's right to revoke a gift, using hadith and rational proofs, and refutes objections from other scholars including Imam Shafi'i, concluding that revocation is legally permissible but religiously disliked (makruh tahrimi).
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute passage defending the Hanafi position that a donor may revoke a gift (hibah) if no compensation (iwad) was received, unless certain impediments exist. The text begins by addressing criticisms of a hadith from Ibn Umar that the donor is more entitled to the gift unless compensated. It argues that even if the hadith is not fully authentic, it serves as supporting evidence (shahid). It then rebuts an objection that the hadith might apply before delivery, showing that a gift requires possession. Another hadith comparing the revoking donor to a dog vomiting and re-eating is cited as explicit proof. The author critiques Ibn Hazm's weakening of the hadith and responds to a narration from Abu Darda that would prohibit revocation, explaining that the prohibition applies only when compensation is not sought. The rational proof (al-maqsud) is that gifts are customarily given with expectation of return, so if the donor receives none, revocation is allowed. The text further responds to a critique by Sahib Tahili regarding the condition of no compensation, arguing that the negation of compensation does not negate the underlying purpose. It then addresses Imam Shafi'i's argument that the hadith 'la yarji'u fi hibatihi' means no unilateral revocation, interpreting it as requiring judicial or mutual consent, and distinguishing the parent's right. Finally, it clarifies that although the donor has the legal right to revoke, doing so is makruh tahrimi (severely disliked) based on the hadith 'al-'a'idu fi hibatihi ka al-'a'idi fi qay'ihi' (the one who revokes his gift is like the one who returns to his vomit).

Key Terms
هبة (hibah): A gift; the transfer of ownership of property without compensation.
رجوع (ruju'): Revocation; the act of the donor taking back the gifted property.
عوض (iwad): Compensation; something given in return for the gift.
زیادۃ متصلة (ziyadah muttasilah): Inseparable increase; an addition to the gifted property that cannot be separated without damage (e.g., planting trees, building).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a donor revoking a gift if no compensation was received?
A) It is absolutely prohibited.
B) It is legally permissible but makruh tahrimi.
C) It is permissible only for parents.
D) It is wajib to revoke.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school balances a donor's legal right to revoke an uncompensated gift with a religious prohibition against doing so, distinguishing between worldly legal validity and divine accountability.

The Four Impediments to Gift Revocation
Lists and explains impediments to gift revocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four impediments (mawani') to revocation of a gift and apply each to concrete scenarios.

Core Idea
Revocation of a gift is blocked by compensation, inseparable increase, death, or transfer of ownership.

You may know that a donor can generally revoke a gift. But Islamic law places clear barriers. This passage enumerates the four definitive impediments that permanently block that right. Understanding these will help you see when a gift becomes irreversible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four impediments
Read the Arabic passage and list each impediment as named: 'iwad (compensation), ziyadah muttasilah (inseparable increase), death of either party, and the gifted property leaving the donee's ownership.
2
Understand the reasoning for each
For each impediment, note the brief rationale given: compensation achieves the purpose; inseparable increase makes partial revocation impossible; death transfers rights; leaving ownership disrupts the original link.
Pay attention to the phrase 'ziyadah muttasilah' – it must be physically attached.
3
Apply to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical gift, check if any of the four impediments are present. If so, revocation is invalid (batil). If none, revocation may be possible.
Recall that the gift must have been without compensation initially.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مانع رجوع امور کی تفصیل

ثُمَّ لِلرُّجُوعِ مَوَانِعُ ذَكَرَ بَعْضَهَا فَقَالَ إِلَّا أَنْ يُعَوِضَهُ عَنْهَا لِحُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ أَوْ يَزِيدَ زِيَادَةً مُتَّصِلَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ لَا وَجهَ إِلَى الرُّجُوعِ فِيهَا دُونَ الزِيَادَةِ لِعَدْمِ الْإِمْكَانِ وَلَا مَعَ الزِيَادَةِ لِعَدْمِ دُخُولِهَا تَحْتَ الْعَقْدِ. قَالَ أَوْ يَمُوتُ اَحَدُ الْمُتَعَاقِدَيْنِ لِاَنَّ بِمَوْتِ الْمُوْهُوبِ لَهُ يَنْتَقِلُ الْمِلْكُ إِلَى الْوَرَثَةِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا انْتَقَلَ فِي حَالِ حَيَاتِهِ وَإِذَا مَاتَ الْوَاهِبُ فَوَارِثُهُ أَجْنَبِيٌّ عَنِ الْعَقْدِ اِذْ هُوَ مَا أَوْجَبَهُ أَوْ يَخْرُجَ الْهِبَةُ عَنْ مِلْكِ الْمَوْهُوبِ لَهُ لِأَنَّهُ حَصَلَ بِتَسْلِيطِهِ فَلَا يَنْقُضُهُ وَ لأَنَّهُ يَتَجَدَّدُ الْمِلْكُ بِتَجَدُّدِ سَبَبِهِ. قَالَ وَإِنْ وَهَبَ لِأَخَرَ أَرْضًا بَيْضَاءَ فَأَنْبَتَ فِي نَاحِيَةٍ مِنْهَا نَخْلاً أو بنى بَيْتًا أَوْ دُكَّانًا أو اريَّا وَكَانَ ذَالِكَ زِيَادَةً فِيهَا فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنْهَا لِأَنَّ هَذِهِ زِيَادَةٌ مُتَّصِلَةٌ وَقَوْلُهُ وَكَانَ ذَالِكَ زِيَادَةً فِيْهَا إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى اَنَّ الدُّكَّانَ قَدْ يَكُونُ صَغَيْرًا حَقِيرًا لَا يُعَدُّ زِيَادَةً أَصْلًا
Then there are impediments to revocation, some of which he mentioned: He said: unless the donee compensates him for it, because the purpose is achieved; or the donee makes an inseparable increase (ziyadah muttasilah), because there is no way to revoke the gift without the increase (that being impossible), nor to revoke along with the increase (since it was not part of the contract). He said: or either of the two contracting parties dies; because upon the death of the donee, ownership passes to the heirs, so it becomes like a transfer during his lifetime; and if the donor dies, his heirs are strangers to the contract, since it is not they who made the contract; or the gifted property leaves the donee's ownership, because it was acquired through the donor's empowerment, so [the donee's] act cannot be undone by him, and because ownership is renewed by a new cause. He said: And if one gives another a vacant piece of land, and the donee plants date palms in a part of it, or builds a house, a shop, or a cistern, and that is an increase in it, then the donor cannot revoke any part of it, because this is an inseparable increase; and his saying 'and that is an increase in it' indicates that a shop may be small and insignificant such that it is not considered an increase at all.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This is a ruling statement listing the impediments (mawani') that prevent the donor from revoking a gift. The first impediment is compensation (iwad): if the donee gives something in return, the donor loses the right to revoke because the purpose of the gift (expectation of return) is fulfilled. The second impediment is an inseparable increase (ziyadah muttasilah): if the donee adds something to the gifted property that cannot be separated without damage—like planting trees, building a house, or constructing a shop—then revocation becomes impossible. The donor cannot take back the original item alone because the increase is attached, and taking both is not allowed because the increase was not part of the gift contract. The third impediment is the death of either the donor or the donee. If the donee dies, the property passes to his heirs, making revocation invalid as if the donee had transferred it during his life. If the donor dies, his heirs are not party to the original contract, so they cannot revoke. The fourth impediment is the gifted property leaving the donee's ownership by any other means (e.g., sale, further gift). Since the donee acquired it by the donor's authorization, the donor cannot undo what the donee has done with it; ownership is renewed by a new cause. An example: if the donor gives a vacant land and the donee plants date palms or builds, the donor cannot revoke any part of it. However, if the improvement is trivial (e.g., a very small shop that is not considered an increase), revocation may still be possible for the land itself.

Key Terms
مانع (mani'): An impediment; a legal barrier that prevents the validity of an act (here, revocation).
زیادۃ متصلة (ziyadah muttasilah): An increase physically attached to the gifted property that cannot be separated without damage.
عوض (iwad): Compensation given by the donee in return for the gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT an impediment to revocation of a gift according to the Hanafi school?
A) The donee gives compensation.
B) The donee plants trees on the gifted land.
C) The gifted property remains with the donee unchanged for one year.
D) The donee dies.

Key Takeaway
A gift becomes irrevocable if any of these four impediments is present: compensation, inseparable increase, death, or transfer of ownership.

The Seven Impediments to Gift Revocation (Mawani' al-Ruju' fi al-Hibah)
Enumeration of impediments to gift revocation with legal reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven impediments to gift revocation in Hanafi fiqh and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind each.

Core Idea
Revocation of a gift is blocked by seven impediments — each rooted in the impossibility of undoing what has been altered or transferred.

The Hanafi school recognizes a donor's right to revoke a gift unless specific impediments exist. This passage from Al-Hidayah enumerates these impediments with their legal rationales. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for correctly applying the law of gifts in real cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impediments
List the impediments mentioned in the text: iwad (compensation), ziyadah muttasilah (inseparable increase), death of either party, and the gift leaving the donee's ownership. Note from commentary that the full list is seven, symbolized by the acronym 'دمع خزقه'.
The passage itself mentions four, but the commentary adds three more from other sources.
2
Analyze the ta'lil for each impediment
For each impediment, examine the reason given in the text (e.g., 'because the objective is achieved' for iwad, 'because no way to revoke without increase or with increase' for ziyadah muttasilah). Also note the analogies used.
The reasoning often involves impossibility or change of ownership.
3
Examine the examples
Work through the examples: land with planting or building, and partial sale. Understand how the principle of 'prevention to the extent of the impediment' applies.
The example of an insignificant increase shows that not every addition blocks revocation entirely.
4
Synthesize the full list from commentary
Using the commentary's acronym 'دمع خزقه', list all seven impediments: iwad, ziyadah muttasilah (increase), death (the donor and donee as two), transfer of ownership, and others (change of species, etc.).
The commentary mentions that al-Mabsut gives nine impediments.
5
Apply the principles to a new scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., donor gives a cow, donee sells it), determine if revocation is possible and which impediment applies.
Check each impediment against the facts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ لِلرُجُوعِ مَوَانِعُ ذَكَرَ بَعْضَهَا فَقَالَ: إِلَّا أَنْ يُعَوِضَهُ عَنْهَا لِحُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ، أَوْ يَزِيدَ زِيَادَةً مُتَّصِلَةً لِأَنَّهُ لَا وَجْهَ إِلَى الرُّجُوعِ فِيهَا دُونَ الزِيَادَةِ لِعَدَمِ الْإِمْكَانِ، وَلَا مَعَ الزِيَادَةِ لِعَدَمِ دُخُولِهَا تَحْتَ الْعَقْدِ. قَالَ: أَوْ يَمُوتَ أَحَدُ الْمُتَعَاقِدَيْنِ لِأَنَّ بِمَوْتِ الْمُوْهُوبِ لَهُ يَنْتَقِلُ الْمِلْكُ إِلَى الْوَرَثَةِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا انْتَقَلَ فِي حَالِ حَيَاتِهِ، وَإِذَا مَاتَ الْوَاهِبُ فَوَارِثُهُ أَجْنَبِيٌّ عَنِ الْعَقْدِ إِذْ هُوَ مَا أَوْجَبَهُ. أَوْ يَخْرُجَ الْهِبَةُ عَنْ مِلْكِ الْمَوْهُوبِ لَهُ لِأَنَّهُ حَصَلَ بِتَسْلِيطِهِ فَلَا يَنْقُضُهُ، وَلِأَنَّهُ يَتَجَدَّدُ الْمِلْكُ بِتَجَدُّدِ سَبَبِهِ. قَالَ: وَإِنْ وَهَبَ لِأَخَرَ أَرْضًا بَيْضَاءَ فَأَنْبَتَ فِي نَاحِيَةٍ مِنْهَا نَخْلًا أَوْ بَنَى بَيْتًا أَوْ دُكَّانًا أَوْ أَرِيًّا وَكَانَ ذَلِكَ زِيَادَةً فِيهَا فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنْهَا لِأَنَّ هَذِهِ زِيَادَةٌ مُتَّصِلَةٌ. وَقَوْلُهُ: وَكَانَ ذَلِكَ زِيَادَةً فِيهَا إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّ الدُّكَّانَ قَدْ يَكُونُ صَغِيرًا حَقِيرًا لَا يُعَدُّ زِيَادَةً أَصْلًا، وَقَدْ تَكُونُ الْأَرْضُ عَظِيمَةً يُعَدُّ ذَلِكَ زِيَادَةً فِي قِطْعَةٍ مِنْهَا فَلَا يَمْتَنِعُ الرُّجُوعُ فِي غَيْرِهَا. أَوْ بَاعَ نِصْفَهَا غَيْرَ مَقْسُومٍ رَجَعَ فِي الْبَاقِي لِأَنَّ الْإِمْتِنَاعَ بِقَدَرِ الْمَانِعِ. وَإِنْ لَمْ يَبِعْ شَيْئًا مِنْهَا لَهُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ فِي نِصْفِهَا لِأَنَّ لَهُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ فِي كُلِّهَا فَكَذَا فِي نِصْفِهَا بِالطَّرِيقِ الْأُولَى.

ترجمہ: پھر رجوع کے لئے کچھ موانع ہیں جن میں سے بعض کو ذکر کیا ہے۔ پس کہا ہے مگر یہ کہ اس کا عوض دے دیا ہو۔ حصول مقصود کی وجہ سے یا موہوب میں کوئی زیادتی متصل ہوگئی ہو کیونکہ زیادتی کے بغیر موہوب میں رجوع کی کوئی وجہ نہیں۔ ممکن نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور نہ زیادتی کے ساتھ کیونکہ یہ زیادتی تحت العقد داخل نہیں۔ یا متعاقدین میں سے کوئی مرجائے اسلئے کہ موہوب لہ کے مرنے سے ملک ورثہ کی طرف منتقل ہوگئی تو ایسا ہوا جیسے اس کی زندگی میں منتقل ہو گئی ہو اور جب واہب مر گیا تو اس کا وارث عقد ہبہ سے اجنبی ہے کیونکہ اس نے عقد نہیں کیا تھا۔ یا ہبہ ملک موہوب لہ سے نکل جائے کیونکہ یہ واہب کے مسلط کرنے سے ہوا تو وہ اس کو تو نہیں سکتا۔ اور اسلئے کہ سبب کے جدید ہونے سے ملک بھی جدید ہو جاتی ہے۔ اگر کسی نے دوسرے کو خالی زمین سبد کی پس موہوب لہ نے اس کے کنارے درخت خرمالگایا یا گھر بنایا یا کان بنائی یا جانور کا تھان بنایا اور حال یہ کہ زمین میں زیادتی ہے تو اس کے کسی حصہ میں رجوع نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ یہ زیادتی متصلہ ہے اور کتاب میں یہ کہنا کہ یہ زمین میں زیادتی ہے اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ دکان کبھی ایسی چھوٹی حقیر ہوتی ہے کہ اس کو کچھ بھی زیادتی شمار نہیں کیا جاتا اور کبھی زمین ایسی وسیع ہوتی ہے کہ یہ زیادتی اس کے ایک ٹکڑے میں شمار ہوتی ہے تو باقی میں رجوع ممتنع نہ ہوگا۔ اگر موہوب لہ نے نصف زمین غیر مقسوم فروخت کر دی تو واہب باقی زمین میں رجوع کرسکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ ممتنع ہونا تو بقدر مانع ہے اور اگر کچھ بھی زمین فروخت نہیں کی تو آدھی میں رجوع کر سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جب اس کو کل پھیر لینے کا اختیار ہے تو آدھی پھیر لینا بطریق اولی جائز ہوگا۔

تشریح: قوله ثم للرجوع.. الخ ہبہ میں رجوع کرنے سے سات امور مانع ہوتے ہیں جن کو صاحب کنز نے مجموعہ (ومع خزقہ) کے حروف سے ظاہر کیا ہے اور یہ مجموعہ شاعر کے اس شعر سے ماخوذ ہے: وما نع عن الرجوع فى الهبة * یا صاحبی حروف دمع خزقه مجموعہ کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اس کو آنسو نے زخمی کر ڈالا۔ خزق بمعنی طعن ہے۔ پس شاعر نے آنسو کو برچھی کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی ہے۔ مبسوط خواہر زادہ میں نو موانع مذکور ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ موت میں دو صورتیں داخل ہیں ایک واہب کی موت اور ایک موہوب لہ کی موت اور نواں مانع ایک جنس سے دوسری جنس کی طرف تغیر ہے۔ قوله الا ان يعوض (1) مجموعہ کے حرف عین سے مراد عوض ہے جو ہند کے بدلہ میں موہوب لہ واہب کو دے کہ واہب رجوع نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ مقصود حاصل ہو گیا۔ لیکن شرط یہ ہے کہ وہ اس کی اضافت ہبہ کی طرف کرے۔ مثلاً موہوب لہ واہب سے کہے کہ یہ چیز اپنے ہبہ کا عوض ہے یا اس کا بدلہ یا اس کے مقابلہ میں لے لے اور واہب اس پر قبضہ کرے تو حق رجوع ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر کوئی اجنبی شخص موہوب لہ کی طرف سے واہب کے ہبہ کا عوض دے دے تب بھی حق رجوع ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ قوله اويزيد زيادة ... (2) مجموعہ مذکورہ میں حرف دال سے نفس شئی موہوب میں زیادہ متصلہ کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ اگر عین موہوب میں کوئی ایسی زیادتی متصل ہو گئی جس سے اس کی قیمت بڑھ گئی۔ مثلاً موہوب زمین تھی موہوب لہ نے اس میں عمارت بنالی یا درخت لگا دیئے یا موہوب لہ نے اسے کھلا پلا کر فربہ کرلیا تو اس صورت میں واہب رجوع نہیں کر سکتا۔ اس لئے کہ اگر وہ زیادتی کے بغیر رجوع کرنا چاہے تو یہ ممکن نہیں کیونکہ فربہی کو دور کرنا اس کے بس کی بات نہیں اور اگر زیادتی کے ساتھ رجوع کرنا چاہے تو یہ بھی نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ زیادتی عقد ہبہ میں داخل نہیں۔
Then for revocation there are impediments, some of which he mentioned: he said: Unless (the donee) gives him compensation for it, because the objective is achieved; or (the donee) makes an inseparable increase, because there is no way to revoke the gift without the increase due to impossibility, nor with the increase because it is not included under the contract. He said: Or one of the contracting parties dies, because by the death of the donee, ownership transfers to the heirs, so it is as if it transferred during his lifetime, and when the donor dies, his heir is a stranger to the contract since he did not make it. Or the gift leaves the ownership of the donee, because it was acquired by his (the donor's) empowerment, so he cannot undo it, and because ownership is renewed with the renewal of its cause. He said: And if he gave another a barren land, and (the donee) planted date palms in one part of it, or built a house, or a shop, or a beehive, and that was an increase in it, then he cannot revoke any part of it because this is an inseparable increase. And his statement 'and that was an increase in it' indicates that a shop may be small and insignificant, not considered an increase at all, and sometimes the land is vast and that is considered an increase in one part of it, so revocation is not prevented in other parts. Or if he sold half of it undivided, he revokes the remainder because the prevention is to the extent of the impediment. And if he did not sell anything from it, he can revoke half of it because he can revoke all of it, so likewise he can revoke half of it by even stronger reason.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, listing the impediments (mawani') that prevent the donor from revoking a gift. The text enumerates several impediments: (1) compensation (iwad) given by the donee, because the donor's objective is fulfilled; (2) an inseparable increase (ziyadah muttasilah) made by the donee, such as planting trees or building a structure, as it is impossible to revoke without the increase and the increase is not part of the original contract; (3) death of either party — if the donee dies, ownership passes to heirs, so revocation is blocked; if the donor dies, his heir is not party to the original contract; (4) the gift leaving the donee's ownership (e.g., sale, another gift), because the donee's ownership was acquired with the donor's consent. The text then gives examples: if a barren land was gifted and the donee plants trees or builds, the donor cannot revoke any part if the addition is considered an increase in the whole land. However, if the shop is insignificant or the land is vast such that the addition only affects a portion, revocation is possible in the rest. The passage also covers partial sale: if half of an undivided land is sold, the donor can revoke the remaining half; if nothing is sold, he can still revoke half (since he can revoke all, so half is a fortiori). The commentary further explains that there are seven impediments in total, symbolized by the acronym 'دمع خزقه' (from a poem), with 'ع' for 'iwad, 'د' for 'ziyadah muttasilah, etc. Some sources mention nine impediments including death of donor and donee separately and change from one species to another.

Key Terms
مانع (mani'): An impediment that prevents the legal right to revoke a gift.
زیادت متصل (ziyadah muttasilah): An inseparable increase physically attached to the gifted property, such as a building or plantation.
عوض (iwad): Compensation given by the donee to the donor as a substitute for the gift, which removes the right to revoke.
رجوع (ruju'): The legal act of a donor taking back a gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A donor gives a piece of land. The donee sells half of the undivided land to a third party. Can the donor revoke the remaining half?
A) No, revocation is blocked entirely because the donee sold part.
B) Yes, because the prevention is only to the extent of the impediment; the donor can revoke the unsold half.
C) Yes, but only if the donor compensates the buyer.
D) No, because the sale transfers ownership to a third party and revocation is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The right to revoke a gift is not absolute; it is blocked by seven well-defined impediments rooted in legal impossibility and changed circumstances.

Revocation of Gift After Partial Sale or Inseparable Increment
States when donor may revoke a gift after partial sale or inseparable increment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-imtina' bi-qadr al-mani'' to determine the donor's right to revoke a gift when part of the property is sold or an inseparable increment is added.

Core Idea
Prevention exists only to the extent of the obstacle: partial sale blocks revocation only in the sold portion.

This passage from the matn addresses a common scenario: after a gift, the recipient sells half of the undivided property or adds an increment. When can the donor revoke? The answer lies in the precise application of the maxim 'al-imtina' bi-qadr al-mani'' — the obstacle prevents only to its own extent. Understanding this principle is central to Hanafi gift law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the obstacle
The act is the donor's revocation of a gift. The obstacles are the sale of half of the undivided property or addition of an inseparable increment.
The gift is assumed to be revocable (non-mahram, no counter-gift).
2
State the maxim applied
The passage relies on the maxim 'al-imtina' bi-qadr al-mani'' — prevention exists only to the extent of the obstacle. The obstacle (sale or increment) only blocks revocation where it occurs.
3
Apply the maxim to the sale of half
If half is sold, the sale prevents revocation only in that sold half. Therefore, the donor may revoke the unsold half.
The ruling uses 'wa la ghayr maqsum' meaning the gift is undivided at the time of sale.
4
Apply a fortiori reasoning (al-tariq al-ula)
If the donor may revoke the entire gift (when no obstacle exists), then revoking half is even more permissible. This is an a fortiori (qiyas jaliy) argument.
The text states: 'because he may revoke all of it, so likewise half of it by even stronger inference.'
5
Apply the maxim to inseparable increment
If the land is large and the recipient adds an inseparable increment (like a building) only in a specific portion, that increment is considered confined to that portion. The donor may revoke the rest, as the obstacle is limited.
Custom ('urf) and the nature of the property determine whether the increment is considered confined to a part or extends to the whole.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا غَيْرَ مَقْسُوْمٍ رَجَعَ فِي الْبَاقِي لِاَنَّ الْاِمْتِنَاعَ بِقَدَرِ الْمَانِعِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَبِعْ شَيْئًا مِنْهَا لَهُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ فِي نِصْفِهَا لِأَنَّ لَهُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ فِي كُلِّهَا فَكَذَا فِي نِصْفِهَا بِالطَّرِيقِ الْأُولَى وَقَدْ تَكُونُ الْأَرْضُ عَظِيمَةٌ يُعَدُّ ذَالِكَ زِيَادَة فِى قِطْعَةٍ مِنهَا فَلَا يَمْتَنِعِ الرَّجُوع فى غيرِها
And [if] half of undivided [gift] is sold, he revokes in the remainder because the prevention is to the extent of the obstacle. And if he did not sell anything from it, he may revoke half of it because he may revoke all of it, so likewise half of it by even stronger inference. And the land may be large such that that [increment] is counted as an increment in a portion of it, so revocation is not prevented in the rest.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn (likely Al-Hidayah) about the donor's right to revoke a gift when part of the undivided gift has been sold by the recipient. The ruling is based on the principle that prevention exists only to the extent of the obstacle (al-imtina' bi-qadr al-mani'). If the recipient sells half of an undivided gift, the donor can revoke the remaining half because the sale prevents revocation only in that sold portion. If the recipient sells nothing, the donor can revoke even half, because having the right to revoke the whole implies the right to revoke half (a fortiori argument). The passage also addresses a nuance: if the land is very large and the recipient adds an inseparable increment (like a building) only in one part, that increment is considered confined to that part, so revocation is not prevented in the rest of the land. This shows the Hanafi principle of precision in applying the obstacle based on custom and extent.

Key Terms
غَيْرَ مَقْسُوْمٍ (ghayr maqsum): Undivided; where the portion sold is not physically separated from the rest
الْاِمْتِنَاعَ بِقَدَرِ الْمَانِعِ (al-imtina' bi-qadr al-mani'): A legal maxim: prevention exists only to the extent of the obstacle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the recipient sells half of an undivided gifted land, what can the donor revoke?
A) The entire land
B) Half of the land
C) The remaining half
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the donor's right to revoke a gift is only prevented to the extent of the obstacle, not beyond.

The Seven Obstacles to Revocation of Gift
Lists seven obstacles preventing revocation of gift with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven major obstacles to revocation of a gift in Hanafi fiqh and explain the legal reasoning why each prevents revocation.

Core Idea
Seven obstacles permanently block the donor's right to revoke a gift.

In Hanafi law, a donor normally has the right to revoke a gift after delivery unless one of seven specific obstacles exists. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah lists those obstacles with commentary, clarifying how each changes the legal status of the gift. Understanding these obstacles is essential for correctly applying the rules of gift revocation in daily transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify each obstacle from the matn
The commentary extracts seven obstacles from the mnemonic 'دمع خزقة'. List each as: 1) عوض (compensation), 2) زيادة متصلة (inseparable increment), 3) موت أحد المتعاقدين (death of either party), 4) خروج الملك (exit from ownership), and the additional ones: تغير من جنس إلى جنس (change of genus), and others as mentioned.
The mnemonic is a memory aid; focus on the legal effect of each.
2
Understand the reasoning behind each obstacle
For each obstacle, the commentator gives the reason why it stops revocation. For example, an inseparable increment (building or planting) is not included in the original gift contract, so revoking the land would cause the donor to own the increment without the donee's consent.
Note the distinction between separable and inseparable increments.
3
Apply the principle to the half-sale case
The text gives an example: if the donee sells half of an undivided gift, the donor can revoke the remaining half. This illustrates that the obstacle (exit from ownership) only applies to the part sold; the unsold part remains revocable.
This is an application of the maxim 'al-imtina' bi-qadr al-mani'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله الا ان يعوض ... قوله او يزيد زيادة متصلة ... قوله او يموت احد المتعاقدين ... قوله او يخرج الملك ... ولو وهب لآخر أرضا خرابا فغرس فيها الموهوب له نخلا أو بنى دارا أو حانوتا أو اصطبل دواب وكان ذلك زيادة فيها لم يرجع في شيء منها ... فان باع نصفها غير مقسوم رجع في الباقي ...
He said: Unless he gives compensation... He said: Or an inseparable increment occurs... He said: Or one of the two contracting parties dies... He said: Or the property leaves ownership... And if he gifted to another a barren land and the donee planted date palms in it or built a house or a shop or a stable, and that was an increment in it, he cannot revoke any part of it... So if he sold half of it undivided, he revokes in the remainder...
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn's brief listing of obstacles to revocation (mawani' al-ruju') in the gift contract. The commentator (Ashraf ul Hadaya) explains each obstacle as derived from the matn's concise text, using the mnemonic 'دمع خزقة' (the letters of which spell the obstacles). The seven obstacles are: 1) Compensation (عوض) – if the donee gives something in return for the gift, the donor cannot revoke because the purpose is achieved. 2) Inseparable increment (زيادة متصلة) – if the donee adds something that becomes part of the gift (e.g., planting trees, building), revocation is prevented because the increment is not part of the original contract. 3) Death of either party (موت احد المتعاقدين) – if the donee dies, the gift passes to heirs; if the donor dies, the heirs are strangers to the contract. 4) Exit from ownership (خروج الملك) – if the donee sells or gives away the item, the donor cannot revoke because the property is now owned by a third party through a new title. Another obstacle mentioned is change of genus (تغير من جنس إلى جنس) – e.g., grinding wheat into flour. The commentary also discusses the nuance of an increment on a large land: if the land is vast and the increment is only in a portion, the donor may revoke the rest. The half-sale case illustrates the principle 'al-imtina' bi-qadr al-mani'. This is a clear exposition of Hanafi law on the limits of the donor's right of revocation.

Key Terms
زيادة متصلة (ziyada muttasila): An increment that becomes physically attached to the gifted property, like building or planting.
خروج الملك (khuruj al-milk): Exit of the gifted item from the donee's ownership, e.g., by sale or gift.
عوض (iwad): Compensation given by the donee in return for the gift, which makes the contract binding.
موت أحد المتعاقدين (mawt ahad al-muta'aqidayn): Death of either the donor or the donee.
تغير من جنس إلى جنس (taghayyur min jins ila jins): Change of the gifted item's genus, e.g., grinding wheat into flour.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT an obstacle to revocation of gift?
A) The donee pays compensation to the donor
B) The donee builds a house on the gifted land
C) The gifted item appreciates in market value
D) The donee sells the gifted item to a third party

Key Takeaway
Revocation of a gift is permanently blocked by seven specific obstacles; the most common are inseparable increments and transfer of ownership.

Revocation of Gift After Death or Transfer of Ownership
Explains when revocation is prohibited after death or disposal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which revocation of a gift is prohibited according to the Hanafi school, and explain the principle of ownership transfer.

Core Idea
Revocation is blocked when ownership transfers due to death or when the donee disposes of the item.

In Hanafi fiqh, a donor may generally revoke a gift before possession or under certain conditions. However, this passage from al-Hidayah clarifies two absolute bars: the death of either the donor or donee, and the donee's disposal of the gifted item. Understanding these barriers is essential for applying gift law correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being regulated
The act is revocation (ruju') of a gift (hiba). The passage specifies when it is not permissible.
Revocation is the donor's claim to reclaim the gifted property.
2
List the two prohibited scenarios
First: death of either the donor or the donee. Second: the gifted item leaves the donee's ownership (e.g., sold or gifted to a third party).
These are explicitly mentioned with Arabic letters 'mim' and 'kha'.
3
Analyze the rationale for each
For death: if donee dies, ownership transfers to heirs; if donor dies, heirs are strangers to the contract. For disposal: new ownership through a valid contract severs the donor's right.
The key principle is that revocation is possible only while the item remains in the donee's ownership.
4
Apply the principle to a new case
Consider: donor gives a book, donee dies. Revocation is barred after death. Consider: donee sells the book to a third party. Revocation is barred after sale.
Transfer of ownership is the common thread.
5
Note the practical implication
Donors must act quickly if they wish to revoke, before death or disposal. Heirs cannot revoke gifts made by the deceased.
This protects the stability of property transactions.

His statement: 'or one of the two contracting parties dies' ... (3) In the aforementioned compilation, the letter 'mim' refers to the death of one of the two contracting parties, i.e., the donor or the donee, indicating that revocation is not permissible even in the case of death. Because if the donee dies, ownership transfers to his heirs, so just as after the transfer of ownership during his lifetime revocation is not permissible, similarly in the case of transfer after death revocation will not be permissible. And if the donor dies, his heirs are purely strangers with respect to the gift contract. His statement: 'or it goes out' ... (4) In the compilation, the letter 'kha' refers to the gifted item leaving the possession of the donee. For example, the donee sells it or gives it as a gift to someone else, then the donor cannot revoke. Also, when a new cause of ownership arises, ownership becomes new. For example, when the donee sold the gifted item, the buyer acquired new ownership through the sale. So the donor cannot break it.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on al-Hidayah, explaining two instances where revocation of a gift (hiba) is prohibited. The first is the death of either the donor or donee. If the donee dies, ownership transfers to his heirs, and revocation is blocked because the property is no longer in the donee's possession. If the donor dies, his heirs cannot revoke because they are considered strangers to the original gift contract. The second instance is when the gifted item leaves the donee's possession through sale or gift to a third party. Once a new ownership is established via a valid contract (like sale), the donor's right to revoke is lost. This is based on the principle that revocation is only possible while the item remains in the donee's ownership.

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): The legal act of the donor reclaiming the gifted property, revoking the gift.
ملک (milk): Ownership or proprietary right over the gifted item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the donor agreed to the sale
D) Because the item has been consumed

Key Takeaway
Revocation of a gift is prohibited once ownership transfers due to death or disposal, as the donor's right is tied to the item remaining in the donee's ownership.

Prohibition of Revoking Gifts to Mahram Relatives and Spouses
Commentary on a gift revocation rule with hadith proof and critical defense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on revoking gifts to mahram relatives and spouses, explain the basis in the hadith, and distinguish the timing condition for spousal gifts.

Core Idea
A gift to a mahram relative or spouse cannot be revoked because the purpose of sila rahmi is achieved at the moment of the gift.

This lesson explains why certain gifts become irrevocable in Hanafi fiqh. When a gift is given to a relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (mahram) or to one's spouse, the law presumes the intention was to strengthen family ties. Once that purpose is fulfilled by the contract, revocation is no longer permitted. We will examine the textual evidence and address objections to the supporting hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the ruling: a gift to a mahram relative or to a spouse (if given during marriage) is irrevocable.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith: 'If a gift is given to a mahram relative, one cannot revoke it' (narrated by Hakim and Daraqutni from Samurah ibn Jundub).
The hadith is ahad, but the commentators defend its authenticity.
3
Analyze the basis
Understand the reasoning: the purpose of sila rahmi is achieved at the time of the gift, so the contract cannot be annulled.
This is an application of the legal maxim that a contract whose purpose is fulfilled cannot be rescinded.
4
Examine the spousal exception
Note the timing condition: if a gift is given to a woman before marriage, the donor can revoke after marriage; if given during marriage, revocation is prohibited.
The marital relationship at the time of the gift is decisive.
5
Evaluate the hadith criticism
Review the commentator's defense: he refutes claims of weakness by distinguishing narrators and citing scholars like al-Hakim, al-Dhahabi, and Ibn Hajar who consider the hadith sound.
Understanding jarh wa ta'dil (criticism and verification of narrators) strengthens the proof.

Thus, if a man married a woman after having given her a gift, he has the option to revoke. But if he divorced her after the gift, he cannot revoke. Commentary on His saying: 'And if he gave a gift...' (5) In the aforementioned collection, the letter Qaf refers to mahram kinship, i.e., such kinship that makes marriage prohibited. So if one gives a gift to a mahram relative, he cannot revoke it. The three Imams also hold this view. Because Hakim al-Bayyi' and al-Daraqutni narrated marfu'an from Samurah ibn Jundub: 'If a gift is given to a mahram relative, one cannot revoke it.' Also because the purpose of the gift is sila rahmi, which has been achieved. And a contract whose purpose has been achieved cannot be annulled. Thus one cannot revoke. And because the purpose is sila rahmi and it has been achieved. Similarly is the case where one spouse gives to the other. Note: The hadith of Samurah was considered defective by Ibn al-Jawzi because of Abdullah ibn Ja'far, and he said it is weak. But the author of Tanqih corrected Ibn al-Jawzi, saying this is wrong. Rather, Abdullah ibn Ja'far is a trustworthy narrator from the narrators of the two Sahihs, and all the narrators of this hadith are trustworthy, and this Abdullah ibn Ja'far is the one from Rayy. The weak one is Ali ibn al-Madini's father, Abdullah ibn Ja'far al-Madini, who earlier passed away from Rayy. Therefore, al-Hakim considered this hadith to meet the condition of Bukhari, and al-Dhahabi in al-Talkhis affirmed it. Also in Talkhis al-Jabir, Ibn Hajar remained silent. Question: Al-Daraqutni said that Abdullah ibn Ja'far is unique in narrating this hadith, and the author of Tanqih called the hadith munkar. Answer: Uniqueness does not make it weak, and there is no reason for it to be munkar because Abdullah ibn Ja'far does not contradict more trustworthy narrators. Because the prohibition of revocation in gift is related to piety. So if one revokes, the ruling is established, even though his example is like a dog that returns to its vomit. Question: Al-Bayhaqi said that this hadith was narrated by Hasan al-Basri from Samurah ibn Jundub, but there is dispute about whether he met Samurah. Answer: According to the majority, his hearing is established. Even al-Bukhari considered the hadith of Hasan from Samurah as evidence, as al-Bayhaqi himself clarified in the selling chapters of his Sunan. So it is surprising that al-Bayhaqi accepts narrations when they agree with him but declares them weak when they contradict him. His saying: 'And likewise what is given as a gift...' (2) In the collection, the letter Za refers to the existence of a marital relationship between donor and donee at the time of the gift. So if one gives a gift to a non-mahram woman and then marries her, he can revoke because the marital relationship did not exist at the time of the gift. But if he gives a gift to his wife and then divorces her, he cannot revoke because the purpose of all this is also sila rahmi, and this is achieved at the time of the gift. The three Imams hold this view.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn regarding revocation of gifts in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by explaining the principle that the purpose of a gift determines whether revocation is allowed. If the gift is intended to strengthen family ties (sila rahmi), then once that purpose is achieved, revocation is prohibited. The commentator then addresses two specific cases: gifts to mahram relatives and gifts between spouses. For mahram relatives, revocation is not allowed based on a hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub narrated by Hakim and Daraqutni, which states that a gift to a mahram relative cannot be revoked. The commentator defends the authenticity of this hadith against criticisms by Ibn al-Jawzi and al-Bayhaqi, citing scholars like Ibn Hajar and al-Dhahabi who consider it sound. For gifts between spouses, the ruling depends on the timing of the marital relationship. If a gift is given to a woman before marriage, the donor can revoke after marriage, but if given during marriage and then divorce occurs, revocation is not allowed because the purpose of strengthening ties was already achieved. All three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on these rulings.

Key Terms
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood relation (e.g., mother, sister, daughter).
صلہ رحمی (sila rahmi): Maintaining family ties and strengthening kinship relationships.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A gift to a mahram relative or spouse during the relationship is irrevocable because the purpose of strengthening family ties is achieved immediately.

Effect of Compensation on Revocation and Partial Reclaim
Explains how compensation affects revocation and handles partial reclaim with an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule regarding revocation after compensation, distinguish the majority position from Imam Zufar's view on partial reclaim, and apply the rule to scenarios of partial reclamation.

Core Idea
Accepting compensation for a gift forfeits revocation; but if the compensation is partially reclaimed, the donor must return the remainder to revoke the whole gift.

This lesson examines the interaction between compensation ('iwad) and the right of revocation (ruju') in gifts. The core principle is that once a donor accepts compensation, the right to revoke the gift is extinguished because the purpose of the gift—to receive something in return—is achieved. However, complications arise when part of the compensation or part of the gifted property is reclaimed by a third party. The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, provides detailed rules for such partial-reclaim scenarios, disagreeing with Imam Zufar on two key points: whether the donor may revoke the gift proportionally without returning the remaining compensation, and whether compensation may be taken from the gifted item itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
When does compensation forfeit the right of revocation? Identify the conditions: the donee must clearly state the compensation is for the gift, the donor must understand this, and the donor must take possession. If these are met, revocation is prohibited.
This applies even if compensation is from a third party voluntarily.
2
Examine partial-reclaim scenarios
Two cases: (a) half the gift is reclaimed → donor takes back half the compensation. (b) half the compensation is reclaimed → donor cannot revoke the gift unless he returns the remaining compensation to the donee, then he may revoke the entire gift.
Case (b) is the point of dispute.
3
Contrast Imam Zufar's view
Imam Zufar allows the donor to revoke half the gift directly without returning the remaining compensation, by analogy with other compensation cases. He also permits compensation from a part of the gifted item itself.
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) reject both.
4
Analyse the majority's proof
The remaining compensation was initially for the whole gift; the reclaim shows full delivery failed. The donor only dropped his right to full delivery, so he may choose to return the remainder and revoke the whole gift.
The text states 'لنا' to signal the majority's proof.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Given a scenario with partial reclaim of compensation, determine the correct outcome under the mufta bihi position.
Focus on the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text

قَالَ وَإِذَا قَالَ الْمُؤهُوبُ لَهُ لِلْوَاهِبِ خُذْ هَذَا عِوَضًا عَنْ هَبَتِكَ اَوْ بَدَلًا عَنْهَا أوْ فِي مُقَابَلَتِهَا فَقَبَضَهُ الْوَاهِبُ سَقَطَ الرُّجُوعُ لِحُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ وَهَذِهِ الْعِبَارَاتُ تُؤَذِى مَعْنَى وَاحِدًا وَإِنْ عَوَّضَهُ أَجْنَبِيٌّ عَنِ الْمُؤْهُوبِ لَهُ مُتَبَرَعًا فَقَبَضَ الْوَاهِبُ الْعِوَضَ بَطَلَ الرُّجُوعُ لِاَنَّ الْعِوَضَ لِإِسْقَاطِ الْحَقِ فَيَصِحُ يَرْجِعُ فِي الْهِبَةِ إِلَّا إِنْ يَرُدَّ مَا بَقِى ثُمَّ يَرْجِعُ وَقَالَ زُفَرُ يَرْجِعُ بِالنِّصْفِ اِعْتِبَارًا بِالْعِوَضِ الْآخَرِ وَلَنَا أنَّهُ يَصْلُحُ عِوَضًا لِلْكُلَّ فِي الْابْتِدَاءِ وَبِالْإِسْتِحْقَاقِ ظَهَرَ أَنَّهُ لَا عِوَضَ إِلَّا هُوَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يُتَخَيَّرُ لِأَنَّهُ مَا أَسْقَطَ حَقَّهُ في الرُّجُوعِ إِلَّا لِيُسَلَّمَ لَهُ كُلَّ الْعِوَضِ فَلَمْ يُسَلَّمَ لَهُ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَرُدَّهُ. قَالَ وَإِنْ وَهَبَ دَارًا فَعَوَّضَهُ مِنْ نِصْفِهَا رَجَعَ الواهب فى النصف الذى لم يُعوّض لأنَّ الْمَانِعَ خَصَّ البَصْفَ. ترجمہ جب کہا موہوب لہ نے واہب سے کہ لے لے یہ عوض اپنے ہبہ کی طرف ت سلوک کے طور پر اور واہب نے عوض لے لیا تو حق رجوع ساقط ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ عوض تو اسقاط حق کے لئے ہوتا ہے تو یہ اجنبی کی طرف سے بھی صحیح ہو کا جیسے ضلع اور صلح کا عوض جب کوئی حق دار نکل آئے نصف ہبہ کا تو والیکی لے لے نصف عوض ۔ کیونکہ موہوب لہ کے لئے وہ سالم نہیں رہا جو نصف عوض کے مقابل ہو اور اگر حقدار انکل آئے نصف عوض کا تو نہ واپس لے نہیہ میں سے مگر یہ کہ لوٹا دے وہ باقی عوض پھر واپس لے اپنا
