لفظ ذکر کیا جس سے واہب یہ سمجھ سکتا ہے کہ یہ اس کے مہبہ کا عوض ہے ۔ مثلا موہوب لہ نے اس سے کہا۔ خذهذا عوضا عن هبتك يا كها جزاء هيبتك يا كباثواب هبتك، يا كها بدل هبتك يا كباخذ هذا عوضًافي مقابله هبتك ، اور واہب نے اس پر قبضہ کر لیا تو حق رجوع ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ خواہ وہ عوض قلیل ہو یا کثیر، جنس ہبہ سے ہو خلاف جنس سے ہو اس لئے کہ یہ معاوضہ محضہ نہیں ہے۔ تو اس میں کمی بیشی سے ربوا متحقق نہ ہوگا۔ البتہ عوض میں شروط ہب قبض و افراز وغیرہ کا لحاظ ضر ور ہے گا۔ سقوط حق رجوع کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ واہب کا مقصد جو عوض پانا تھا وہ حاصل ہو گیا مذکورہ تمام الفاظ مکافات ردال ہیں۔ لہذار جوع کا حق ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ ہاں اگر واہب کو یہ معلوم نہ ہو کہ میرے مہیبہ کا عوض ہے تو واہب کو اپنے ہبہ میں اور موہوب لہ کو اپنے عوض میں رجوع کا اختیار رہے گا۔ نیز یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ عوض شئی موہوب کے علاوہ سے ہو۔ اگر موہوب ہی کا کچھ حصہ عوض میں دیا مثلاً موہوب ہزار درہم تھے۔ انہیں میں سے کچھ درہم عوض کے طور پر دیئے یا موہوب ایک گھر تھا اور اس کا ایک کمرہ عوض میں دے دیا تو یہ جائز نہ ہوگا۔ وعند زفر یجوز۔
He said: And when the donee says to the donor, 'Take this as compensation for your gift, or as a substitute for it, or in exchange for it,' and the donor takes possession of it, the right of revocation falls because the purpose is achieved. These expressions all convey the same meaning. And if a third party, voluntarily, compensates the donee's behalf, and the donor takes possession of the compensation, the right of revocation becomes void because the compensation is for the purpose of dropping the right, so it is valid from a third party, like the compensation in khul' and sulh. And if half of the gift is reclaimed, the donor takes back half of the compensation because that which corresponds to half is not delivered to him. And if half of the compensation is reclaimed, he does not revoke the gift unless he returns what remains, then he revokes. Zufar said: He revokes half, by analogy with the other compensation. Our argument is that the remaining compensation is valid as compensation for the whole initially, and by the reclaim it becomes clear that there is no compensation except that which remains, except that he has a choice because he did not drop his right of revocation except to have the entire compensation delivered to him. Since it is not delivered, he may return it. He said: And if he gave a house as a gift, and then was compensated for half of it, the donor revokes the half for which he was not compensated, because the impediment is specific to the half. Translation: When the donee said to the donor, 'Take this as compensation for your gift, or its substitute, or in exchange for it,' and the donor took possession, the right of revocation fell due to the achievement of the purpose. All these expressions convey the same meaning. And if a third party gave compensation on behalf of the donee voluntarily, and the donor took it, the right of revocation fell because compensation is for dropping the right, so it is valid from a third party, like compensation in khul' and sulh. When a rightful claimant appears to half the gift, the donor takes back half the compensation because the corresponding half was not delivered to him. And if a rightful claimant appears to half the compensation, he does not revoke the gift from it unless he returns the remaining compensation then revokes. Imam Zufar says: He can revoke half, by analogy with the other compensation. Our evidence is that the remaining compensation is valid as compensation for the whole initially, but by the reclaim it becomes clear that there is no compensation except that remaining, though the donor is given a choice because he did not drop his right of revocation except for the entire compensation to be delivered to him. Since it is not delivered, he may return it. If a house is gifted, and compensation is given for half of it, the donor can revoke the half for which no compensation was given, because the impediment is specific to the half. Commentary on His saying: 'And when the donee says...' The donee, when giving compensation to the donor for his gift, used a word from which the donor understands that it is compensation for his gift. For example, the donee said to him: 'Take this as compensation for your gift, or as recompense for your gift, or as reward for your gift, or as a substitute for your gift, or take this as compensation in exchange for your gift.' And the donor took possession, then the right of revocation falls, whether the compensation is small or large, of the same genus as the gift or not, because this is not a pure exchange, so no riba occurs from discrepancy. However, conditions like possession and segregation must be observed. The reason for the fall of the right of revocation is that the donor's purpose of obtaining compensation has been achieved. All the mentioned phrases are words of recompense and return. Therefore the right of revocation falls. However, if the donor did not know that it was compensation for his gift, then the donor retains the option to revoke his gift and the donee retains the option to revoke his compensation. Also it is necessary that the compensation be something other than the gifted object. If part of the gifted object itself is given as compensation, e.g., the gift was a thousand dirhams and some dirhams from them were given as compensation, or the gift was a house and one room was given as compensation, then it is not valid. According to Zufar, it is valid.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn regarding the effect of compensation ('iwad) on the right of revocation in a gift. The author explains that when a donee offers compensation to the donor in clear terms (like 'take this as compensation for your gift') and the donor accepts and takes possession, the donor's right to revoke the gift is forfeited because the purpose of obtaining compensation has been achieved. This applies even if a third party offers compensation on behalf of the donee voluntarily. The text then discusses partial reclaim scenarios: if half of the gifted property is rightfully reclaimed from the donee, the donor can take back half of the compensation. If half of the compensation is reclaimed, the donor cannot revoke the gift without first returning the remaining compensation. Imam Zufar disagrees and says the donor can revoke half of the gift directly, by analogy with other types of compensation. The Hanafi position (of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) is that the donor has a choice to either keep the remaining compensation or return it and revoke the entire gift. Finally, the text discusses a case where compensation is given for only part of the gift: the donor can revoke the part for which no compensation was given. The commentary also clarifies conditions for valid compensation: the donor must understand it is for the gift, the compensation must be from outside the gifted item, and possession/segregation rules apply. Imam Zufar permits compensation from a part of the gifted item itself, but the majority Hanafi view prohibits it.

Key Terms
عوض ('iwad): Compensation given in exchange for a gift, which forfeits the donor's right of revocation.
استحقاق (istihqaq): A rightful claim by a third party that causes part of the gifted property or compensation to be taken back.
رجوع (ruju'): The donor's right to take back the gifted item; this right is forfeited upon acceptance of compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (excluding Zufar), if half of the compensation for a gift is reclaimed, what must the donor do to revoke the entire gift?
A) Revoke half the gift without returning anything.
B) Revoke the entire gift without returning anything.
C) Return the remaining compensation then revoke the entire gift.
D) He cannot revoke under any circumstances.

Key Takeaway
Receiving full compensation forfeits revocation; partial reclaim of compensation does not allow proportional revocation—the donor must return the remainder to revoke the whole gift.

Donee's Explicit Compensation Drops Donor's Right to Revoke Gift
Ruling on donee offering compensation using explicit terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which explicit compensation from the donee drops the donor's right to revoke a gift, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding compensation from the gifted item itself.

Core Idea
Explicit compensation from the donee extinguishes the donor's right to revoke, but compensation must be from outside the gifted property.

When a donee gives the donor something in return for the gift, using clear words like 'take this as compensation,' and the donor accepts, the donor's right to take back the gift is lost. However, this ruling depends on specific conditions, including that the compensation comes from a separate source. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its conditions, and a minority view from Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its primary effect
Recognize that the donee's explicit offer of compensation using words like 'iwad', 'badal', or 'fi muqabil' causes the donor's right to revoke to fall when the donor takes possession.
The key is the explicit link (ta'līq) between the compensation and the gift.
2
List the conditions for the right to fall
Extract from the passage the conditions: (1) explicit wording, (2) donor takes possession, (3) donor knows it is compensation for the gift, (4) compensation is from property other than the gifted item.
Imam Zufar disagrees on the fourth condition.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi difference
Note that Imam Zufar permits compensation from the gifted item itself, but the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) reject it. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
This difference does not affect the main ruling when compensation is from an outside source.

He said: When the donee says to the donor: 'Take this as compensation for your gift' or 'as an exchange for it' or 'in return for it' and the donor takes possession, the right of revocation falls due to the achievement of the intended purpose. These expressions all convey the same meaning. Translation: When the donee said to the donor: 'Take this compensation for your gift' or 'its exchange' or 'in return for it' and the donor took possession of it, the right of revocation falls because the objective has been achieved. And all these expressions have the same meaning. Commentary on the saying 'and when the donee said...': The donee gave compensation to the donor for his gift using such a wording that the donor can understand it is compensation for his gifted item. For example, the donee said to him: 'Take this as compensation for your gift' or 'as a return for your gift' or 'as a reward for your gift' or 'as an exchange for your gift' or 'take this as compensation in return for your gift', and the donor took possession, then the right of revocation falls. Whether the compensation is little or much, from the same genus as the gift or different, because this is not a pure exchange, so increase or decrease does not constitute riba. However, the conditions of hibah like possession and segregation etc. must be observed. The reason for the fall of the right of revocation is that the donor's objective of obtaining compensation has been achieved. All the mentioned phrases indicate compensation. Therefore the right of revocation falls. Yes, if the donor does not know that it is compensation for his gift, then the donor has the right to revoke his gift and the donee has the right to revoke his compensation. Also, it is necessary that the compensation be from something other than the gifted object. If part of the gifted object itself is given as compensation, for example the gifted item was a thousand dirhams and some of those dirhams were given as compensation, or the gifted item was a house and one room of it was given as compensation, then this is not permissible. And according to Zufar, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Hidayah. The passage establishes that when a donee explicitly offers compensation to the donor using clear words indicating that it is in exchange for the gift, and the donor accepts and takes possession of that compensation, the donor's right to revoke the gift is extinguished. The reason is that the donor's objective—obtaining compensation—has been fulfilled. The Hanafi school stresses that the compensation must be from outside the gifted property itself; giving part of the gifted item back as compensation is invalid (except according to Imam Zufar). Additionally, the donor must be aware that the compensation is for the gift; if the donor does not realize this, the right to revoke remains. The compensation may be any amount, regardless of whether it equals the gift's value, since this is not a pure sale subject to riba rules.

Key Terms
الرجوع (al-ruju'): The donor's right to take back the gifted property after it has been given, before it is lost or transferred.
العوض (al-'iwad): Compensation given by the donee (or a third party) to the donor in return for the gift, which drops the donor's right to revoke.
هبة (hibah): The gift itself, which is the subject of the transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect when the donee says to the donor 'Take this as compensation for your gift' and the donor takes possession?
A) The donor's right to revoke the gift remains.
B) The donor's right to revoke the gift is dropped.
C) The gift becomes invalid.
D) The donee must give additional compensation.

Key Takeaway
Explicit compensation from the donee drops the donor's right to revoke, provided the compensation is from outside the gifted property and the donor is aware it is compensation.

Third Party Compensation in Gifts Drops Right of Revocation
Ruling on third party compensation in gifts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a third party's compensation on behalf of the donee nullifies the donor's right of revocation, and explain the qiyas analogy with khul' and sulh.

Core Idea
Compensation drops a right, not a tangible benefit, so a third party can validly provide it.

In the Hanafi school, a gift (hiba) can be revoked under certain conditions, but once the donor receives compensation (iwad) for the gift, the right of revocation is lost. This lesson examines a specific scenario: what if a third party (ajnabi), not the donee, voluntarily gives the compensation? The ruling is clear—it is valid and drops the revocation right. The reasoning relies on a qiyas (analogy) with established contracts like khul' (divorce by compensation) and sulh (compromise), where a third party's payment is also accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a third party (ajnabi) voluntarily giving compensation (iwad) to the donor on behalf of the donee (mawhub lahu). The ruling: the donor's right to revoke the gift is nullified upon taking possession of the compensation.
This is a specific application within hiba (gift) law.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The passage does not cite a direct nass (Qur'an or hadith); instead, it uses qiyas. The analogy is drawn with khul' and sulh, where a third party can validly pay compensation to drop a right.
The proof is reasoning-based (zanni al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (analogical link)
In both khul' and sulh, the payment functions to drop a right (the husband's right to marital bond, the guardian's right to qisas). In hiba, compensation similarly drops the donor's right to revoke. Since dropping a right is not a tangible thing, it does not require the right-holder (donee) to personally perform the payment.
The illah (effective cause) is the nature of compensation as a means to drop a right.
4
Note the scope and exceptions
This ruling is specific to hiba and analogous contracts. It is distinguished from sale (bai'), where a third party cannot be liable for the price because the benefit (ownership of the item) goes to the buyer, not a mere dropping of a right.
The passage highlights this distinction: in sale, ownership transfers, so the price must come from the buyer.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds this ruling as sahih (valid) and mufta bihi. There is no known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point, but other schools may differ.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

وَإِنْ عَوَّضَهُ أَجْنَبِيٌّ عَنِ الْمُؤْهُوبِ لَهُ مُتَبَرَّعًا فَقَبَضَ الْوَاهِبُ الْعِوَضَ بَطَلَ الرُّجُوعُ لِاَنَّ الْعِوَضَ لِإِسْقَاطِ الْحَقِ فَيَصِحُ مِنَ الْأَجْنَبِي كَبَدَلِ الْخُلْعِ والصلح

ترجمہ اور اگر اس کا عوض دیا کسی اجنبی نے موہوب لہ کی طرف سے سلوک کے طور پر اور واہب نے عوض لے لیا تو حق رجوع ساقط ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ عوض تو اسقاط حق کے لئے ہوتا ہے تو یہ اجنبی کی طرف سے بھی صحیح ہو سکتا ہے جیسے ضلع اور صلح کا عوض جب کوئی حق دار نکل آئے نصف ہبہ کا تو والیکی لے لے نصف عوض ۔ کیونکہ موہوب لہ کے لئے وہ سالم نہیں رہا جو نصف عوض کے مقابل ہو

تشریح قوله وان عوض .... عوض کے لئے یہ ضروری نہیں کہ موہوب لہ ہی دے بلکہ اگر اس کی طرف سے کسی اجنبی نے واہب کو اس سے عوض دے دیا تب بھی حق رجوع ساقط ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ عوض دینا تملیک مین کے لئے نہیں بلکہ حق رجوع ساقط کرنے کے لئے ہوتا ہے اور یہ اجنبی کی طرف سے بھی صحیح ہو گا جیسے ضلع اور صلح کے عوض اجنبی کی طرف سے صحیح ہوتا ہے۔ مثلا کسی اجنبی نے عورت کے شوہر سے کہا کہ تو اس کو اس شرط پر خلع دے دے کہ ہزار درہم عوض ضلع مجھ پر ہے تو یہ جائز ہے اسی طرح کسی اجنبی نے ولی مقتول سے کہا کہ تو قاتل کو قصاص معاف کر دے اس شرط پر کہ مال صلح یادیت مجھ پر ہے تو یہ بھی جائز ہے اس کی تحقیق یہ ہے کہ ہبہ کا عوض دینے میں موہوب لہ کا فائدہ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اس سے واہب کا حق رجوع ساقط ہو جاتا ہے اور یہ سقوط حق کوئی شئی نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اجنبی کی طرف سے عوض کی ادائیگی صحیح ہوگی ۔ جیسے عورت کو بدل ضلع کے ذریعہ سے سقوط ملک زوج کا فائدہ ہوتا ہے اور اجنبی کا بدل خلع جائز ہے۔ بخلاف باب بیچ میں شمن کے کیونکہ اس میں مشتری کے لئے بیح صحیح سالم رہتی ہے تو اجنبی پر یمن کا وجوب جائز نہ ہوگا۔
And if a third party compensates him on behalf of the donee voluntarily, and the donor takes possession of the compensation, the right of revocation is nullified because compensation is for dropping a right, so it is valid from a third party, like the substitute of khul' and sulh. Translation: And if a third party gave compensation on behalf of the donee voluntarily and the donor took the compensation, then the right of revocation is dropped. Because compensation is for dropping a right, so it is also valid from a third party, like the compensation of khul' and sulh. When a rightful claimant appears for half the gift, then the donor takes half the compensation... Commentary: It is not necessary that the donee himself give compensation; rather, if a third party gives compensation to the donor on his behalf, then also the right of revocation is dropped. Because giving compensation is not for ownership but for dropping the right of revocation, and this is also valid from a third party, just as the compensation of khul' and sulh is valid from a third party. For example, a third party says to the husband: 'Divorce her on the condition that a thousand dirhams as compensation for khul' is upon me'; this is valid. Similarly, a third party says to the guardian of the deceased: 'Forgive the qisas for the killer on the condition that the blood money is upon me'; this is also valid. The reasoning is that in giving compensation for a gift, the benefit to the donee is that the donor's right of revocation drops, and dropping a right is not a thing. Therefore payment of compensation by a third party is valid. Like the benefit to the wife through the substitute of khul' is the dropping of the husband's ownership, and a third party's substitute of khul' is valid. Unlike the case of price in sale, because there the sale remains valid for the buyer, so obligation of price on a third party is not valid.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (qiyas) from Al-Hidayah. The passage addresses the scenario where a third party, not the donee, voluntarily gives compensation to the donor on behalf of the donee. The ruling is that this also drops the donor's right to revoke the gift. The reason is that the function of compensation here is to drop the donor's right, not to give ownership to the donor. Since dropping a right is not a tangible thing, a third party can validly perform it. The text draws an analogy with khul' (divorce by compensation) and sulh (compromise) where a third party can offer compensation on behalf of the wife or the victim's family. This is distinguished from the case of sale, where a third party cannot be liable for the price because the benefit (ownership of the purchased item) goes to the buyer, not a mere dropping of a right.

Key Terms
أجنبي (ajnabi): A person who is neither the donor nor the donee, a third party.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife by paying compensation to the husband.
صلح (sulh): A compromise agreement, especially in blood money cases where the victim's family forgives qisas for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, why is a third party's compensation on behalf of the donee valid?
A) Because the third party becomes the owner of the gift.
B) Because compensation is for dropping a right, which is not a tangible thing.
C) Because the donee has authorized the third party in writing.
D) Because the donor has no right to revoke after taking any compensation.

Key Takeaway
A third party's voluntary compensation to the donor nullifies the right to revoke the gift because compensation functions to drop a right, not to confer a tangible benefit.

Partial Claim on Gift or Compensation: The Hanafi-Zufar Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partial claim and effect on revocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when half of the compensation is claimed in a hibah with 'iwad, explain the disagreement with Imam Zufar, and apply the correct rule to similar partial-claim scenarios.

Core Idea
The donor cannot reclaim half the gift when half the compensation is claimed; he must return the remainder or accept it.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding hibah with compensation. When a third party claims ownership of part of the compensation, the majority Hanafi position imposes a restriction: the donor cannot simply retract a proportional part of the gift. Instead, he must either accept the remaining compensation or return it and revoke the entire gift. Imam Zufar disagrees, analogizing to barter sales. Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation of how the nature of compensation (as dropping a right, not a price) shapes Hanafi contract law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage first deals with claiming half the gift (donee can retract half compensation) then half the compensation (donor's limitation). Note the asymmetry: in the first case the donee can reclaim proportionally; in the second, the donor cannot.
The key distinction: who is claiming what?
2
Trace Zufar's analogy
Imam Zufar likens hibah with compensation to barter (sale of commodity for commodity). In barter, if part of one commodity is claimed, the other party can reclaim a proportional part. Zufar extends this to the gift: if half the compensation is claimed, the donor can reclaim half the gift.
Zufar's argument is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) based on the apparent similarity.
3
Analyze the Hanafi counter-proof
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) argue that the remaining compensation could have been the whole compensation at inception; it remains valid for the whole gift. The donor's revocation right was dropped only for full compensation, so he has a choice to return the remainder and revoke entirely, or be content.
The key difference: in hibah, compensation is for dropping a right, not for ownership transfer like in sale.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Zufar: donor can reclaim half the gift without returning anything. Under majority: donor must either accept the remaining half or return it and revoke the whole gift.
Practical consequence: the donor cannot fragment the gift.
5
Note the textual correction
The commentary clarifies that Imam Zufar meant 'half the gift' not 'half the compensation' as some later commentators misunderstood. This is noted in Kafi, Kifayah, etc.
Prevents misinterpretation of Zufar's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اسْتَحقَ نِصْفُ الْهِبْةِ رَجَعَ بِنِصْفِ الْعِوَضِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُسَلَّمَ لَهُ مَا يُقَابِلُ نِصْفَهُ وَإِنِ اسْتُحِقَّ نِصْفَ الْعِرَضَ لَمْ يَرْجِعُ فِي الْهِبَةِ إِلَّا إِنْ يَرُدَّ مَا بَقِى ثُمَّ يَرْجِعُ وَقَالَ زُفَرُ يَرْجِعُ بِالنِّصْفِ اِعْتِبَارًا بِالْعِوَضِ الْآخَرِ وَلَنَا أنَّهُ يَصْلُحُ عِوَضًا لِلْكُلَّ فِي الْابْتِدَاءِ وَبِالْإِسْتِحْقَاقِ ظَهَرَ أَنَّهُ لَا عِوَضَ إِلَّا هُوَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يُتَخَيَّرُ لِأَنَّهُ مَا أَسْقَطَ حَقَّهُ في الرُّجُوعِ إِلَّا لِيُسَلَّمَ لَهُ كُلَّ الْعِوَضِ فَلَمْ يُسَلَّمَ لَهُ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَرُدَّهُ.

ترجمہ اور اگر حقدار نکل آئے نصف ہبہ کا تو وہ لے لے نصف عوض ۔ کیونکہ موہوب لہ کے لئے وہ سالم نہیں رہا جو نصف عوض کے مقابل ہو اور اگر حقدار نکل آئے نصف عوض کا تو نہ واپس لے سکتا ہے مگر یہ کہ لوٹا دے وہ باقی عوض پھر واپس لے اپنا ہبہ۔ امام زفر فرماتے ہیں کہ نصف مہر واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ دوسرے عوض پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے ، ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باقی ماندہ عوض ابتداء میں کل ہبہ کا عوض ہو سکتا ہے اور استحقاق سے یہ ظاہر ہو گیا کہ عوض نہیں مگر وہی باقی ماندہ لیکن واہب کو اختیار دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنا حق رجوع ساقط نہیں کیا مگر اس لئے تا کہ پورا عوض اس کے لئے سالم رہے۔ وہ سالم نہیں رہا تو وہ واپس کر سکتا ہے۔

تشریح قوله واذا استحق نصف الهبة ... اگرعوض دے دینے کے بعد نصف موہوب کسی اور کا نکلا تو موہوب لہ اپنا نصف عوض واہب سے واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ نصف عوض کے مقابلہ میں جو ہبہ تھا وہ موہوب لہ کے لئے سالم نہیں رہا۔ اور اگر نصف عوض کسی اور کا نکلا تو واہب یہ نہیں کر سکتا کہ نصف موہوب واپس لے لے بلکہ جو نصف عوض اس کے پاس باقی ہے وہ موہوب لہ کو واپس کر کے اپنا کل موہوب واپس لے گا یا اس نصف عوض پر قناعت کرے گا۔ امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ جیسے موہوب لہ اپنا نصف عوض واپس لیتا ہے اسی طرح واہب بھی اپنا نصف ہبہ واپس لے سکتا ہے جیسے بیع عرض بالعرض میں ہوتا ہے کہ اگر ان میں سے کسی ایک عوض کا کچھ حصہ مستحق نکل آئے تو مستحق علیہ کو اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ جو مستحق کے مقابلہ میں ہے وہ اپنے ساتھی سے واپس لے لے۔

تنبیہ صاحب ہدایہ کے قول و قَالَ زفر يرجع ب النصف “ میں نصف سے مراد نصف ہبہ ہے جیسا کہ کافی و کفایہ اور غایۃ البیان وغیرہ میں مصرح ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے جویر جع بنصف العوض کہا ہے۔ یہ موصوف کا سہو ہے۔ (نتائج)

قوله ولنا انه يصلح . ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس قدر عوض باقی رہا ہے وہ ابتداء میں کل مہبہ کا عوض ہوسکتا ہے اور جو ابتداء میں کال کا عوض ہو سکتا ہو وہ بقاء میں بھی کل کا عوض ہو سکتا ہے کیونکہ ابتداء کی نسبت بقاء اہل تر ہے اور نصف استحقاق میں لئے جانے کے بعد یہ ظاہر ہو گیا کہ جو کچھ باقی رہا ہے یہی عوض ہے۔ لیکن اتنی بات ہے کہ واہب کو اختیار حاصل ہو جائے گا کہ اگر چاہے تو باقی عوض پھیر دے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنا حق رجوع اسی امید پر ساقط کیا تھا کہ کل عوض اس کومل جائے اور جب وہ نہیں ملا تو اس کو اختیار ہوا کہ باقی ماندہ کو واپس کر دے جب وہ واپس کر دیا تو ہبہ بلاعوض رہ گیا۔ لہذا ہبہ واپس لے سکتا ہے۔
And when half of the gift is claimed [by a third party], he takes back half of the compensation because what corresponds to half is not delivered to him. And if half of the compensation is claimed, he does not take back from the gift except if he returns what remains then he takes back. And Zufar said: He takes back half by analogy with the other compensation. And our proof is that the remaining compensation can be compensation for the whole at the beginning, and by the claim it appears that there is no compensation except that, except that he has a choice because he dropped his right to revocation only so that the entire compensation would be delivered to him, and it was not delivered, so he may return it. Translation: And if a rightful claimant appears for half the gift, then the donor takes half the compensation. Because for the donee, that which corresponds to half the compensation did not remain safe. And if a rightful claimant appears for half the compensation, then the donor cannot take back [the gift] unless he returns what remains, then he takes back his gift. Imam Zufar says: He can take back half, by analogy with the other compensation. Our proof is that the remaining compensation could be compensation for the whole at the beginning, and by the claim it becomes clear that there is no compensation except the remaining part. However, the donor is given a choice because he dropped his right to revocation only so that the entire compensation would be safe for him. It did not remain safe, so he can return it. Commentary on the saying 'and when half of the gift is claimed...': If after giving compensation, half of the gifted property turns out to belong to someone else, then the donee can take back half of the compensation from the donor. Because the gift that corresponded to half the compensation did not remain safe for the donee. And if half of the compensation turns out to belong to someone else, then the donor cannot take back half of the gift; rather, he must either return the remaining half of the compensation to the donee and then take back his entire gift, or be content with that half compensation. Imam Zufar says: Just as the donee takes back his half compensation, similarly the donor can take back his half gift, as in the case of a sale of commodity for commodity where if part of one commodity is claimed, the party from whom it is claimed has the option to take back the corresponding part from his counterpart. Caution: In the author of Hidayah's statement 'and Zufar said: He takes back half' the half refers to half the gift, as clarified in Kafi, Kifayah, and Ghayat al-Bayan. The author of Inayah said it refers to half the compensation; that is an error. (Nata'ij) His statement 'and our proof is that it can be compensation'... Our proof is that the remaining compensation could be compensation for the whole at the beginning, and what can be compensation for the whole at the beginning can also be compensation for the whole in continuation, because continuation is more entitled than the beginning. And after half is taken due to claim, it becomes clear that what remains is the only compensation. But the donor is given a choice: if he wishes, he can return the remaining compensation. Because he dropped his right to revocation only in hope that he would get the entire compensation, and when he did not get it, he has the option to return the remainder. When he returns it, the gift becomes without compensation, so he can take back the gift.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute (the Hanafi school vs. Imam Zufar). The passage discusses two scenarios after compensation has been given and a third party claims ownership of part of the gifted property or part of the compensation. First, if half of the gifted property is claimed, the donee may take back half of the compensation because the delivery of the gifted property corresponding to that half failed. Second, if half of the compensation is claimed, the donor cannot automatically take back half of the gift. Instead, the donor must either return the remaining compensation to the donee and then revoke the entire gift, or accept the remaining compensation. Imam Zufar disagrees in the second scenario, analogizing it to a barter sale where each party can reclaim part for part. The Hanafi argument is that the remaining compensation could have served as compensation for the whole at inception, so after the claim it becomes the sole compensation; nevertheless, the donor has a choice to return it because he only dropped his right to revoke on the expectation of receiving full compensation.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istikhaq): A third party's claim of ownership over part of the gifted property or compensation, establishing that it was not owned by the giver.
عوض ('iwad): The compensation given to the donor for the gift.
رجوع (ruju'): The donor's right to revoke the gift and take it back, which is dropped by accepting the 'iwad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After compensation is given, half of the compensation is claimed by a third party. According to the majority Hanafi position, what can the donor do?
A) Take back half of the gift immediately.
B) Return the remaining compensation and then revoke the entire gift.
C) Keep the remaining compensation and still revoke the gift.
D) Automatically revoke the entire gift without returning anything.

Key Takeaway
In hibah with 'iwad, partial claim of the compensation does not allow proportional revocation; the donor must either accept the remainder or return it to fully revoke.

Gift of House with Compensation for Half
Ruling on partial compensation for a gifted house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a donee compensates only a portion of a gift, and explain why partial revocation is valid.

Core Idea
Compensation for part only blocks revocation for that part; the other half returns, creating permissible co-ownership.

What happens when a house is gifted but the donee pays compensation for only half? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling: the donor can take back the half for which no compensation was given. This results in joint ownership (shuyu'), which is acceptable because it arises after the contract. This lesson unpacks the rationale and contrasts it with the rule in divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key act
Recognize that the act is a gift (hibah) with partial compensation. The donee compensates exactly half the house.
The compensation is a payment in exchange for dropping the right to revoke.
2
Determine the ruling on revocation
The donor may revoke the half that was not compensated. The compensation only prevents revocation for the part it covers.
The preventing factor (the compensation) is specific to half, so it does not block revocation of the other half.
3
Analyze the consequence
The donor gets back half, so the donor and donee become co-owners (shuyu') of the house. This is valid because the joint ownership arises after the gift, not before.
Earlier joint ownership would have been problematic for a valid sale, but here it is permissible.
4
Address the objection
The text raises a question: if compensation drops the right to revoke, why doesn't it drop it entirely? The answer: compensation is not purely a drop; it also involves exchange, so partiality (tab'id) is allowed.
Contrast with divorce, where partial dropping (ta'b'id) is not permitted because divorce is a pure dropping of the marriage tie.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِنْ وَهَبَ دَارًا فَعَوَّضَهُ مِنْ نِصْفِهَا رَجَعَ الواهب فى النصف الذى لم يُعوّض لأنَّ الْمَانِعَ خَصَّ البَصْفَ.

ترجمہ اگر ایک گھر ہبہ کیا پس اس کے نصف کا عوض دے دیا تو واہب اس نصف کو واپس لے سکتا ہے جس کا عوض نہیں دیا۔ کیونکہ مانع صرف نصف کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔

تشریح قوله وان وهب دارا.... الخ اگر کسی نے ایک گھر دوسرے کو ہبہ کیا اور موہوب لہ نے اس کے نصف کا عوض دے دیا تو واہب اس نصف کو واپس لے سکتا ہے جس کا عوض نہیں دیا اس لئے کہ رجوع سے مانع امر خاص کر نصف کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ ہے کہ اس سے شیوع لازم آتا ہے۔ لیکن یہ شیوع چونکہ بعد کو طاری ہوا ہے اس لئے کچھ مضر نہ ہوگا۔

سوال یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی کہ عوض اسقاط حق کے لئے ہوتا ہے تو اس کا اثر کل میں ہونا ضروری ہے تا کہ تجری لازم نہ آئے جیسے طلاق میں ہوتا ہے۔ جواب عوض من كل وجہ اسقاط نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں مقابلہ کے معنی بھی ہیں اس اعتبار سے تجری جائز ہے، بخلاف طلاق کے۔
He said: And if he gifts a house and he gives him compensation for half of it, the donor takes back the half for which compensation was not given, because the preventing factor is specific to the half. Translation: If a house is gifted, and then compensation is given for half of it, the donor can take back the half for which compensation was not given, because the impediment is specific to the half. Commentary on the saying 'and if he gifts a house...': If someone gifts a house to another, and the donee gives compensation for half of it, then the donor can take back the half for which compensation was not given, because the impediment to revocation is specific to the half. At most, this entails joint ownership (shuyu'), but this joint ownership occurs later, so it is not harmful. Question: It has passed earlier that compensation is for dropping a right, so its effect must be in the whole to avoid the occurrence of tab'id (division), like in divorce. Answer: Compensation is not purely for dropping; it also contains the meaning of exchange. From this perspective, tab'id is permissible, contrary to divorce.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from Al-Hidayah. When a house is gifted and the donee gives compensation for only half of it, the donor may revoke the gift of the other half for which no compensation was received. The reason is that the compensation only prevents revocation for the half it covers. This results in the donor and donee becoming co-owners of the house, with the donor owning half (the uncompensated half) and the donee owning the other half. The commentary addresses a potential objection: compensation is meant to drop the right to revoke, so why does it not drop revocation for the whole gift? The answer is that compensation here also has aspects of exchange, so partial dropping is allowed, unlike in divorce where partiality (tab'id) is not permissible.

Key Terms
شيوع (shuyu'): Joint ownership that results when only part of the gifted property is returned to the donor.
تبعيض (tab'id): Dividing a single transaction into parts; here, partially dropping the right of revocation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man gifts a house to his friend. The friend gives compensation for half of the house. Which part can the donor revoke?
A) The entire house.
B) The half for which compensation was given.
C) The half for which compensation was not given.
D) He cannot revoke any part.

Key Takeaway
Compensation for only part of a gifted property prevents revocation only for that part; the donor may revoke the remainder, and the resulting co-ownership is valid.

Condition for Valid Revocation of a Gift
Condition for valid revocation of a gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid revocation of a gift in Hanafi fiqh and identify the required elements.

Core Idea
Revocation of a gift requires mutual consent or court order – unilateral revocation is invalid.

This lesson presents a foundational rule from Al-Hidayah regarding the revocation of a gift (hiba). The Hanafi school holds that a donor cannot unilaterally take back a gift; either both parties must agree, or a judge must order it. This safeguards the donee's ownership and prevents arbitrary revocation, especially since the permissibility of revocation itself is a disputed matter among scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
The act under discussion is 'revocation' (رجوع) of a gift (hiba). The text states it is not valid (لا يصح) under certain conditions.
This ruling applies after the gift has been fully executed and possession transferred.
2
State the Condition
Revocation is valid only in two scenarios: mutual consent (تراضيهما) between donor and donee, or a court order (حكم الحاكم) from a judge.
Mutual consent means both agree; court order resolves disputes.
3
Understand the Rationale
The reason given is that the permissibility of revocation is a matter of ikhtilaf among scholars and its basis is weak (وفي أصله وهاة). Thus, to avoid conflict, it is restricted to consensual or judicially decided cases.
This shows how ikhtilaf can affect the strictness of conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا يَصِحُ الرُّجُوعُ إِلَّا بِتَرَاضِيهِمَا أَوْ بِحُكْمِ الْحَاكِمِ لأَنَّهُ مُخْتَلَفْ بَيْنَ الْعُلَمَاءِ وَفِي أَصْلِهِ وِهَاءٌ وَفِي
He said: Revocation is not valid except with mutual consent of both or by the ruling of a judge, because it is disputed among scholars and in its origin there is weakness.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from Al-Hidayah. The passage states that the revocation of a gift is only valid if both parties agree (the donor and donee) or if a judge (hakim) issues a ruling. The reason given is that the permissibility of revocation is a matter of disagreement among scholars, and its basis is weak. Therefore, to avoid conflict, the intervention of a judge or mutual agreement is required. This ensures that revocation is not done unilaterally and arbitrarily.

Key Terms
تراض (taradi): Mutual consent between donor and donee for the revocation.
حكم الحاكم (hukm al-hakim): A court order from a judge deciding the revocation, especially when parties disagree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can a donor validly revoke a gift according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only with the court order of a judge.
B) Unilaterally if the gift is still in the donee's possession.
C) Either with mutual consent or by a judge's order.
D) Only if the donee agrees.

Key Takeaway
Revocation of a gift is only valid when both parties agree or a judge orders it.

Stranger's Compensation in Gift: Dropping the Right of Revocation
Ruling that stranger can give 'iwad, dropping right of revocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a stranger's compensation in a gift drops the donor's right of revocation, and explain the legal reasoning distinguishing it from sale.

Core Idea
A stranger's compensation drops the right of revocation because its purpose is isqat, not tamlik — a distinction from sale.

In the Hanafi school, a donor may normally revoke a gift unless an impediment exists. One such impediment is the giving of compensation ('iwad). But what if the compensation comes from a stranger rather than the donee? This lesson explains the ruling and the reasoning based on qiyas to khul' and sulh, and why it differs from sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that even if a stranger gives the compensation, the donor's right of revocation is dropped. The act is valid (sahih).
The compensation must be actually paid or promised? The text implies payment by stranger is valid.
2
Understand the rationale
The compensation is given not for ownership (tamlik) but to drop the right of revocation (isqat). Dropping a right is a non-entity, so it can be done by anyone.
Isqat is a negation, not a positive act.
3
Examine the analogy
The author analogizes to khul' (divorce by compensation) and sulh (compromise in qisas), where a stranger's compensation is also valid because it serves to drop rights.
In khul', the stranger's payment drops the husband's ownership; in sulh, it drops the heir's right to qisas.
4
Distinguish from sale
In sale, the price ('iwad) is for ownership transfer (tamlik), so a stranger cannot be obligated to pay it. In gift, the 'iwad is for isqat, so a stranger can give it.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the scope of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الهبة

عوض دے دیا تب بھی حق رجوع ساقط ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ عوض دینا تملیک مین کے لئے نہیں بلکہ حق رجوع ساقط کرنے کے لئے ہوتا ہے اور یہ اجنبی کی طرف سے بھی صحیح ہو گا جیسے ضلع اور صلح کے عوض اجنبی کی طرف سے صحیح ہوتا ہے۔ مثلا کسی اجنبی نے عورت کے شوہر سے کہا کہ تو اس کو اس شرط پر خلع دے دے کہ ہزار درہم عوض ضلع مجھ پر ہے تو یہ جائز ہے اسی طرح کسی اجنبی نے ولی مقتول سے کہا کہ تو قاتل کو قصاص معاف کر دے اس شرط پر کہ مال صلح یادیت مجھ پر ہے تو یہ بھی جائز ہے اس کی تحقیق یہ ہے کہ ہبہ کا عوض دینے میں موہوب لہ کا فائدہ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اس سے واہب کا حق رجوع ساقط ہو جاتا ہے اور یہ سقوط حق کوئی شئی نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اجنبی کی طرف سے عوض کی ادائیگی صحیح ہوگی ۔ جیسے عورت کو بدل ضلع کے ذریعہ سے سقوط ملک زوج کا فائدہ ہوتا ہے اور اجنبی کا بدل خلع جائز ہے۔ بخلاف باب بیچ میں شمن کے کیونکہ اس میں مشتری کے لئے بیح صحیح سالم رہتی ہے تو اجنبی پر یمن کا وجوب جائز نہ ہوگا۔
The gift. If compensation is given, the right of revocation is dropped, because giving compensation is not for ownership but to drop the right of revocation, and this is valid from a stranger, just as compensation in khul' and sulh is valid from a stranger. For example, a stranger said to a woman's husband: 'Give her khul' on condition that the compensation of one thousand dirhams is upon me' — this is permissible. Similarly, a stranger said to the guardian of the slain: 'Forgive the qisas on condition that the sulh money is upon me' — this is also permissible. The verification is that in giving compensation for a gift, the benefit for the donee is that the donor's right of revocation is dropped, and this dropping of a right is not a thing. Therefore, payment of compensation by a stranger is valid, just as a woman benefits from the dropping of the husband's ownership through khul' compensation, and the stranger's compensation in khul' is valid. Unlike the chapter of sale regarding price, because there the sale remains valid and sound for the buyer, so obligating the price upon a stranger is not permissible.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on gift (al-hibah) addresses the ruling when a stranger (ajnabi) gives the compensation ('iwad) instead of the donee. The author states that even in such a case, the donor's right of revocation is dropped. The reasoning is that the 'iwad in gift is not intended to transfer ownership (tamlik) but to drop the right of revocation (isqat al-haqq). Dropping a right is a non-entity, so it can be validly performed by anyone. The author provides analogies from khul' (divorce by compensation) and sulh (compromise in qisas), where a stranger's compensation is valid. He contrasts this with sale (bay'), where the price is for ownership transfer, so a stranger cannot be obligated to pay. The underlying principle is that 'iwad for isqat is valid from a stranger, while 'iwad for tamlik is not.

Key Terms
عوض ('iwad): Compensation given in exchange for a gift; here it serves to drop the donor's right of revocation.
رجوع (ruju'): The donor's right to take back a gift before delivery or in certain conditions after delivery.
سقوط حق (suqut al-haqq): The dropping or extinguishment of a right; here it is the donor's right of revocation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it valid for a stranger to give the compensation ('iwad) for a gift in Hanafi law?
A) Because the stranger becomes the owner of the gift
B) Because the compensation serves to drop the donor's right of revocation, which is a non-entity
C) Because gifts require three parties
D) Because the donor can demand compensation from anyone

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a stranger can validly give compensation for a gift, and it drops the donor's right of revocation because the compensation is for isqat (dropping a right), not for tamlik (ownership transfer).

Proof that Remaining Compensation Suffices for the Whole Gift
Hanafi proof for remaining 'iwad as full compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi proof that remaining 'iwad suffices for the whole gift and explain the donor's option to return it and revoke.

Core Idea
Remaining compensation can substitute for the whole gift because initial validity implies continued validity; but the donor may opt to return it.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi proof for a nuanced ruling in the law of gift (hiba) with compensation ('iwad). When part of the compensation is lost due to a third-party claim, the remaining portion can still serve as full 'iwad, relying on the maxim 'al-baqa' ahl min al-ibtida''. However, the donor is not forced to accept this; he may return the remainder and revoke the gift entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the remaining compensation after part is claimed. The ruling is that it suffices as full 'iwad for the gift, but the donor has an option.
The ruling balances the rights of donor and donee.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is a rational analogy based on the principle that what is valid initially is even more valid at continuation. The text explicitly cites: 'whatever could be compensation for the whole initially can also be compensation for the whole subsequently'.
This is a dalil 'aqli, not a textual proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The legal reasoning: The remaining 'iwad could have served as the full 'iwad at the start of the contract. Since the continuation is more deserving of validity than the beginning, it can serve as full 'iwad now. This is supported by the maxim 'al-baqa' ahl min al-ibtida''.
This is a form of qiyas or istihsan.
4
Note the donor's option
The donor originally gave up his right to revoke hoping to receive full compensation. Since he did not, he may return the remaining compensation and revoke the gift. This protects the donor from an unexpected loss.
This option prevents injustice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولنا انه يصلح . ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس قدر عوض باقی رہا ہے وہ ابتداء میں کل مہبہ کا عوض ہوسکتا ہے اور جو ابتداء میں کال کا عوض ہو سکتا ہو وہ بقاء میں بھی کل کا عوض ہو سکتا ہے کیونکہ ابتداء کی نسبت بقاء اہل تر ہے اور نصف استحقاق میں لئے جانے کے بعد یہ ظاہر ہو گیا کہ جو کچھ باقی رہا ہے یہی عوض ہے۔ لیکن اتنی بات ہے کہ واہب کو اختیار حاصل ہو جائے گا کہ اگر چاہے تو باقی عوض پھیر دے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنا حق رجوع اسی امید پر ساقط کیا تھا کہ کل عوض اس کومل جائے اور جب وہ نہیں ملا تو اس کو اختیار ہوا کہ باقی ماندہ کو واپس کر دے جب وہ واپس کر دیا تو ہبہ بلاعوض رہ گیا۔ لہذا ہبہ واپس لے سکتا ہے۔
His statement: 'And for us, it is suitable.' Our proof is that whatever amount of compensation remains could have been compensation for the entire gift initially, and whatever could be compensation for the whole initially can also be compensation for the whole subsequently, because the subsequent state is more deserving than the initial state. After half is taken due to claim, it becomes apparent that what remains is the compensation. However, the donor will have the option: if he wishes, he may return the remaining compensation. This is because he dropped his right of revocation with the hope that he would receive the entire compensation, and when he did not receive it, he has the option to return the remaining. When he returns it, the gift becomes without compensation, so he can take back the gift.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This short passage provides the Hanafi proof for the ruling that remaining compensation suffices for the entire gift. The reasoning is based on the principle that when part of the compensation is lost (due to istihqaq), the remaining part can still be valid as the whole 'iwad because initially it could have been the whole. The author uses the maxim 'al-baqa' ahl min al-ibtida' (the remaining state is more deserving than the initial state). However, the donor is given the option to return the remaining compensation because he revoked his right with the expectation of full compensation. If he returns it, the gift becomes without 'iwad, so he can revoke the gift. This balances the rights of both parties.

Key Terms
عوض ('iwad): Compensation or consideration given in exchange for a gift.
بقاء أهل من ابتداء (al-baqa' ahl min al-ibtida'): A legal maxim meaning that what is valid at the beginning is even more valid at the continuation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi proof in this passage, what happens to the remaining compensation when half of the 'iwad is legally claimed?
A) The remaining compensation becomes invalid and the gift is revoked.
B) The remaining compensation suffices as full 'iwad, but the donor may return it and revoke the gift.
C) The donee must pay the claimed amount to complete the 'iwad.
D) The donor must accept the remaining compensation and cannot revoke.

Key Takeaway
Remaining 'iwad suffices as full compensation via the maxim 'al-baqa' ahl min al-ibtida'', but the donor may return it and revoke the gift if full compensation was not received.

Partial Revocation of Gift After Compensation for Part
Ruling on partial revocation of gift with partial compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on revoking part of a gift when compensation is given for only half, and explain why tafriq is allowed.

Core Idea
Compensation only blocks revocation for the part it covers; partial revocation creating shuyu' is valid.

In gift (hiba), once a donee gives compensation ('iwad), the donor loses the right to revoke that part. But what if compensation is given for only half? This passage from Al-Hidayah tackles that exact scenario, ruling that the unpaid half may be taken back even if it creates joint ownership. It also addresses a subtle objection from the nature of 'iwad, distinguishing it from talaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the first part of the passage: the donor can revoke the half for which no compensation was given. Note the key consequence: it creates shuyu' (joint ownership), but that is acceptable.
Shuyu' that arises later is permissible here, unlike a gift that is initially undivided.
2
Locate the impediment and its scope
The passage says the impediment to revocation (the 'iwad) is specific to the half that was compensated. Find where it states that the impediment is 'makhsus' (specific) to that half.
This is the key legal reasoning: the effect of 'iwad is not general across the whole gift without evidence.
3
Follow the objection and response
A question is raised: if 'iwad functions as isqat (dropping a right), it should apply to the whole gift to avoid tafriq, just as in talaq. The answer distinguishes: 'iwad in gift also includes an exchange (muqabalah) element, so tafriq is allowed.
Compare with talaq where conditions cannot be split; the nature of 'iwad differs.
4
Confirm the ruling's applicability
The passage ends by reaffirming the ruling: partial revocation is valid. No other school disagreement is mentioned, so it is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
This is a clear ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وان وهب دارا.... الخ اگر کسی نے ایک گھر دوسرے کو ہبہ کیا اور موہوب لہ نے اس کے نصف کا عوض دے دیا تو واہب اس نصف کو واپس لے سکتا ہے جس کا عوض نہیں دیا اس لئے کہ رجوع سے مانع امر خاص کر نصف کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ ہے کہ اس سے شیوع لازم آتا ہے۔ لیکن یہ شیوع چونکہ بعد کو طاری ہوا ہے اس لئے کچھ مضر نہ ہوگا۔

سوال یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی کہ عوض اسقاط حق کے لئے ہوتا ہے تو اس کا اثر کل میں ہونا ضروری ہے تا کہ تجری لازم نہ آئے جیسے طلاق میں ہوتا ہے۔ جواب عوض من كل وجہ اسقاط نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں مقابلہ کے معنی بھی ہیں اس اعتبار سے تجری جائز ہے، بخلاف طلاق کے۔
His statement: 'And if he gifted a house...' If someone gifted a house to another and the donee gave compensation for half of it, the donor may take back the half for which no compensation was given, because the impediment to revocation is specific only to the half for which compensation was given. At most, this results in shuyu' (joint ownership), but since this shuyu' arises later, it is not harmful.

Question: It has passed before that 'iwad is for dropping a right, so its effect must encompass the whole to avoid tafriq (division), as in talaq. Answer: 'Iwad is not entirely for isqat; it also contains the meaning of muqabalah (exchange). In that respect, tafriq is permissible, unlike talaq.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a house is gifted and the donee gives compensation for only half. The ruling is that the donor may revoke the half for which no compensation was given, even though this creates joint ownership (shuyu') between the donor and donee. The impediment to revocation (the 'iwad) only applies to the half for which compensation was given. The text then answers a potential objection: if 'iwad is for isqat of the right of revocation as previously stated, it should encompass the whole gift to avoid tafriq (dividing the right), just as in talaq where a condition affecting the entire divorce is invalid if it leads to tafriq. The response is that 'iwad in gift is not purely isqat; it also has an element of exchange (muqabalah), so tafriq is permissible. Thus, revocation of only part of the gift is valid.

Key Terms
شیوع (shuyu'): Joint ownership or undivided share; here it arises because the donor takes back half of a house that was already gifted.
تجزی (tafriq/tajzi): Division or splitting of a legal effect; here it means the right of revocation can be split between parts of the gift.
عوض ('iwad): Compensation given by the donee to the donor in exchange for the gift, which blocks revocation of the compensated part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a donee gives compensation for half of a gifted house, what is the legal status of the other half?
A) The donor cannot revoke it because the gift is one unit.
B) The donor can revoke it even if it creates joint ownership.
C) The donor can only revoke it with the donee's consent.
D) The donor must return the compensation to revoke it.

Key Takeaway
Partial revocation of a gift is valid when compensation is given for only part, because the effect of 'iwad is limited to the part compensated, and shuyu' arising later is permissible.

6 min
Revocation Valid Only with Mutual Consent or Judge's Ruling
Condition for valid revocation in gift: mutual consent or judicial decree

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for valid revocation of a gift and explain the three reasons (ikhtilaf, weak proof, uncertainty) for requiring mutual consent or a judge's ruling.

Core Idea
Revocation of a gift requires mutual consent or a judge's ruling because the right to revoke is disputed and its proof is weak.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the author explains an important restriction on the donor's right to revoke a gift. While the Hanafi school permits revocation, it does not allow the donor to simply take back the gifted property unilaterally. Instead, valid revocation can only occur through mutual consent of both parties or by a judge's decree. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this condition and its legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is revocation (ruju') of a gift (hibah) after delivery. The ruling is that it is valid only with mutual consent of donor and donee or by a judge's ruling.
2
Understand the three reasons
The author gives three reasons: (1) it is a matter disputed among scholars (ikhtilaf), (2) the proof for revocation is weak (khilaf al-qiyas), (3) there is uncertainty about whether the gift's objective was achieved.
These reasons necessitate a definitive resolution via consent or judgment.
3
Trace the legal consequences
If the donee emancipates the gifted slave before judgment, it is valid. If the donee withholds and the property perishes, he is not liable. After judgment, similar rule applies unless he withholds after demand (then transgression).
This shows the donee's ownership is intact until valid revocation.
4
Distinguish revocation as faskh
Revocation is a rescission (faskh) from the beginning, so the donor does not need to take fresh possession. It is valid even in shared property (shai'). This differs from returning a defective item in sale, which is not a rescission but a claim for soundness.
The key difference: in sale, the right is in the quality; in gift, the right is to rescind.
5
Note the intra-madhhab dispute
The commentary discusses the nature of the ikhtilaf, whether it traces to Companions or Followers. The Hanafi position is that revocation is allowed, while Shafi'i generally does not allow it.
The condition of consent/judgment is a precaution due to the dispute.

ترجمہ اور صحیح نہیں ہے ہبہ سے رجوع کرنا مگر دونوں کی رضاء سے یا حاکم کے حکم کرنے سے کیونکہ رجوع کا جواز علماء کے درمیان مختلف فیہ ہے اور اس کی اصلیت کے ثبوت میں ضعف ہے۔ اور مقصود کے حاصل ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں خفاء ہے تو فیصلہ کے لئے قضاء یا رضاء کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر ہبہ کوئی غلام ہو اور موہوب لہ حکم قاضی سے پہلے اسے آزاد کرے تو آزاد کرنا نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر اس نے غلام کو روک لیا اور وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس میں موہوب لہ کی ملک قاہم ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر وہ چیز قضاء قاضی کے بعد اس کے پاس ہلاک ہو گئی۔ اس لئے کہ پہلا قبضہ مانتی نہیںتھا اور یہ قبض اس پر دائم ہے مگریہ کہ اب کی طلب کے بعد وہ اس کو روک لے ۔ کیونکہ یہ تعدی ہے اور جب وائب نے قضاء یا رضاء سے رجوع کیا تو یہ اصل ہی سے فتح ہوگا یہاں تک کہ واہب کا قبضہ کرنا شرط نہ ہوگا۔ اور یہ رجوع شائع ومشترک میں بھی صحیح ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ عقد جائز ہو کر اور اصل ہی سے حق فسخ کا موجب ہو کر واقع ہوا تھا۔ پس فسح کی وجہ سے اس نے اپنا ایسا حق بھر پور پالیا جو اس کے لئے ثابت تھا تو یہ نسل علی الاطلاق طاہر ہوگا۔ بخلاف بعد القبض بوجہ عیب واپس کرنے کے۔ کیونکہ یہاں مشتری کا حق سلامتی کے وصف میں ہے نہ کہ نسخ میں پس دونوں میں فرق ہو گیا۔

قوله و في اصله وهاء . دوسری علت یہ ہے کہ رجوع کی اصلیت ثابت ہونے میں ضعف ہے۔ بایں معنی کہ اس کا ثبوت خلاف قیاس
He said: 'And revocation is not valid except by mutual consent of both or by the ruling of a judge, because it is a matter disputed among scholars, and there is weakness in its origin, and there is obscurity in whether the objective is achieved or not, so a final decision is needed by consent or by judgment. Thus, if the gift was a slave and the donee emancipated it before the judgment, it is effective; and if he withheld it and it perished, he is not liable because his ownership remains; similarly if it perishes in his hand after judgment, because the initial possession was not guaranteed and this is a continuation thereof, unless he withholds it after demand, because that is transgression. When he revokes by judgment or mutual consent, it is a rescission from the beginning, so the donor's possession is not required, and it is valid in a shared property, because the contract occurred as a revocable contract giving the right of rescission from the beginning, so by rescission he fulfills a right established for him, and it becomes manifest absolutely, unlike return due to defect after possession, because there the right is in the quality of soundness, not in rescission, so they differ.'

Translation: Revocation of a gift is not valid except with the consent of both or by the order of a judge, because the permissibility of revocation is disputed among scholars, there is weakness in its proof, and there is uncertainty in the attainment of the objective, so a decision is necessary by qada' or rida'. Thus, if the gift was a slave and the donee freed it before the judge's ruling, the emancipation is effective. If he withheld it and it perished, he is not liable, because his ownership stands. Similarly, if it perishes in his hand after the judgment, because the first possession was not guaranteed and this is a continuation thereof, unless he withholds it after demand, because that is transgression. When the donor revokes by judgment or mutual consent, it is a rescission (faskh) from the beginning, so the donor's possession is not required, and it is valid in a shared property, because the contract was revocable, giving the right of rescission from the beginning, so by rescission he recovers his right fully, and it is effective absolutely, unlike return due to defect after possession, because there the buyer's right is in the quality of soundness, not in rescission, so they differ.

Commentary on 'He said: nor is revocation valid': It is already known that the donor may revoke his gift, but the validity of revocation is only when it is through a judge or by mutual consent. The meaning is that if the donor simply revokes without consent or judgment, it is of no effect; he becomes a usurper and is liable for the value if the property perishes. The author gives three reasons: (1) it is a disputed issue; (2) its origin is weak (khilaf al-qiyas); (3) uncertainty of objective. A discussion follows about the nature of the dispute: some attribute it to the Companions, but Ibn Hazm denies any Companion disagreed, so it is better to attribute it to the Followers.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This is a major ruling in the chapter on gift: revocation (ruju') after possession is valid only with the mutual consent of donor and donee or by a judge's ruling. The author provides three reasons: (1) the permissibility of revocation is disputed among scholars (Hanafi allows, Shafi'i generally does not); (2) the evidence for revocation is weak (it is khilaf al-qiyas, meaning contrary to analogy); (3) there is uncertainty whether the objective (the gift) has been achieved or not. Therefore, a definitive resolution is needed. The text then discusses consequences: if the donee emancipates the gifted slave before the judge's ruling, it is valid because his ownership is intact; if he withholds it and it perishes, he is not liable because the property is his. After judgment, if it perishes, he is also not liable unless he withheld it after demand. The revocation, when properly done, is a rescission (faskh) from the beginning, so the donor does not need to take fresh possession; it is valid even in a shared property. This differs from returning a defective item in a sale, which is not a rescission but a claim for soundness. The commentary further discusses the nature of the dispute, noting that the disagreement among later scholars does not weaken the Hanafi position; rather, it traces back to the Companions and Followers.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission (annulment) of a contract from its inception; revocation of gift is treated as faskh, not a new contract.
مختلف فيه (mukhtalaf fih): A matter on which there is scholarly disagreement; here, the permissibility of revocation.
خلاف قیاس (khilaf al-qiyas): A ruling that departs from standard analogy; the permissibility of revocation is considered khilaf al-qiyas because normally ownership transfer is final.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is revocation of a gift not valid by the donor's unilateral action according to Al-Hidayah?
A) Because gifts are irrevocable in all schools
B) Because it is a disputed issue and the evidence is weak, so a definitive resolution is needed
C) Because the donee's ownership cannot be overridden
D) Because the gift is considered a sale

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, revocation of a gift after delivery is valid only with mutual consent or a judge's ruling, because the right to revoke is disputed and its proof is weak; otherwise, the donor becomes a usurper.

Conditions for Valid Revocation of a Gift
Ruling statement on revocation conditions and branch cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a donor may validly revoke a gift and apply the ruling to scenarios involving donee's actions.

Core Idea
Revocation after the donor's purpose is achieved requires mutual consent or a judge's order.

The Hanafi school generally permits a donor to revoke a gift after delivery, but this right is restricted once the donor's purpose in giving is fulfilled. Since the purpose is subjective, the law requires a clear procedural safeguard: either both parties agree to the revocation, or a judge orders it. This lesson unpacks the third 'illa (cause) and its practical branch rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third 'illa
The third cause that restricts revocation is the attainment of the donor's purpose (ḥuṣūl al-maqṣūd). Understand that the purpose may be reward, generosity, or compensation.
Purpose is hidden so needs objective determination.
2
Apply the procedural condition
When the purpose is achieved, revocation is invalid unless there is mutual consent of donor and donee or a judge's decree. Without either, revocation is void.
This is the core rule.
3
Analyze branch rulings
Work through the examples: if the donee frees a gifted slave before court order, it is valid; if he refuses to return after revocation, he becomes liable; if the item perishes after court order but before delivery, no liability unless he withheld.
These illustrate how the procedural condition and ownership affect liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و في حصول المقصود تیسری علت یہ ہے ہمارے نزدیک رجوع کرنا گو جائز ہے۔ لیکن حصول مقصود کے بعد جائز نہیں ہے ہو تا اور واہب کا مقصد حل ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں خفاء ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اگر ہبہ سے اس کا مقصد ثواب یا اظہار سماحت تھا تو وہ حاصل ہو چکا اس لحاظ سے رجوع نہیں کر سکتا اور اس کا مقصد عوض پانا تھا تو یہ حاصل نہیں ہوا لہذار جوع کرنے کا حق رہا۔ پس ان وجوہ ثالثہ مذکورہ کے پیش نظر ضروری ہے کہ دو باتوں میں سے کسی ایک بات پر فیصلہ ہو یعنی یا تو واہب و موہوب لہ دونوں باہم راضی ہوں یا قاضی واپسی کا حکم کرے اس کے بغیر رجوع کرنا صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر ہبہ کوئی غلام ہو جس سے واہب نے رجوع کیا اور موہوب لہ نے حکم قاضی سے پیشتر اسے آزاد کر دیا تو اس کا آزاد کرنا نافذ کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر موہوب لہ نے واہب کے رجوع کرنے اور ہبہ طلب کرنے کے بعد اس کو دینے سے انکار کیا تو وہ ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس میں موہوب لہ کی ملکیت قائم ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر حکم قاضی ہو جانے کے بعد واہب کے دینے سے پہلے مئی موہوب تلف ہو گئی تب بھی موہوب لہ ضائن نہ ہو گا۔ جب کہ اس کے دینے سے انکار نہ کیا ہو اس لئے کہ پہلا قبضہ اس کے ضمانتی نہیں تھا تو بدل کر ضمانتی نہیں ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ موجودہ قبضہ تو وہی پہلا قبضہ چلا آرہا ہے۔ ہاں اگر حکیم قاضی کے بعد واہب اس کو طلب کرے اور موہوب لہ روک لے تو البتہ ضامن ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اب اس کی طرف سے تعدی پائی گئی۔
His statement: 'and in the attainment of the purpose' – this is the third cause. According to us, revocation is permissible, but after the attainment of the purpose it is not permissible. And the donor's purpose is hidden in whether it has been achieved or not. Because if his purpose from the gift was reward or showing generosity, then it has been achieved; in that respect he cannot revoke. And if his purpose was to receive compensation, then it has not been achieved, so he retains the right to revoke. Therefore, in view of these three mentioned causes, it is necessary that a decision be made on one of two things: either both the donor and donee mutually agree, or the judge orders the return. Without this, revocation will not be valid. Even if the gifted item was a slave and the donor revoked and the donee freed him before the judge's order, his freeing is enforceable. And if the donee refuses to give after the donor's revocation and demand, then he is liable because the donee's ownership remains. Similarly, if after the judge's order but before the donor's taking, the gifted item is destroyed, the donee is not liable as long as he did not refuse to give, because the first possession was not a guarantee for him, so it does not become a guarantee by exchange, as the current possession is the same first possession. Yes, if after the judge's order the donor demands and the donee withholds, then he is liable because there is transgression from him.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Al-Hidayah, explaining the third reason ('illa) that restricts the donor's right to revoke a gift. The Hanafi position is that revocation is generally permissible, but not after the donor's purpose in giving the gift has been fulfilled. Since the purpose is subjective, the ruling requires either mutual consent of both parties or a judge's decree to effect revocation. Without either, revocation is invalid. Several branch rulings illustrate: if the donee frees a gifted slave before a judge's order, it is valid because ownership remains with him. If he refuses to return after revocation, he becomes liable. If the item perishes after the judge's order but before delivery, the donee is not liable if he did not refuse, as his possession is the same original one. Only if he withholds after the judge's order does he become a guarantor due to transgression (ta'addi).

Key Terms
رجوع (rujū'): Donor's revocation of a gift after delivery.
مقصود (maqṣūd): The donor's purpose in giving the gift (thawab, generosity, or compensation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is required for a valid revocation of a gift after the donor's purpose has been achieved?
A) Only the donor's will
B) Mutual consent of donor and donee OR a judge's order
C) Return of the gift to the donor's possession
D) A written contract

Key Takeaway
Revocation of a gift after the donor's purpose is achieved requires either mutual consent of both parties or a judge's order; otherwise it is invalid.

Donee’s Liability: No Recourse against Donor in Gift
Ruling that donee cannot recover from donor in gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a donee cannot recover from a donor when a third party takes compensation, and distinguish between gratuitous and commutative contracts regarding liability for deception.

Core Idea
In a gift, the donee bears the risk of third-party claims because he is not an agent—only deception within a sale gives recourse.

This passage establishes a key liability rule in Hanafi fiqh: when a gifted item is destroyed and a third party proves ownership, the donee has no claim against the donor. The reasoning hinges on the nature of a gratuitous contract (tabarru') and the absence of agency. The commentary expands by contrasting with wadi'ah and mudarabah, and clarifies the scope of deception (ghurur) as a basis for recourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The gifted item is destroyed (or claimed) after delivery. A third party proves ownership and takes compensation from the donee. The ruling: the donee cannot recover anything from the donor.
This is the core legal outcome.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is by analogy (qiyas) and reasoning (ta'lil): the donee is not an agent for the donor, and the contract is gratuitous, so no expectation of safety. Contrast with deposit (wadi'ah) and mudarabah where the holder acts as an agent.
The proof is derived from the nature of tabarru' contracts.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In a gift, the donee acts for himself; the donor does not guarantee freedom from defects or claims. In a commutative contract (sale), the seller guarantees clear title, and deception within that contract creates liability. In a gratuitous contract, deception does not create liability unless it occurs within the context of a commutative contract.
The commentary illustrates with the walad maghrur case.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school. Some other schools allow the donee recourse if the donor knowingly gave away another's property (i.e., active deception). The Hanafi position limits recourse to commutative contracts.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Apply the distinction
Test the distinction: if a depositary pays compensation for deposited goods, he recovers from the depositor. If an agent (mudarib) pays for a claim on mudarabah assets, he recovers from the capital owner. In both, the holder is an agent acting for the owner.
Agency (niyaba) is the key factor.
