⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا تَلَفَتِ الْعَيْنُ الْمَوْهُوْبَةُ فَاسْتَحَقَّهَا مُسْتَحِقٌ وَضَمَّنَ الْمَوْهُوبَ لَهُ لَمْ يَرْجِعُ عَلَى الْوَاهِبِ بِشَيْءٍ لِأَنَّهُ عَقْدُ تَبَرُّعٍ فَلَا يُسْتَحَقُّ فِيهِ السَّلَامَةُ وَهُوَ غَيْرُ عَامِلٍ لَهُ وَالْغُرُورُ فِي ضِمْنَ عَقْدِ الْمُعَاوَضَةِ سَبَتْ لِلرُّجُوعِ لَا فِي ضِمْنِ غَيْرِهِ. ترجمہ جب تلف ہو جائے مبہ کی ہوئی چیز پھر اس کا کوئی حقدار نکل آئے اور وہ موہوب لہ سے ضمان لے لے تو موہوب لہ واہب سے کچھ نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ یہ عقد تبرع ہے تو اس میں سلامتی کا مستحق نہ ہو گا اور وہ واہب کے لئے کام کرنے والا بھی نہیں ہے اور جو دھوکا عقد معاوضہ کے ضمن میں ہو و و رجوع کا سبب ہوتا ہے نہ کہ وہ جو غیر عقد کے ضمن میں ہو۔ تشریح قوله و اذا تلف اگر مال موہوبہ تلف ہو جائے اور کوئی شخص اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر کے موہوب لہ سے تاوان لے لے تو موہوب لہ اپنے واہب سے کچھ واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ ہبہ ایک احسان کا معاملہ ہے تو اس میں یہ استحقاق نہیں ہوسکتا کہ جو چیز دی گئی ہے۔ وہ موہوب لہ کو مسلم رہے۔ پھر وہ بیبہ قبول کرنے میں واہب کے لئے عامل بھی نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ واہب اس کا ضامن رہے بلکہ وہ خود اپنے لئے عامل ہے۔ قوله وهو غير عامل .... اس کے ذریعہ موقع سے احتراز کیا ہے اگر وہ کچھ تاوان دے۔ تو مودع پر رجوع کا حقدار ہے کیونکہ وہ ودیعت پر قبضہ کر کے اس کی حفاظت میں مودع کے لئے عامل ہوتا ہے لانه يحفظه لاجلہ ۔ اسی طرح مضارب سے بھی اعتراض ہے کہ وہ اگر مال مضاربت سے کچھ خرید لے پھر مال مضاربت میں کسی کا استحقاق نکل آئے اور مستحق اس سے تاوان لے لے تو وہ رب المال پر رجوع کا حقدار ہے۔ لأنه عامل له . قوله و الغرور .. سوال مقدر کا جواب یہ ہے کہ واہب نے محل مستحق میں موہوب لہ کے لئے ملک ثابت کر کے اس کو دھوکا دیا ہے اور فریب دینا موجب ضمان ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے بائع اگر مشتری کو دھوکا دے تو وہ ضامن ہوتا ہے جواب یہ ہے کہ موجب ضمان دھوکا وہ ہوتا ہے جو عقد معاوضہ کے ضمن میں ہو جیسے بیع وغیرہ اور جو غیر معاوضہ کے ضمن میں ہو وہ موجب ضمان نہیں ہوتا۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی نے دوسرے کا راستہ کے پر امن ہونے کی خبر دی اور وہ اس پر چل پڑا اور اس کو چوروں نے لوٹ لیا تو مخبر سے کچھ نہیں لے سکتا۔ سوال اتنی بات تو فی عقد المعاوضہ کہنے سے بھی معلوم ہو جاتی ہے۔ پھر لفظ ضمن بڑھانے سے کیا فائدہ؟ جواب ... اس کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ ولد مغرور کے مسئلہ میں مشتری بائع پر قیمت لینے میں رجوع کرتا ہے۔ حالانکہ ولد میں معاوضہ نہین ہے۔ البتہ عقد معاوضہ کے ضمن میں غرور موجود ہے۔
He said: When the gifted item is destroyed and a claimant proves entitlement and exacts compensation from the donee, the donee has no recourse against the donor for anything because it is a gratuitous contract, so it does not entitle one to safety, and he is not an agent for him. And deception in the context of a commutative contract is a cause for recourse, not in the context of a non-commutative one. Translation: When the gifted item is destroyed, then a claimant appears and takes compensation from the donee, the donee cannot take anything from the donor. Because this is a gratuitous contract, so he does not deserve safety, and he is not acting for the donor. And deception in a commutative contract is a cause for recourse, not that which is within a non-commutative one. Elaboration: His statement 'and if it is lost': If the gifted property is lost and someone proves his entitlement and takes compensation from the donee, then the donee cannot recover from the donor. Because hibah is a favor transaction; it does not entitle that the given item remain safe for the donee. Moreover, the donee is not an agent for the donor in accepting the gift, such that the donor would be liable; rather, he acts for himself. As for the deposit (wadi'ah), if the depositary pays compensation to a claimant, he can recover from the depositor because he holds the deposit as an agent for the depositor (he preserves it for his sake). Similarly, in mudarabah, if the agent buys with the mudarabah capital and a third party claims ownership and takes compensation, the agent can recover from the rabb al-mal (capital owner) because he is his agent. As for deception: An implied question: the donor deceived the donee by establishing ownership over the property that was actually owned by another; deception necessitates liability, like a seller who deceives a buyer. The answer: Deception that necessitates liability is that which occurs within a commutative contract, like sale; deception in a non-commutative contract does not. For example, if someone informs another that a road is safe and he walks and is robbed, he cannot claim from the informant. Objection: That could be known from the phrase 'in a commutative contract'; what benefit is there in adding the word 'context' (dhimn)? Answer: Its benefit is seen in the case of the deceived offspring (walad maghrur): the buyer recovers the price from the seller, even though the offspring is not a commutative contract, but deception occurs in the context of a commutative contract.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the matn, addressing the liability of the donee when a gifted item is destroyed and a third party appears. The Hanafi position is that the donee cannot sue the donor for compensation, because hibah is a gratuitous contract (tabarru') and does not imply a guarantee that the item is free of third-party claims. The donee acts for himself, not for the donor. This is contrasted with contracts of deposit (wadi'ah) and mudarabah where the holder acts as an agent for the owner and can recover. The passage also addresses the issue of deception (ghurur): only deception within a commutative contract (like sale) gives rise to liability, not in non-commutative ones. The commentator raises an objection about the word 'dhimn' (context) and answers that it covers cases like the 'walad maghrur' where a buyer of a slave recovers the price for a child born to the slave, even though the child was not part of the sale contract, but the deception occurred in the context of the sale.

Key Terms
عقد تبرع (aqd tabarru'): Gratuitous contract like gift, where no compensation is given.
غرور (ghurur): Deception by the donor leading to loss for donee.
ضمان (daman): Liability or compensation for loss.
عامل (‘āmil): Agent; one who acts on behalf of another.
ولدمغرور (walad maghrur): Child born to a slave woman purchased by a deceived buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can't the donee recover from the donor when a third party takes compensation for the gifted item?
A) Because the donee was negligent
B) Because hibah is a gratuitous contract and the donee is not acting as an agent
C) Because the donor is not responsible for defects
D) Because the donee should have checked the title

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a donee cannot recover from a donor for a gift claimed by a third party because the gift is a gratuitous contract and the donee acts independently, not as an agent.

Hibah bi Shart al-Iwad: Hybrid Nature and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on gift with condition of compensation with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the nature of hibah bi shart al-iwad and evaluate the counter-argument of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Hibah bi shart al-iwad is initially a gift and ultimately a sale—a unique Hanafi hybrid.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi view on a gift made with a condition of compensation. The classical schools disagree: Hanafis see it as a dual-nature contract, while Zufar and al-Shafi'i treat it as a pure sale. Understanding this dispute is key to grasping how Hanafi usul accommodates mixed contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its initial requirements
Read the first part of the passage to identify the conditions: possession in the session and no co-ownership (shuyu'). Understand why possession is required: because it starts as a gift.
The text says 'because it is a gift initially'.
2
Identify the opposing position (Zufar and al-Shafi'i)
Locate where the text says 'Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: It is a sale initially and ultimately'. Note their proof: the meaning of sale is exchange for compensation, and contracts are judged by meanings.
They analogize to selling a slave to himself being manumission.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof (honey and vinegar analogy)
The Hanafi argument is that the contract has two aspects (gift and sale), so we combine them where possible. The text gives the example of honey and vinegar mixed together—both retain their properties.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the possibility of combining.
4
Evaluate the counter-proof (sale of slave to himself)
The Hanafis distinguish: in that case, it is impossible to consider it a sale because the slave cannot own himself, so only manumission remains. But here, both aspects can be given effect: deferred ownership from hibah and bindingness from sale.
This shows why the analogy fails.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Hanafi: possession in the session is required; shuyu' invalidates. Under Zufar/Shafi'i: it is a pure sale from the start, so possession is not a condition for validity.
This affects how the contract is executed.

قَالَ وَإِذَا وَهَبَ بِشَرْطِ الْعِوَضِ اُعْتُبِرَ التَّقَابُضُ فِى الْمَجْلِسِ فِي الْعِوَضَيْنِ وَيَبْطُلُ بِالشُّيُوعِ لِأَنَّهُ هِبَةٌ ابْتِدَاءً فَإِنْ تَقَابَضَا صَحَ الْعَقْدُ وَصَارَ فِي حُكْمِ الْبَيْعِ يُرَدُّ بِالْغَيْبِ وَخَيَارِ الْرُّؤْيَةِ وَيُسْتَحَقُّ فِيْهِ الشُّفْعَةُ لِأَنَّهُ بَيْعٌ إِنْتِهَاءً وَقَالَ زُفَرُ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ هُوَ بَيْعَ ابْتِدَاءً وَاِنْتِهَاءً لِاَنَّ الله مَعنَى الْبَيْعِ وَهُوَ التَّمْلِيكُ بِعِوَضِ وَالْعِبْرَةُ فِي الْعُقُودِ لِلْمَعَانِى وَلِهَذَا كَانَ بَيْعُ الْعَبْدِ مِنْ نَفْسِهِ اِعْتَاقًا وَلَنَا إِنَّهُ اشْتَمَلَ عَلَى جِهَتَيْنِ فَيُجْمَعُ بَيْنَهُمَا مَا أَمْكَنَ عَسَلًا بِالشَّهِينِ وَقَدْ أَمْكَنَ لِاَنَّ الْهِبَةَ مِنْ حُكْمِهَا تَأَخَّرُ الْمِلْكِ إِلَى الْقَبْضِ وَقَدْ يَتَرَاحْى عَنِ الْبَيْعِ الْفَاسِدِ وَالْبَيْعَ مِنْ حُكْمِهِ اللُّزُومُ وَقَدْ تَنْقَلِبُ الْهِبَةُ لَازِمَةً بِالتَّعْوِيْضِ فَجَمَعْنَا بَيْنَهُمَا بِخِلَافِ بَيْعِ نَفْسِ الْعَبْدِ مِنْهُ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُمْكِنُ اعْتِبَارُ الْبَيْعِ فِيهِ إِذْ هُوَ لَا يَصْلُحُ مَالِكاً لِنَفْسِهِ

ہوئے ابتداء میں بہیہ کا حکم رکھا اور اس مجلس میں باہمی قبضہ ہونے کے بعد انتہاء میں اس کو بیچ ٹھرایا۔ بخلاف غلام کو خود اسی کے ہاتھ فروکت کرنے کے جس پر امام زفر اور امام شافعی نے قیاس کیا ہے کہ اس میں بیع کا اعتبار کرنا ناممکن ہے ورنہ لازم آئے گا کہ مولی نے عوض لے لیا اور غلام کو غلام کی ملک میں دے دیا۔ حالانکہ یہ باطل ہے۔ پس یہی کہا جائے گا کہ مولیٰ نے مال لے کر آزاد کیا ہے۔
باندی ہند کی مگر اس کا حمل مستفی کیا تو استثناء باطل ہے اور ہبہ صحیح ہے
فَضْلٌ قَالَ وَمَنْ وَهَبَ جَارِيَةً إِلَّا حَمْلَهَا صَحْتِ الْهَبَةُ وَبَطَلَ الإِستثناء لان الْإِسْتِثْنَاءَ لَا يَعْمَلُ إِلَّا فِي مَحَلَّ يَعْمَلُ فِيهِ الْعَقْدُ وَالْهِبَةُ لَا تَعْمَلُ فِي الْحَمْلِ لِكَوْنِهِ وَصْفًا عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ فِي الْبُيُوعِ فَانْقَلَبَ شَرَطًا فَاسِدَا وَالْهِبَةُ لَا تَبْطُلُ بِالشَّرُوطِ الْفَاسِدَةِ وَهذَا هُوَ الْحُكم فى النكاح والخلع والصلح عَنْ دَمِ الْعَمَدِ لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَبْطُلُ بِالشُّرُوطِ الْفَاسِدَةِ بِخِلَافِ الْبَيْعِ وَالْاجَارَةِ وَالرَّهْنِ لِأَنَّهَا تَنْظُلُ بِهَا
ترجمہ جس نے ہبہ کی باندی سوائے اس کے حمل کے تو صحیح ہوگا ہیں اور باطل ہوگا استثناء کیونکہ استثناء عمل اسی محل میں کرتا ہے جس میں عقد عمل کرتا ہے اور ہبہ حمل میں کوئی عمل نہیں کرا۔ اس کے وصف ہونے کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ ہم نے بیوع میں بیان کیا ہے ۔ بیس بیا استثناء بدل کر شرط فاسد ہو گیا اور ہبہ شروط فاسدہ سے باطل نہیں ہوتا۔ اور یہی حکم ہے نکاح و ضلع میں اور خون عمد سے صلح میں کیونکہ یہ بھی شروط فاسدہ سے باطل نہیں ہوتے۔
He said: When a gift is made with a condition of compensation, mutual possession in the session is required for both compensations, and it becomes void due to shuyu' because it is a hibah initially. Then if they take possession from each other, the contract becomes valid and falls under the ruling of sale; it is returned for defect and option of sight, and pre-emption is established in it, because it is a sale ultimately. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: It is a sale initially and ultimately, because the meaning of sale is present, which is transfer of ownership for compensation, and consideration is given to meanings in contracts. For this reason, the sale of a slave to himself is manumission. Our proof is that it comprises two aspects, so we combine them as much as possible, like honey and vinegar. And it is possible because: from the rulings of hibah is that ownership is deferred until possession, and this also occurs in a defective sale; and from the rulings of sale is that it is binding, and hibah becomes binding with compensation. So we combine both. Unlike the sale of a slave to himself, because considering it a sale is impossible since he cannot be owner of himself. 
[Translation of Urdu commentary on page 271] 
A separate section: He said: Whoever gifts a slave-girl except her pregnancy, the gift is valid and the exception is void, because the exception only operates in a place where the contract operates, and hibah does not operate in the pregnancy since it is a description, as we explained in sales. So it becomes an invalid condition, and hibah is not invalidated by invalid conditions. And this is the ruling in marriage, khul', and sulh for intentional homicide, because they are not invalidated by invalid conditions, unlike sale, lease, and pledge, because they are invalidated by them.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct rulings: first, the nature of a gift made with a condition of compensation (hibah bi shart al-iwad), and second, the effect of excluding an unborn child when gifting a slave-girl. The main text begins with the ruling of the Hanafi school: when a gift is made with a condition that the donee must give something in return, it is considered a gift at the inception, so both parties must take possession of their respective items in the same session; if the property is co-owned (musha'), the contract becomes void. However, if they take possession, the contract becomes valid as a form of sale, meaning it becomes binding, subject to options of defect and sight, and the right of pre-emption applies. This reflects the Hanafi compromise: initially it's a gift (so possession is required), but ultimately it's a sale (so it becomes binding). Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue that it is a sale from the start because the essence is exchange of property for compensation; they point to cases like selling a slave to himself being considered manumission, showing that meanings prevail over words. The Hanafis respond that the contract combines both aspects, and where possible, both should be given effect. Since hibah can have deferred ownership and can become binding with compensation, and sale is inherently binding, they combine: at the outset, it's a gift (ownership after possession), after possession, it's a sale (binding). This is unlike selling a slave to himself, which cannot be a genuine sale. The second ruling concerns a gift of a slave-girl with an exception of her pregnancy. Since the pregnancy is a description, not an independent subject of the contract, the exception is invalid and becomes a void condition. However, because hibah is a gratuitous contract, it is not invalidated by a void condition; the gift of the slave-girl itself is valid, and the condition is ignored. This ruling also applies to marriage, khul', and settlement for intentional homicide, as these contracts are also not invalidated by void conditions, unlike sale, lease, and pledge.

Key Terms
ہبہ بشرط العوض (hibah bi shart al-iwad): A gift made on condition that the donee provides compensation to the donor.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): An invalid or void condition in a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what condition is required at the time of contract for a gift with a condition of compensation (hibah bi shart al-iwad) to be initially valid?
A) The gift must be registered with witnesses.
B) Possession of both items must occur in the same session.
C) The donee must be a relative.
D) The compensation must be exactly half the value.

Key Takeaway
Hibah bi shart al-iwad is a hybrid contract: initially hibah (possession required), ultimately sale (binding, options, pre-emption).
